INTRODUCTION

介绍

H ere’s the big idea in 81 words:

用81个字概括一下核心思想：

I don’t like being pressured into making a purchase. And I’m not alone. Over decades of being marketed, pitched, sold, and lied to, we’ve all grown resistant to sales persuasion. The moment we feel pressured to buy, we pull away. And if we’re told what to do or what to think, our defenses go up. In other words, buyers don’t put much trust in you and your ideas. However, everyone trusts their own ideas.

我不喜欢被强迫购买。而且我并非孤例。几十年来，我们不断被各种营销手段、推销和谎言蒙蔽，早已对销售说服习以为常。一旦感到购买压力，我们就会立刻退缩。如果有人告诉我们该做什么或该怎么想，我们就会竖起防备。换句话说，买家并不信任你和你的想法。然而，每个人都相信自己的想法。

Accordingly, today, products are bought, not sold.

因此，如今产品是被购买的，而不是被出售的。

If you’re trying to make a deal in this environment, it’s never been harder. Buyers in your industry are skeptical of new products and services, and if you’re the person who has to sell to them, they’ll be skeptical of you as well. They fact-check everything you say, sometimes while you’re saying it. And buyers are always looking for a better deal, thinking they can somehow improve on your offer, no matter how good it is.

在这种环境下达成交易，难度前所未有。你所在行业的买家对新产品和服务都持怀疑态度，如果你是负责向他们推销的人，他们也会对你抱有怀疑。他们会核实你说的每一句话，有时甚至在你说话的时候就开始核实。而且，买家总是想方设法寻找更优惠的价格，无论你的报价有多好，他们总觉得还能找到更划算的办法。

Instead of pushing your idea on the buyer, it’s a better move to guide them to discover it on their own, so they believe it, trust it, and get excited about it. Then they’ll want to buy it and will feel good about the chance to work with you.

与其强迫买家接受你的想法，不如引导他们自己去发现，这样他们才会相信、信任并对此感到兴奋。如此一来，他们不仅会想要购买，还会乐于与你合作。

This book is dedicated to showing you how to plant your idea in the mind of another so they will discover it, appreciate it, and fall in love with it on their own. But you cannot accomplish this with standard sales methods. Instead, you need to flip the script.

本书旨在教你如何将你的想法植入他人脑海，让他们自行发现、欣赏并爱上它。但传统的销售方法无法做到这一点。你需要彻底颠覆常规。

—

I’M OREN KLAFF. Several years ago, I wrote a book called Pitch Anything , in which I taught readers a unique method to prepare and deliver a pitch that would wow buyers and investors every time. It was a method I’d developed for myself in the world of tech, but it proved to be incredibly useful for others as well. As word spread about the effectiveness of Pitch Anything , soon over a million people were using it in their everyday business, and before I knew it, I was getting calls from people at companies like Google, Amazon, and Bank of America telling me how useful they’d found my method.

我是奥伦·克拉夫。几年前，我写了一本书，名为《推销任何事物》（Pitch Anything），书中我教读者一种独特的方法，教他们如何准备和进行每次都能打动买家和投资者的精彩推介。这套方法最初是我在科技领域为自己开发的，但事实证明它对其他人也同样非常有效。随着《推销任何事物》的有效性广为人知，很快就有超过一百万人将其运用到日常业务中。不知不觉中，我接到了来自谷歌、亚马逊和美国银行等公司的电话，他们都告诉我我的方法非常实用。

Next, companies from Germany, Italy, and Russia were calling. The result: I was being invited to help pitch large deals in far-flung parts of the world. I’d never imagined my ideas would travel so far from Silicon Valley.

接下来，来自德国、意大利和俄罗斯的公司也纷纷打来电话。结果是：我受邀前往世界各地，协助洽谈大型项目。我从未想过我的想法会从硅谷传播到如此遥远的地方。

In the years since I wrote Pitch Anything , the marketplace has changed. Buyers have become more cold and digital, and so I have changed with them, creating new methods for closing deals. These new methods are what I’ve put in this book.

自从我写了《推销任何产品》之后，市场发生了变化。买家变得更加冷漠和数字化，我也随之改变，创造了新的成交方法。这些新方法就是我在这本书里分享的内容。

Bluntly, here’s the problem: Enthusiastic sellers make an impressive pitch but then quickly switch over to “closing mode,” applying just the kind of unwanted pressure that blows up deals these days faster than you can say “Sign here.” Or aspiring sellers will make the world’s greatest pitch and then stop, unsure of what to do next, hoping the deal will come through all on its own.

坦白地说，问题就在这里：热情洋溢的销售人员会做出令人印象深刻的推销，但随后却迅速切换到“成交模式”，施加不必要的压力，而这种压力正是如今导致交易失败的罪魁祸首，速度之快，简直让人来不及说“签字”。或者，一些雄心勃勃的销售人员会做出世界上最精彩的推销，然后却突然停了下来，不知所措，希望交易能够自行达成。

Both these approaches are the norm, and painful to watch. For that reason, I developed a revolutionary approach, a way to win every deal without spending a single moment selling or trying to close—a way to sell without selling at all. In other words, the buyer feels it’s his or her idea to work with you and makes the deal happen. You don’t apply pressure, try to overcome objections, or give chase.

这两种方法都很常见，但看着却让人很痛苦。因此，我开发了一种革命性的方法，一种无需花费任何时间推销或试图促成交易就能拿下每一笔生意的方法——一种“不推销也能成交”的方法。换句话说，买家会觉得是他们自己主动选择与你合作，并最终促成交易。你无需施加压力，无需试图克服异议，也无需苦苦追问。

So here’s what I want you to understand right from the beginning of this book. Closing a deal without sales pressure is not a mystery. It’s not some superpower that certain people have and others don’t. Getting a deal done is a step-by-step process and it’s available to anybody who knows how to follow a few basic rules. Because once you know the rules, you never have to push someone to close; instead, you can make them feel like they came up with your idea themselves, which leads a deal to close naturally, as if it were always meant to happen. This ability to flip the script will help you in any situation and close any deal.

所以，我希望你在本书一开始就明白一点：无需销售压力就能达成交易并非什么神秘的秘密，也不是某些人拥有而其他人没有的超能力。完成交易是一个循序渐进的过程，只要掌握一些基本规则，任何人都能做到。因为一旦你了解了这些规则，你就无需强迫客户成交；相反，你可以让他们感觉你的想法是他们自己想出来的，这样交易就会自然而然地达成，仿佛命中注定一般。这种扭转乾坤的能力将帮助你应对任何情况，促成任何交易。

In this book, I’m going to teach you those rules and show you the steps to persuade your prospects without pressuring them. First, I’ll introduce the idea of Inception—planting an idea in someone else’s brain. From there, I’ll show you how to use the Dominance Hierarchy and the rules of Certainty to turn the tables and put yourself in a position of strength, instead of the buyer holding all the cards. Next, I’ll demonstrate the power of a Pre-Wired Idea and how to make your deal feel Plain Vanilla, like it’s the most normal and obvious thing in the world—in other words, something your prospect’s mind can easily grasp. Then you’ll discover how to use the buyer’s natural Pessimism as a force in your favor, and how to be Compelling when it matters most. Finally, you’ll get to see how all these ideas work together as I describe in detail what can only be called “the deal of a lifetime.”

在这本书中，我将教你这些规则，并向你展示如何在不施加压力的情况下说服潜在客户。首先，我会介绍“植入式营销”的概念——在别人的脑海中植入一个想法。接下来，我会教你如何运用支配层级和确定性法则来扭转局面，让你掌握主动权，而不是让买家完全掌控局面。然后，我会演示预先设定的想法的力量，以及如何让你的交易显得平淡无奇，就像世界上最正常、最显而易见的事情一样——换句话说，让你的潜在客户能够轻松理解。之后，你将发现如何利用买家天生的悲观情绪为你所用，以及如何在关键时刻展现你的说服力。最后，我会详细描述一个堪称“千载难逢的交易”，让你看到所有这些理念是如何协同运作的。

To protect the confidentiality of my clients and more effectively illustrate how you can apply these ideas, I’ve changed many identifying details of people and companies involved and fictionalized some aspects of the stories. Nonetheless, every one of these examples is based on a real-life business deal in which I used these techniques effectively.

为了保护客户的隐私，并更有效地展示如何应用这些理念，我更改了许多涉及人员和公司的身份信息，并对故事的部分内容进行了虚构。尽管如此，每个案例都基于我实际运用这些技巧完成的商业交易。

For example, let me tell you about the time I tried to sell a $10 million software deal to one of the most powerful men in Russia.

例如，让我来告诉你我曾经试图向俄罗斯最有权势的人之一推销一份价值 1000 万美元的软件合同的经历。

#↩

CHAPTER 1

第一章

Why You Need Inception

为什么你需要《盗梦空间》

T he truly rich in Russia are called oligarchs, a term that has come to mean control, power, and ruthlessness. And Viktor [last name redacted] definitely deserves the title. His luxurious office sits atop a high rise overlooking the Moscow River. Viktor sits behind a presidential desk, wearing a tourbillion watch that I recognize from a popular gear and gadgets website, list price $1 million. Every wall in this office is decorated with photos of oil rigs, factories, container ships, and cargo planes he presumably owns; over his desk is a massive and oddly beautiful painting of an oil refinery with a caption engraved in brass, NOVOGROD #12 . Viktor is heavyset, tall, and burly—in another life he might have been a rugby player. His smile isn’t a smile at all. The executives of all his companies fear him, and I fear him too.

在俄罗斯，真正的富豪被称为寡头，这个词如今已成为掌控、权力和冷酷无情的代名词。而维克托（姓氏已隐去）绝对配得上这个称号。他那间豪华的办公室坐落在莫斯科河畔一座高楼的顶层。维克托坐在总统级办公桌后，戴着一块我曾在某知名电子产品网站上见过的陀飞轮腕表，标价100万美元。办公室的每一面墙上都挂满了石油钻井平台、工厂、集装箱船和货机的照片，想必这些都是他名下的产业；办公桌上方悬挂着一幅巨大而又奇特的油画，描绘的是一座炼油厂，旁边用黄铜镌刻着“诺沃格罗德12号”。维克托身材魁梧，高大魁梧——如果换一种人生，他或许会是一名橄榄球运动员。他的笑容并非真正的笑容。他旗下所有公司的管理人员都畏惧他，我也同样畏惧他。

There are three things you need to know about doing deals with Russian oligarchs. Number one, they aren’t interested in losing money—ever, under any circumstances. Second, they don’t make emotional decisions; Russians are raised on a steady diet of math, physics, engineering, and electronics, and they analyze every decision ten different ways, then have a shot of vodka and analyze it one more time. Third, you simply cannot lose an oligarch’s money and say, “Yikes, sorry it didn’t work, but I tried really hard,” like you can in Silicon Valley. Instead, you need to do whatever it takes to get their money back.

与俄罗斯寡头做生意，你需要了解三件事。第一，他们绝不想赔钱——无论在任何情况下。第二，他们不会凭感情用事做决定；俄罗斯人从小就接受数学、物理、工程和电子学的熏陶，他们会从十个不同的角度分析每一个决定，然后喝上一杯伏特加，再仔细分析一遍。第三，你不能像在硅谷那样，赔了寡头的钱之后说：“哎呀，抱歉，没成功，但我真的尽力了。”相反，你必须竭尽全力把钱追回来。

So, if there’s a World Championship of Dealmaking, this is it.

所以，如果真有世界交易锦标赛，那就是这场了。

Why would I ever leave my comfortable Los Angeles office to travel across the world to participate in this kind of stress-inducing meeting?

我为什么要离开舒适的洛杉矶办公室，飞越半个地球去参加这种令人压力巨大的会议呢？

MicroGenetics, the company I represented, needed to hire a dozen or more PhD mathematicians, but in the United States, these are a very rare and expensive commodity. Competent mathematicians easily command a million dollars per contract on the global exchange, and that was way over the company’s budget. In Russia, however, you can still find skilled but affordable mathematicians, but not without a powerful local sponsor. Viktor was a man who could wave his finger and get us whatever we wanted. Bottom line, my client needed both his money and his approval in order to navigate the layers of bureaucracy that come with any deal in Russia.

我所代表的MicroGenetics公司需要聘请十几位数学博士，但在美国，数学博士非常稀缺且价格昂贵。在国际人才交易平台上，优秀的数学家每份合同的薪酬轻松就能达到一百万美元，这远远超出了公司的预算。然而，在俄罗斯，你仍然可以找到技术精湛且价格合理的数学家，但前提是必须有当地有影响力的赞助人。维克托就是这样一位能言善辩、举手之劳的人。总之，我的客户需要他的资金和认可，才能在俄罗斯的任何交易中顺利通过层层官僚程序。

This is how I found myself standing on the fifty-ninth floor of a tower in downtown Moscow, in an office that felt more like an exhibit at the Getty museum than a place of business. I was flanked on each side by translators and analysts, eager to get rid of me and keep Viktor on his precise daily schedule.

就这样，我发现自己站在莫斯科市中心一座摩天大楼的五十九层，身处一间与其说是办公场所，不如说是盖蒂博物馆展厅的办公室里。我的两侧站着翻译和分析师，他们都急于打发我走，好让维克托继续按部就班地完成每日工作。

My presentation was just getting underway, but I was already in serious trouble. At first, Viktor was listening to me with great interest, nodding his head in comprehension as I explained our genetic sequencing technology that we believed would save millions of lives and revolutionize health care. When I paused to take a quick breath, he jumped in to criticize my deal in perfect English: “Your software code has many syntax and computational errors.” But when I countered that point, describing a rock-solid contract we had with a major US tech firm, proving the technology worked, Viktor stared at me blankly, needing his translator to explain each word, even then looking distant and lost.

我的演讲才刚刚开始，就已经陷入了困境。起初，维克托听得津津有味，我解释我们引以为豪的基因测序技术时，他频频点头表示理解。这项技术我们相信能够拯救数百万人的生命，并彻底改变医疗保健行业。当我停下来喘口气时，他立刻用一口流利的英语插话批评我的方案：“你们的软件代码语法和计算错误很多。” 但当我反驳他的观点，并列举了我们与一家美国大型科技公司签订的一份稳固的合同，证明这项技术行之有效时，维克托却茫然地看着我，需要翻译逐字逐句地解释，即便如此，他看起来仍然心不在焉，不知所措。

Back and forth we went like this. Every question he shot at me was forceful and articulate and from the mind of a brilliant investor. Every answer I gave was met with a blank stare. Then Viktor would say, “Please you explain this more better,” and translators would step in for a long, drawn-out exchange that went nowhere.

我们就这样来回争论。他抛给我的每一个问题都掷地有声、条理清晰，一看就是一位杰出投资者的思维。而我给出的每一个回答，都换来他茫然的眼神。然后维克托会说：“请你解释得更清楚些。”接着翻译就会介入，展开一场冗长乏味、毫无进展的对话。

I had to explain our technology to him in the same way I might show my elderly neighbor how to send a text message. “Human genetic data is like millions of grains of sand,” I said, using a weird analogy I had just made up. Next I was using gestures that looked like hand puppets to help make this point.

我不得不向他解释我们的技术，就像教我年迈的邻居如何发短信一样。“人类基因数据就像数百万粒沙子，”我用一个刚编的奇怪比喻说道。接下来，我用一些像手偶一样的手势来辅助说明。

Viktor cut me off: “That makes no sense.”

维克托打断我的话：“这根本说不通。”

Oh god. He was right. It didn’t. Now my mouth was saying things my brain hadn’t approved of yet.

天哪。他说得对。确实没成功。现在我的嘴里说出了一些我大脑还没认可的话。

I was losing control of this deal. But I had to keep moving forward. So I launched into the most exciting part of my pitch, explaining the revolutionary new features that set us apart in the world of genetic data.

我感觉自己快要失去对这笔交易的控制了。但我必须继续推进。于是，我开始阐述推介中最激动人心的部分，解释那些让我们在基因数据领域脱颖而出的革命性新功能。

Just before I finished, Viktor turned away from me, ignoring what I was saying. With his back to me, he spoke in Russian to his team of advisers for a few minutes. I didn’t know if I was supposed to leave, wait quietly, or perform a magic trick.

就在我即将说完的时候，维克托转过身去，完全无视我的话。他背对着我，用俄语和他的顾问团队交谈了几分钟。我不知道自己该离开，还是该安静地等着，或者该表演个魔术。

Finally, he turned back to me, a little surprised I was still there. His eyes narrowed in an unfriendly way; then, when I opened my mouth to say something, he smiled broadly, waving his hand to cut me off. “Yes, yes, we know all this,” he said, and looked at me as if I were a boring commercial you have to watch before the real show begins.

最后，他转过身来看着我，似乎有些惊讶我还站在那里。他眼神变得不友好，眯了起来；然后，当我刚要开口说话时，他咧嘴一笑，挥手打断了我。“是是是，我们都知道这些，”他说着，看着我，仿佛我是正片开始前必须看完的无聊广告。

Viktor had taken away all my usual control points. He was using his power and a supposed language barrier to put me into a low-status position. I was acting needy and anxious, and negotiating against myself. This was a dealmaker’s nightmare. I knew he was going to make an offer, because I was still in the room, but I also knew the terms of the deal would be horrendous.

维克托剥夺了我所有惯常的掌控权。他利用自己的权力，以及所谓的语言障碍，把我置于低人一等的地位。我表现得既需要帮助又焦虑不安，实际上是在和自己谈判。这简直是谈判者的噩梦。我知道他肯定会提出条件，因为我还待在房间里，但我同时也知道，交易的条款肯定会非常苛刻。

As this unfolded, I was watching myself fall back onto the classic sales approach, with its tired old script: First become likable and build rapport, then explain “features and benefits,” next do a trial close, and then fight like an alley cat to overcome all the objections the buyer has come up with.

随着事情的发展，我发现自己又回到了经典的销售方法，带着老套的剧本：首先要讨人喜欢，建立融洽的关系，然后解释“产品特性和优势”，接下来进行试探性成交，然后像野猫一样拼命克服买家提出的所有异议。

Russian oligarchs do not like being sold this way or argued with, especially by Americans. And Viktor is definitely no exception to this rule. He has a big mustache, which the President of Russia once suggested he shave off because it looked too “Soviet.” He said nyet to that request, and nyet to virtually every other demand put in front of him before and since. If I tried to overcome his objections and push a deal, he would never go along with it. I knew it. So if I wanted to walk out of that room with a check—on fair terms—it was going to have to be his idea to work with me.

俄罗斯寡头不喜欢被这样推销，也不喜欢被人争论，尤其是不喜欢被美国人推销。维克托当然也不例外。他留着浓密的胡子，俄罗斯总统曾建议他刮掉，因为这胡子看起来太“苏联范儿”了。他拒绝了这个建议，而且几乎拒绝了之前和之后提出的所有其他要求。我知道，如果我试图克服他的反对意见，促成交易，他绝不会同意。所以，如果我想带着支票——而且是公平的条件——走出那个房间，那最终还是得由他主动提出与我合作。

I took a deep breath. It was time to flip the script.

我深吸了一口气。是时候扭转局面了。

I had been working on a completely novel way of telling other people about an idea or product so that they would come up with the idea to buy without my even having to ask. It’s called Inception, and it’s based on the latest research in neuroscience and behavioral economics. I’ve uncovered a way to plant an idea deep in another person’s subconscious so that they take ownership of it and propose it to me as if it were theirs.

我一直在研究一种全新的方法，可以向他人介绍某个想法或产品，让他们在未经我开口的情况下就产生购买的念头。这种方法叫做“植入式营销”，它基于神经科学和行为经济学的最新研究成果。我发现了一种方法，可以将一个想法深深植入他人的潜意识中，让他们认同这个想法，并像对待自己的创意一样主动向我提出。

This approach is needed because traditional sales methods get you stuck in arguments and logical stand-offs—which is where I was headed with Viktor. Inception relies on a completely new set of tools: the Status Tip-Off, the Flash Roll, Pre-Wired Ideas, Plain Vanilla, being Compelling, and the Buyer’s Formula. I’ll show you all of these later.

之所以需要这种方法，是因为传统的销售方式容易陷入争论和逻辑僵局——我之前和维克托的谈判就差点陷入这种境地。Inception 依赖于一套全新的工具：地位提示、快速反应、预设想法、平易近人、引人入胜以及买家公式。稍后我会一一介绍这些工具。

Back in Moscow, Viktor was moving fast and he wasn’t giving me a chance to use any of these advanced principles. I knew what I needed to say, but he would switch the conversation to Russian at the worst possible time, and I couldn’t get him to listen or understand me—he was just too good at the game. My time was about done and I’d gotten absolutely nowhere.

回到莫斯科后，维克托的节奏很快，根本不给我机会运用这些高阶技巧。我知道自己该说什么，但他总会在最不合时宜的时候把话题切换到俄语，我根本无法让他听懂我的话——他棋艺太精湛了。我的时间快到了，却一无所获。

Try to imagine this for a second. You’ve spent twenty-five minutes talking to your only prospect, and in that time you’ve been ignored, interrupted, misinterpreted, and told your state-of-the-art technology seems old and outdated. None of your persuasive points have found a home, and all the material you have left to deliver is no better than the stuff that’s already been rejected.

试想一下：你花了二十五分钟和唯一的潜在客户交谈，结果却被无视、打断、误解，甚至被告知你最先进的技术看起来老旧过时。你所有的说服论点都无人理睬，剩下的材料也和之前被拒绝的那些一样糟糕。

The problem I was facing in that room is the same problem salespeople face in any industry: You know what decision you want the buyer to make, but the more you push in that direction, the more they dig in, slow down, and change the agenda. They want to make their own decision on their own timeline. Buyers buy how they want to buy, not how you want to sell.

我在那个房间里遇到的问题，其实是所有行业销售人员都会遇到的问题：你知道你想让买家做出什么决定，但你越是强迫他们，他们就越是固执己见，放慢脚步，改变主意。他们想按照自己的节奏做决定。买家会按照自己的意愿购买，而不是按照你想卖的方式。

This is why today most things are bought; they aren’t sold.

这就是为什么如今大多数东西都是被买的，而不是被卖的。

I realized that Viktor had pushed me to act like an amateur salesman and I was trying too hard to pitch him on the merits of the deal. I reminded myself to stop selling and instead establish myself as an expert, because a smart buyer like Viktor would never do a fair deal with an amateur.

我意识到维克托让我表现得像个业余推销员，我太想向他推销这笔交易了。我提醒自己停止推销，转而展现自己的专业性，因为像维克托这样精明的买家绝不会和一个业余人士做公平的交易。

I was ready to create Inception but I was also nervous to try this new approach on such a powerful dealmaker. Hopefully Viktor couldn’t tell how anxious I was feeling, but then I realized it didn’t matter. Inception doesn’t involve feelings. I steadied myself and went back to work, focusing on elevating my status and proving my expertise.

我准备好实施“盗梦空间”计划，但同时也忐忑不安，毕竟要对付维克托这样一位实力雄厚的交易撮合者，这种新方法实在难以奏效。我希望维克托察觉不到我的焦虑，但后来我意识到这并不重要。“盗梦空间”计划不涉及情感。我调整好情绪，重新投入工作，专注于提升自身地位，证明我的专业能力。

I delivered a Flash Roll—a sixty-second display of pure technical mastery designed to alleviate any doubts about your authority on a subject. When Viktor turned to his translators for help, I was ready.

我做了个“闪电演示”——短短六十秒，就展现了纯粹的技术造诣，旨在消除任何人对我某个领域权威性的疑虑。当维克多向他的翻译寻求帮助时，我已经做好了准备。

“Viktor, I do not allow you to be confused about this,” I said. “You’re one of the best investors in the world. And I am offering a Plain Vanilla deal, nothin’ fancy at all. This is easy stuff. And we are almost out of time, so for the moment, you have to accept what I’m telling you at face value.”

“维克托，我不允许你在这件事上产生任何误解，”我说。“你是世界上最优秀的投资者之一。我提供的只是一份最普通的交易，没有任何花哨的东西。这很简单。而且我们时间不多了，所以现在，你只能相信我说的。”

He nodded in acceptance, and I could tell I had impressed him. By flipping the script on him, I’d taken him by surprise. “Continue, please,” he said imperiously, as oligarchs generally do.

他点头表示接受，我看得出来我给他留下了深刻的印象。我出其不意地扭转了局面，让他措手不及。“请继续，”他居高临下地说，就像寡头们通常那样。

Finally, I had the chance to reveal something called a Pre-Wired Idea that I knew would act like a back door to his mind. The moment you deliver a Pre-Wired Idea, buyers suddenly understand everything they need to know about what they should do next, without you having to explain it or sell it or even say anything at all.

最后，我终于有机会向他展示一种叫做“预设理念”的东西，我知道它就像一扇通往他内心的后门。一旦你提出这个预设理念，买家就会立刻明白接下来该怎么做，而你甚至无需解释、推销，或者开口说话。

My time was nearly up. “Viktor, this deal is a great fit for your company,” I said. “But you already know that. So let’s figure out what we’re going to do together. Just tell me one of these two things. First, if you don’t want to work with me, just say, ‘Oren, I don’t want to do the deal.’ It’s OK—I allow you to say that to me, and we can easily part ways. Otherwise, the second option is for you to say, ‘Oren, I like you and I like the deal—let’s move ahead.’ Those are the choices; I just need to hear one. Either one is fine with me. Just tell me which it is.”

我的时间快到了。“维克托，这笔交易非常适合你们公司，”我说，“不过你肯定也知道。所以我们来商量一下接下来该怎么做。你只需要告诉我以下两种情况中的一种。第一，如果你不想和我合作，就直接说：‘奥伦，我不想做这笔交易。’没关系——我允许你这么说，我们可以很轻松地分道扬镳。否则，第二种选择是，你可以说：‘奥伦，我很欣赏你，也很欣赏这笔交易——我们继续推进吧。’就这两种选择；我只需要听到其中一种。两种我都接受。告诉我你的选择就好。”

Then I waited.

然后我就开始等待。

It felt like a huge risk to say this, but it was no risk at all—because the alternative would be to ask for the sale, to which he would instantly reply, “Send us the information and we’ll think about it.” Translation: “Nyet.”

说出这句话感觉风险很大，但其实一点风险都没有——因为另一种选择是直接提出出售，而他会立刻回答：“把资料发给我们，我们考虑一下。”翻译过来就是：“不。”

The next three minutes were silent and stressful, and I finally drank the warm vodka that had been poured for me an hour earlier. The silence grew uncomfortable for Viktor, and I let him be uncomfortable. He scratched some numbers on a notepad only because he wanted to end our staring contest. No matter the pressure and risk, I was not going to chase him. He had to chase me, if only a little bit. And then, at last, the ice broke. “Can we see the data again, please?” he said politely. My method had worked. He was chasing me, ever so slightly. Did I jump with excitement at this moment, or pull out a bunch of charts and graphs and race to a close? No I did not. Instead, I pulled out my phone and began looking for an Uber. And while I did, I casually explained my Buyer’s Formula to him, just to be helpful.

接下来的三分钟沉默而令人窒息，我终于喝下了那杯一个小时前就倒好的温热伏特加。维克托感到沉默难耐，我任由他感到不自在。他只是在记事本上潦草地划了几笔数字，想结束我们之间的对视。无论压力和风险有多大，我都不会追着他跑。他得追着我跑，哪怕只是一点点。然后，终于打破了僵局。“我们能再看看数据吗？”他礼貌地问道。我的方法奏效了。他开始追着我跑了，虽然只是略微而已。我当时应该兴奋得跳起来，还是拿出一堆图表，急忙结束谈话？不，我没有。相反，我拿出手机开始叫优步。与此同时，我漫不经心地向他解释了我的“买家公式”，只是为了帮他一把。

“I do these kinds of medical software deals all the time,” I said nonchalantly, like I’m in an oligarch’s office every day. “The tricky part is handling patient data.” And then I explained how I would choose to invest or not invest in the deal I was offering him. “Anyway, from doing this so many times, that’s just how I would look at it.”

“我经常做这种医疗软件交易，”我漫不经心地说，仿佛每天都在寡头办公室里似的。“棘手的部分是处理病人数据。”然后我解释了我会如何选择是否投资我向他提出的这笔交易。“总之，我做过这么多次，这就是我的看法。”

This was it—the moment it all comes down to. It was time to ask Viktor if he was “in.” It was time to push him for a yes.

就是现在——一切尘埃落定的时刻到了。是时候问问维克托是否“愿意”了。是时候逼他答应了。

Except it wasn’t.

但事实并非如此。

With the Inception scripts, you never tell the buyer what you want them to do—you never pressure them for a yes. You let them tell you they want to buy. I looked Viktor in the eye and said, “I need to head out for another meeting across town.”

按照《盗梦空间》的剧本，你永远不会告诉买家你想让他们做什么——你永远不会强迫他们答应。你要让他们自己告诉你他们想买。我看着维克多的眼睛说：“我得去城里另一个地方开会了。”

And then I heard the magic words that come when you successfully take a buyer through the six steps of Inception. “I like this deal. We can work together, so thank you please, now stay,” he said thoughtfully, this time in very good English.

然后，我听到了成功引导买家完成“启动”六步流程后才会出现的神奇话语。“我喜欢这笔交易。我们可以合作，所以谢谢您，请留下来吧。”他若有所思地说，这次他的英语非常好。

An hour later I had a $10 million deal on fair terms, a plan to hire the needed mathematicians, and the endorsement of a Russian oligarch.

一小时后，我达成了一项价值 1000 万美元、条款公平的交易，制定了招聘所需数学家的计划，并得到了俄罗斯寡头的支持。

WHERE THE “OLD SCRIPT” CAME FROM

“旧剧本”的由来

In ancient times, life was short and dangerous; survival from sunrise to sunset was not a sure thing. For much of early civilization, at least a quarter of all human males on the planet were killed every year by war, famine, tribal infighting, and things that bite, sting, inject poison, or stomp.

在古代，生命短暂而危险；从日出到日落能否存活都并非易事。在早期文明的大部分时期，地球上每年至少有四分之一的男性死于战争、饥荒、部落内讧，以及各种咬伤、蜇伤、毒液注射或践踏等意外。

Everywhere you turned, there was something that could easily kill you. Moving too slow or in the wrong direction meant the difference between life and death; there was no time to second-guess yourself. Nobody else could be trusted. To survive, you needed to trust your own judgment above that of all others, no matter what, acting on your own ideas without hesitating, and resisting the influence of risky outside ideas. Anything new and foreign is untested and, therefore, not to be trusted. The human brain is thus wired by evolution to distrust any information from the outside world and to greatly favor that which originates inside us.

无论你走到哪里，都可能随时丧命。行动迟缓或方向错误都可能生死攸关；你没有时间犹豫不决。任何人都不可信。为了生存，你必须始终相信自己的判断，胜过一切他人，毫不犹豫地执行自己的想法，并抵制外界危险思想的影响。任何新鲜事物和外来事物都未经检验，因此不可信赖。人类大脑的进化使其不信任任何来自外部世界的信息，而格外重视源自我们内心的信息。

Since childhood, others have been trying to smuggle their ideas into your mind. So naturally your mental defenses have gotten really good. It’s as if you have a small team of cognitive security guards and bouncers who are trained to keep unfamiliar and confusing ideas away.

从孩提时代起，就有人试图将他们的想法偷偷植入你的脑海。因此，你的心理防御机制自然而然地变得非常强大。就好像你拥有一支由认知保安和门卫组成的小队，他们训练有素，能够将陌生和令人困惑的想法拒之门外。

But salespeople are well trained too. The typical sales script tries to push past this resistance by exploiting your survival instincts, or the patterns of thinking you use when you’re stressed and need to move quick, without time to think. Consider these sales scripts: “I have another buyer on the line who wants it.” “This is the last one we have in stock.” “It’s thirty percent off !” These statements may sound innocent enough, but they are actually carefully constructed mental manipulations designed to stress your natural decision-making system.

但销售人员也训练有素。典型的销售话术会利用你的求生本能，或者说你在压力下需要快速行动、来不及思考时所使用的思维模式，来突破你的抵触情绪。想想这些销售话术：“还有一位顾客在线，他也想要这件商品。”“这是我们库存里最后一件了。”“打七折！”这些话听起来似乎没什么问题，但实际上都是精心设计的心理操控手段，旨在扰乱你自然的决策机制。

In the past, buyers accepted a high-pressure sales script as an unwanted but necessary part of the buying process because they genuinely needed the information that only an experienced sales rep could provide. But today, everyone can find, research, and buy anything online—so high-pressure sales scripts are not just unwelcome, they are hated.

过去，买家之所以接受高压销售话术，是因为他们虽然不受欢迎，但也是购买过程中必不可少的一部分，因为他们确实需要只有经验丰富的销售代表才能提供的信息。但如今，每个人都可以在网上查找、研究和购买任何东西——因此，高压销售话术不仅不受欢迎，而且令人厌恶。

In fact, these tactics are so outdated that even car manufacturers are abandoning them. In their studies, car companies found that the high-pressure scripts do more harm than good, often causing people to do the opposite of what you’re asking, just to prove that you aren’t controlling them—a phenomenon known as psychological reactance.

事实上，这些策略早已过时，就连汽车制造商也开始放弃使用。汽车公司的研究发现，高压推销话术弊大于利，往往会导致人们做出与你要求相反的事情，只是为了证明你并没有控制他们——这种现象被称为心理抗拒。

The way most people think of it, the act of selling is defined by psychological pressure. Salespeople always end up at this uncomfortable moment when they need to “close” and get the buyer to commit. But the buyer always responds in the same way:

在大多数人看来，销售行为是由心理压力驱动的。销售人员总会遇到需要“成交”并促使买家做出承诺的尴尬时刻。但买家的反应总是千篇一律：

  • First, by pacifying the seller: “Yes, yes, this looks terrific, you really have a great product.”
    首先，安抚卖家：“是的，是的，这看起来棒极了，你们的产品真的很好。”
  • Second, by backing away: “I just need to look a little more closely at the numbers.”
    其次，通过退缩：“我需要更仔细地看一下这些数字。”
  • Finally, by deferring the decision to an unavailable third party: “I will need to talk to my partner; he needs to approve an important decision like this.”
    最后，他将决定权推给了无法到场的第三方：“我需要和我的伴侣谈谈；像这样的重要决定需要他批准。”

If you’ve ever tried to sell anything to anyone, you’ve heard all this before, and you already know this is where deals go to die. Yet most salespeople feel pretty good when they get to the end of their pitch and the buyer says, “Yes, yes, this looks terrific, I just need to look a little more closely and talk to my partner; please write up everything you mentioned in a proposal, send it over, and we will discuss it and get back to you.” In fact, you shouldn’t feel good at all, because that deal is as good as dead.

如果你曾经尝试向任何人推销过东西，你肯定听过这些话，也知道交易往往止步于此。然而，大多数销售人员在推销结束时，如果买家说：“嗯，嗯，这看起来很棒，我需要再仔细看看，跟我的合伙人商量一下；请把您提到的所有内容写成一份提案，发过来，我们讨论一下再回复您”，他们都会感觉良好。但实际上，你根本不应该感到高兴，因为这笔交易基本上已经告吹了。

THE SCIENCE OF INCEPTION

受孕的科学

If you’ve ever bought a product you didn’t even know you wanted, or made choices that seemed a little out of character, then it’s likely you’ve had an idea implanted in your mind.

如果你曾经买过自己都不知道自己想要的产品，或者做出过一些看似与你性格不太相符的选择，那么很可能你的脑海中已经植入了一个想法。

Inception is the allegedly impossible implantation of an idea in someone’s mind so that they think it’s their own. It involves the ability to introduce parts of an idea to someone and create the perfect conditions for the whole idea to “surface” as if it were theirs, not yours.

“盗梦空间”指的是将一个想法植入他人脑海，使其误以为是自己的想法，而这在理论上是不可能的。它需要将想法的部分内容引入他人脑海，并创造完美的条件，使整个想法“浮现”出来，仿佛是对方的原创，而不是自己的。

You may have seen this in the movie of the same name. Inception is a 2010 Academy Award–winning sci-fi-action thriller written and directed by Christopher Nolan. In the film, an industrious neurological spy steals inaccessible, secret information from the mind of a rival businessman. The character’s mission is to plant certain ideas within his rival’s subconscious mind.

你可能在同名电影中见过这种手法。《盗梦空间》是一部荣获2010年奥斯卡金像奖的科幻动作惊悚片，由克里斯托弗·诺兰编剧并执导。影片讲述了一位勤奋的神经学间谍从竞争对手的脑海中窃取难以获取的秘密信息。他的任务是在竞争对手的潜意识中植入某些想法。

Like many good science fiction stories, the movie invented some of its own science. But it is seeded with a kernel of truth. Creating ideas for other people, however unlikely it may sound, is not only possible, it happens every day at the highest levels of business and government.

就像许多优秀的科幻故事一样，这部电影也虚构了一些科学概念。但它也蕴含着一些真理。为他人创造想法，无论听起来多么不可思议，不仅是可能的，而且在商业和政府的最高层每天都在发生。

Have you ever seen a sign that reads ONE PER CUSTOMER and immediately thought, “I’m going to figure out how to get two ”? This is a classic form of Inception. You simply forbid an action in order to encourage it, creating a kind of universal Do Not Push button that everyone wants to press. The reason? None of us want to be told what to do.

你有没有见过“每人限购一件”的标牌，然后立刻想到“我得想办法弄到两件”？这其实是典型的“盗梦空间”手法。你先禁止某种行为，然后反而鼓励它发生，从而创造出一个每个人都想按的“禁止按钮”。原因很简单：我们都不想被人指使。

But this example is just a hint of the full power of Inception, as I’m about to show you.

但这个例子仅仅是《盗梦空间》全部威力的冰山一角，接下来我就要向你展示这一点。

Certainly I did not invent the Inception method. It was always there in plain sight. I just uncovered it and explained how it works best in business situations. After all, writers for detective shows such as CSI and Law & Order have been implanting ideas in our minds for years. Consider how watching one of these shows always leads you to a moment when you as the viewer are able to put the pieces of the crime together and figure out who did it. You might say something like “I know what’s going on here! It has to be the cop—he stole the drugs and set the whole thing up!” This moment is predetermined, inevitable.

当然，我并非“盗梦空间”方法的发明者。它一直就在我们眼前。我只是把它挖掘出来，并解释了它在商业环境中如何发挥最佳效果。毕竟，像《犯罪现场调查》（CSI）和《法律与秩序》（Law & Order）这样的侦探剧的编剧们多年来一直在我们脑海中植入各种想法。想想看，观看这些剧集总会有一个时刻，让你作为观众能够将犯罪线索拼凑起来，找出真凶。你可能会说：“我知道是怎么回事了！肯定是那个警察——他偷了毒品，然后策划了这一切！”这个时刻是预先设定好的，是必然的。

You feel a rush of excitement when you identify the culprit before the big reveal happens on-screen, but that was always the writers’ plan. You’re meant to discover the answer on your own and feel good about it. That eureka moment has been carefully planned and programmed to deliver an insight at exactly the right time. When you put the pieces together before the detectives do, you feel smart, happy, powerful, and in control (exactly the emotions needed to motivate you to buy some canned beer, frozen pizza, and extra-soft toilet tissue). And you tune in next week so you can feel that way again.

在屏幕上揭晓真相之前，当你猜中真凶时，那种兴奋感油然而生，但这其实正是编剧的用意。他们希望你能自己发现答案，并为此感到自豪。这种灵光乍现的时刻经过精心策划和安排，旨在恰到好处地传递信息。当你比侦探们更早地拼凑出真相时，你会感到自己聪明、快乐、充满力量，一切尽在掌握（这些正是促使你购买罐装啤酒、冷冻披萨和超柔软卫生纸的必要情绪）。于是，你下周会准时收看，再次体验这种感觉。

Even if you don’t watch crime procedurals, you’ve probably experienced a moment like this, when a solution to the problem you’re working on suddenly materializes in your mind. Something just clicks and you see the answer. It feels almost like divine inspiration. You don’t doubt it. You don’t second-guess it. You trust it, believe in it, and act on it immediately—because it was your idea . And we are certain about our own ideas.

即使你不看犯罪剧，你也可能经历过类似的时刻：你正在研究的问题，解决方案突然在你脑海中浮现。就像灵光一闪，答案就出现了。这感觉几乎像是神启。你不会怀疑，也不会反复斟酌。你会相信它，坚信它，并立即付诸行动——因为这是你自己的想法。而我们总是对自己的想法充满信心。

We don’t just find it satisfying when our brain comes up with ideas on its own, we also value those ideas more highly. If you handed someone an origami swan folded out of plain printer paper and asked the person how much they would pay for it, they might say they’d pay nothing, or just twenty-five cents. Almost never a dollar. But if instead you taught them step-by-step how to fold the same swan out of plain paper themselves, then asked them to estimate the value of the paper bird they’d just folded, you would get a much higher number. Maybe three dollars or even four. Researchers have proven this many times in multiple settings.

我们不仅会因为大脑自主产生想法而感到满足，还会更加重视这些想法。如果你递给别人一只用普通打印纸折成的折纸天鹅，问他们愿意出多少钱，他们可能会说一分钱也不愿意出，或者只愿意出25美分。几乎没人会出1美元。但如果你一步一步地教他们如何用普通纸自己折出同样的折纸天鹅，然后让他们评估一下自己折的这只纸鸟的价值，你会得到一个更高的数字。也许是3美元，甚至4美元。研究人员已经在多种情况下多次证实了这一点。

The same is true with an idea. Make people feel like the idea is coming from them and they will place more value on it, believe it more deeply, adopt it more quickly, and remember it more easily.

想法也是如此。如果人们觉得这个想法是他们自己提出的，他们就会更重视它，更深信不疑，更快地接受它，也更容易记住它。

This book will reveal the Inception script to you. In the pages that follow, I will show you exactly how to target the part of the brain that produces the feeling of Ding! I’ve got it! When you present an idea like this, everyone who is listening will trust and believe in it because the idea will feel like it originated in the depths of their own minds.

这本书将为你揭示《盗梦空间》的剧本。在接下来的篇章中，我将向你展示如何精准地激活大脑中产生“叮！我明白了！”这种感觉的区域。当你提出这样的想法时，所有听众都会信任并相信它，因为这个想法仿佛源自他们内心深处。

So how do you plant an idea in someone’s head in a way that makes them feel like it was theirs (especially if you’re not the head writer for a long-running crime drama)? Researchers have found that Inception moments arrive suddenly, in a burst; there is no gradual buildup in the brain. We sit there, pondering all the pieces of the puzzle, and at some point, out of the blue, there is a huge spike of activity in the superior temporal gyrus, a tiny bundle of neurons on the right side of the brain, just below the temple, that’s tied to the feeling of certainty we get when an idea is our own. And then, a short while later, we consciously know the answer.

那么，如何才能将一个想法植入他人脑海，让他们感觉这个想法是自己想出来的呢？（尤其如果你不是长篇犯罪剧的首席编剧）研究人员发现，这种“盗梦空间”般的灵感迸发是突然发生的，如同脉冲一般；大脑中并没有逐渐积累的过程。我们坐在那里，思考着所有可能的线索，突然间，大脑右侧颞上回（位于太阳穴下方的一小束神经元）的活动出现了巨大的峰值。颞上回与我们对某个想法的确定感密切相关，这种确定感源于我们自己的想法。然后，不久之后，我们便会恍然大悟，知道了答案。

When you can reliably re-create this exact sequence of events in the mind of the person you are trying to influence, you will be able to trigger Inception.

当你能够可靠地在你想影响的人的脑海中重现这一系列事件时，你就能触发“盗梦空间”。

Does that sound impossible? Or like science fiction? In truth, it’s neither. It starts by throwing out the old scripts. I’m going to teach you a new one. Master these six techniques and you’ll never have to ask someone to do what you want again; they will come up with the idea all by themselves.

听起来是不是天方夜谭？或者像科幻小说？其实，两者都不是。首先要摒弃旧有的思维模式。我会教你一套全新的方法。掌握这六项技巧，你就再也不用开口求人了；他们会自己想出办法。

#↩

CHAPTER 2

第二章

The New Dominance Hierarchy

新的支配等级

W ho gets what, and why?

谁得到什么，为什么？

It’s tempting to think you should get financial rewards in a fair way, according to your effort, sacrifice, and contribution, and while this might sound great in the gospels, it is not how we as a species operate . Humans operate, and have always operated, within a rigid power framework that I call the dominance hierarchy , where the few who exist at the top get more of the best of everything, and those at the bottom get the scraps.

人们很容易认为，付出、牺牲和贡献理应得到公平的经济回报。虽然这在福音书中听起来很美好，但这并非我们人类的生存之道。人类一直以来都生活在一个僵化的权力框架中，我称之为等级制度。在这个框架下，少数处于顶层的人攫取一切最好的东西，而底层的人只能得到残羹剩饭。

For the last million years it was nearly impossible to change your social position in society without an army behind you, because status was based purely on physical strength. Life was a simple system where the biggest, toughest, most aggressive members of a social group would get anything and everything they wanted until they were eventually challenged and killed by an up-and-comer in a never-ending cycle of life and death.

在过去的一百万年里，如果没有军队的支持，几乎不可能改变一个人的社会地位，因为社会地位完全取决于体力。生活是一个简单的体系：一个社会群体中体型最大、最强壮、最具攻击性的成员可以得到他们想要的一切，直到最终被后来者挑战并杀死，如此循环往复，永无止境。

Something changed around the first millennium. As human tribes got bigger and more complex it was no longer possible to challenge everyone to fight in order to establish your place in the social layer cake. A new dominance hierarchy emerged in which social status surpassed physical size as the means to influence others.

大约在公元第一个千年左右，情况发生了变化。随着人类部落规模的扩大和复杂性的增加，通过挑战所有人进行战斗来确立自己在社会阶层中的地位已不再可行。一种新的等级制度应运而生，社会地位超越了体型，成为影响他人的主要手段。

But we never truly mastered this new dominance hierarchy. Even today, improving your social ranking rarely happens easily, quickly, or even at all because your ranking is one of the most difficult things to change unless you have been trained to do so. Social mobility for most people is fixed at birth. Unless you are very lucky and get picked out of a fast-food restaurant while wearing a chicken suit like Brad Pitt or can throw a 99-mile-per-hour fastball like Max Scherzer to earn $200 million, social mobility is limited.

但我们从未真正掌握这种新的等级制度。即使在今天，提升社会地位也鲜少易事，因为除非经过专门训练，否则社会地位是最难改变的事情之一。对大多数人来说，社会流动性在出生时就已确定。除非你运气极佳，像布拉德·皮特那样穿着鸡服在快餐店被选中，或者像马克斯·谢泽尔那样投出时速99英里的快速球赚到2亿美元，否则社会流动性是有限的。

While those on top ultimately fall, and those on the bottom eventually rise, this typically occurs across a span of several generations. The hard truth is that you inherit your underlying social ranking from your parents the same way you inherit your height. In other words, your birth is your fate unless you master the tools that will allow you to change your position in the social layer cake. The problem is that most people have misunderstood the process of how to do this.

虽然身居高位者终将跌落谷底，底层者终将崛起，但这通常需要几代人的时间才能完成。残酷的现实是，你的社会地位就像你的身高一样，是从父母那里继承来的。换句话说，除非你掌握了改变自身社会地位的技巧，否则你的出身就是你的命运。问题在于，大多数人误解了如何做到这一点。

But it can be done.

但这并非不可能。

After spending many years studying the science of power and dominance, my team and I have discovered a way for you to match status and power with anyone, in any business or social situation. And it takes only about thirty seconds to pull off when you understand how it works. In order to explain the process, and why it is so effective, I need to introduce you to Ötzi the Iceman.

经过多年对权力和支配力科学的研究，我和我的团队发现了一种方法，无论在任何商业或社交场合，都能让你与任何人势均力敌，掌控权力。一旦你理解了它的运作原理，只需大约三十秒就能掌握。为了解释这个过程以及它为何如此有效，我需要向你介绍一下冰人奥茨。

Ötzi excited the scientific community when he was found frozen in the Italian Alps in 1991 in near-perfect condition. Finally, archaeologists would be able to study the daily routines and social structures of a 70,000-year-old man. An analysis of Ötzi’s stomach’s contents revealed that his last meal was ibex (a horrible-tasting kind of deer) and poison fern.

1991年，奥茨冰人在意大利阿尔卑斯山被发现，他几乎完好无损地被冰封在山上，这令科学界兴奋不已。考古学家终于有机会研究一位7万年前老人的日常生活和社会结构。对奥茨冰人胃内容物的分析显示，他的最后一餐是野山羊（一种味道极其难吃的鹿）和毒蕨。

Ötzi didn’t have a very good last couple of days, and it’s doubtful he had many good days at all during his short nomadic life. His toes were mangled from years of frostbite, half his teeth were gone, parasitic worm eggs filled his intestines, and he was partially blind from repeated doses of fern toxin. But it wasn’t the poison that killed him—it was an arrow in the back of his head from some locals whose territory he walked into. That area must have been “locals only.”

奥茨冰人生命的最后几天过得并不好，而且在他短暂的游牧生活中，恐怕也鲜少有好日子可过。他的脚趾因多年冻伤而严重变形，一半的牙齿都掉了，肠道里充满了寄生虫卵，而且由于反复接触蕨类毒素，他的双目也部分失明。但最终夺走他性命的并非毒素，而是他误入的当地居民的领地后脑勺中箭。那片区域一定是“本地人专属”的。

The day he was killed, Ötzi either had the wrong kind of tattoos or was wearing the wrong color of clothing or didn’t have the right amulet on his arm. What scientists have discovered after studying Ötzi’s remains, and the remains of others like him, is that early humans relied on visual cues to determine social status and tribal affiliation. As tribes got bigger and the social layer cake expanded, we had to start responding to external cues of power such as uniforms, tattoos, clothing, family crests, and titles. It soon became second nature for us to recognize and act on these indicators of position and power.

奥茨冰人遇害那天，要么是纹身不对，要么是衣服颜色不对，要么是手臂上没有佩戴合适的护身符。科学家们通过研究奥茨冰人的遗骸以及其他类似冰人的遗骸发现，早期人类依靠视觉线索来判断社会地位和部落归属。随着部落规模的扩大和社会阶层的增多，我们不得不开始关注诸如制服、纹身、服饰、家族徽章和头衔等外部权力信号。很快，识别并运用这些地位和权力的标志就成了我们的本能反应。

Today, a mix of subtle visual and verbal cues help you instantly recognize the social status of people around you. The way you dress, the precise words you use in conversation, the tone of your voice, and your behavior in specific situations will all telegraph your status within a group or society at large.

如今，一些微妙的视觉和语言线索可以帮助你迅速识别周围人的社会地位。你的穿着打扮、谈话中使用的措辞、语气以及在特定场合的行为，都会透露你在群体或整个社会中的地位。

When you learn to recognize and control these words and symbols, you can change your position in the social layer cake at will. You can enter a completely unfamiliar social group in just a few seconds and create enormous influence in the process. During the past few years I have worked with the high-status ultra-rich on some very large deals, and I’ve seen the power of simple cues to rapidly create wealth or leave behind missed opportunities. In the process, I’ve mastered a new set of tools that will allow you to change your position in the dominance hierarchy by simply uttering a few sentences. That’s how I closed one of the craziest deals of my career.

当你学会识别和掌控这些词语和符号，你就能随心所欲地改变自己在社会阶层中的位置。你可以在短短几秒钟内融入一个完全陌生的社交群体，并在此过程中建立巨大的影响力。过去几年，我曾与一些地位显赫的超级富豪合作，参与过一些规模巨大的交易，亲眼见证了简单的暗示如何迅速创造财富，或错失良机。在此过程中，我掌握了一套全新的工具，只需几句话，就能改变你在权力等级中的位置。我正是凭借这套工具，促成了我职业生涯中最疯狂的交易之一。

IN SEARCH OF $25 MILLION

寻找2500万美元

I was speeding down Rexford Drive in Los Angeles, past heirloom hedges and giant wrought-iron gates that concealed some of the most legendary real estate in Beverly Hills. During the next two hours I was going to have one shot to make a $25 million deal, which was not an ideal situation because this deal looked manageable when I started, but now nothing about it was going my way and at this point there was only one man who could help.

我当时正飞驰在洛杉矶的雷克斯福德大道上，路过古老的树篱和巨大的锻铁大门，它们掩映着比佛利山庄一些最传奇的房产。接下来的两个小时里，我只有一次机会促成一笔价值2500万美元的交易。情况并不乐观，因为这笔交易起初看起来还算顺利，但现在一切都对我不利，而此时此刻，只有一个人能帮到我。

John King is a very wealthy but very off-the-grid loner with no attachments who was unreachable by phone and popped up only for the occasional hit-and-run media appearance. Think of him as the billionaire business version of Jason Bourne. Since 1999 his website had only two words, “coming soon.” His receptionist was an answering machine. Nobody in my Rolodex could connect us, either. For two weeks I’d been searching for him, because this was the man I needed to pitch my deal to. It’s not that he was avoiding me; he just didn’t know I existed and hadn’t been around to hear my offer. But that’s something I knew how to fix. Let me explain:

约翰·金是个非常富有但极其隐居的独行侠，没有任何牵绊，电话也打不通，只偶尔在媒体上露面，一闪而过。你可以把他想象成亿万富翁版的杰森·伯恩。自1999年以来，他的网站上只有两个字：“即将上线”。他的接待员是一台答录机。我通讯录里的人也帮不上忙。我找了他两个星期，因为我需要向他推销我的项目。倒不是他故意躲着我，只是他根本不知道我的存在，也没机会听到我的提议。不过我知道该怎么解决这个问题。让我来解释一下：

My business model is pretty simple. People hire me to do three basic things:

我的商业模式很简单。人们雇佣我做三件基本事情：

  1. Get meetings with wealthy investors.
    与富有的投资者会面。
  2. Pitch them an irresistible offer.
    向他们提出一个无法拒绝的条件。
  3. Close the deal and get the money.
    完成交易，拿到钱。

I charge a lot for this kind of work, so nobody ever hands me the easy jobs, and over time I’ve become the patron saint of tough deals. If no one else can get it done, Just give it to Oren , people would say.

我做这类工作收费很高，所以没人会把简单的活儿交给我，久而久之，我成了棘手交易的守护神。人们常说，如果别人搞不定，那就交给奥伦吧。

My client on this deal was a successful solar company with plans to buy a large plot of land in Arizona and build a lucrative energy farm. I had promised to find and deliver $25 million, which should have been a manageable task. Except it wasn’t. One problem had led to another and every investor I’d lined up had evaporated before their wire transfer came through. It was starting to feel like this deal was cursed.

我的客户是一家成功的太阳能公司，计划在亚利桑那州购买一大片土地，建造一座利润丰厚的太阳能发电厂。我承诺筹集并交付2500万美元，这本应是一项轻松的任务。然而，事实并非如此。一个问题接踵而至，我联系上的所有投资者都在汇款到账前就消失了。我开始觉得这笔交易似乎被诅咒了。

With time running out, I now had no choice but to focus on a single investor who could snap up the whole deal. That put me on a collision course with John King, one of the top energy investors in the world. For a guy like John, this deal was just the right size for a quick yes. A guy on his level could do it with a handshake and two sheets of paper, if he loved it. But, of course, he wasn’t going to be easy to persuade because he wasn’t easy to find.

时间紧迫，我别无选择，只能集中精力寻找一位能够一口气拿下整个项目的投资者。这让我与约翰·金——世界顶级能源投资者之一——正面交锋。对于像约翰这样的人来说，这笔交易的规模恰到好处，他可以迅速答应。如果他看中了，像他这样的大人物只需握手和两张纸就能搞定。当然，要说服他并不容易，因为他本身就很难找到。

With the clock ticking and my repeated attempts to get in touch with John coming up short, I was close to losing my commission while making quite a few people angry. If you’re in sales or have ever had a big deal lined up, you’ve probably been at this point before, where your hopes of success are dwindling and suddenly you’re open to new suggestions or doing some things that seem a little out of character. That’s how I decided to attend the unusual sounding Altitude Series conference, which was part music festival and part business meet-up, and not my normal cup of tea. But a reliable source had told me John was possibly going to attend, and that was all I knew. The situation didn’t sound very promising, but I was down to try anything.

时间一分一秒地流逝，我多次尝试联系约翰却都无果，眼看就要丢掉佣金，还惹恼了不少人。如果你是销售人员，或者曾经有过洽谈大单的经历，你可能也经历过这种时刻：成功的希望越来越渺茫，突然间，你开始愿意接受新的建议，或者做一些看似与你性格不符的事情。正因如此，我决定参加听起来很特别的“高海拔系列”会议。这个会议融合了音乐节和商务洽谈的元素，完全不是我平时喜欢的类型。但一位可靠的消息人士告诉我，约翰可能会出席，而我对此也一无所知。情况听起来不太乐观，但我愿意尝试任何方法。

While typical business conferences are usually held downtown at a large hotel near the convention center, the address for the Altitude Series took me up Benedict Canyon to a mansion in the North Beverly Hills. The founders of Altitude were rule breakers. After all, they had once asked me to help them buy an entire mountain ski resort, which I did, and which is how I knew them in the first place and was able to get an invitation. As I pulled up to the gate, I started to enter a different and unfamiliar world, as you’ll see in a moment.

典型的商务会议通常在市中心会议中心附近的大型酒店举行，但Altitude Series的举办地点却在北比佛利山庄，沿着本尼迪克特峡谷一路向上，来到了一栋豪宅。Altitude的创始人都是特立独行的人。毕竟，他们曾经邀请我帮忙收购一座山地滑雪度假村，而我也确实这么做了，正是这件事让我认识了他们，并最终获得了邀请。当我把车停在门口时，我仿佛踏入了一个截然不同、陌生的世界，稍后你就会明白我的意思。

Cars were parked up and down the street, but according to my invitation I had “VIP access” and “on-site valet parking,” so I hit the call button, announced myself, and the enormous gate creaked open. I pulled my car onto the circular drive and up to the private residence, which was the size of a country club.

街道两旁停满了车，但根据我的邀请函，我享有“贵宾通道”和“现场代客泊车”服务，于是我按下呼叫按钮，表明身份，巨大的大门吱呀一声打开了。我把车开上环形车道，来到这座私人住宅前，它的大小堪比一个乡村俱乐部。

As I pulled to a stop by the fountain in the center of the cobblestone driveway, a young valet stepped toward my window with his hand outstretched for the keys. The car I was driving might not look like much to you, but my red 1971 Alfa Romeo Sprint GT is an enthusiast special and I spent three years restoring it. Nobody touches it but me. I rolled down the window to tell the valet what I always tell valets: I want to park it myself, no offense, happy to tip you, just point me to an open spot.

我把车停在鹅卵石车道中央的喷泉旁，一位年轻的泊车员走到我的车窗前，伸出手要车钥匙。我开的这辆车或许在你看来毫不起眼，但我的这辆1971年款红色阿尔法罗密欧Sprint GT可是车迷的珍藏版，我花了三年时间才把它修复好。除了我，谁也别想碰它。我摇下车窗，像往常一样对泊车员说：我想自己停车，别介意，我很乐意给你小费，你只要告诉我哪里有空位就行。

“Oh yeah, I figured you’d want to park it yourself,” the kid said, talking fast.

“哦，是啊，我就知道你会想自己停车，”孩子语速飞快地说。

But what he said next, I wasn’t expecting at all. “I just was curious whether you had the dual-Weber carb-kit, because it sounds like you’re running a set of four-valve, flat-top, forged pistons. ” That immediately caught my attention. He continued, “I bought a 1969 Sprint last year and had Simon at Alfaholics blueprint the motor with that same setup. . . . ”

但他接下来说的话，我完全没想到。“我只是好奇你是不是装了双韦伯化油器套件，因为听起来你用的是一套四气门平顶锻造活塞。” 这立刻引起了我的注意。他接着说：“我去年买了一辆1969年的Sprint，然后让Alfaholics的Simon用同样的配置对发动机进行了精密调校……”

Those forty-two words acted like a secret code to let me know this kid was on a completely different and higher level of the social layer cake than I’d initially thought. In about eight seconds I went from thinking, This random college kid is going to dent my car , to This fine young man can hook me up with Simon at Alfaholics! Clearly he was an enthusiast at my level, and probably even higher.

那四十二个字就像一个秘密代码，让我意识到这孩子在社交层面上的水平远超我的预期。短短八秒钟，我的心态就从“这陌生大学生会不会把我的车撞凹”变成了“这位帅哥能帮我联系上Alfaholics的Simon！”。显然，他和我一样是个狂热爱好者，甚至可能比我更胜一筹。

Without a second thought I tossed my keys to the kid, along with fifty bucks. He smiled and slid into the driver’s seat of my prized Alfa, as I walked toward the garden entrance. “I’ve got a safe spot on the other side,” he shouted. Perfect. I never looked back.

我毫不犹豫地把钥匙和五十块钱扔给了那孩子。他笑着坐进了我那辆宝贝阿尔法罗密欧的驾驶座，我则走向花园入口。“我在另一边有个安全的地方，”他喊道。太好了。我头也不回地走了。

THE CONFERENCE

会议

Think for a moment about the last business conference you attended. Exciting? Probably not. Most conferences are tiresome industry events you want to leave as soon as the main speaker has wrapped up, but I knew Altitude was different and special the second I walked in because to the left and right, the famous and nearly famous packed the entire backyard and house. Live musicians played in small alcoves. Celebrities mingled with other beautiful people at cozy bar stations. Small stages had been erected at the outside perimeter of the garden for speakers to hold forth on various topics like climate solutions, artificial intelligence, energy, and space. I’d come here to talk to John King, but I was getting distracted by all these casual conversations between some of my favorite movie stars and musicians around every corner.

想想你上次参加的商务会议。令人兴奋吗？大概不会。大多数会议都是令人厌烦的行业盛会，你恨不得主讲人一结束就赶紧离开。但我一踏进Altitude就知道它与众不同，因为左右两边，名人和准名人挤满了整个后院和房子。现场乐队在小壁龛里演奏。明星们在舒适的吧台边与其他俊男靓女们觥筹交错。花园外围搭建了小型舞台，演讲者们就气候解决方案、人工智能、能源和太空等各种话题畅谈。我本来是来找约翰·金的，但却被周围我最喜欢的电影明星和音乐家们轻松愉快的交谈分散了注意力。

Hungry, I grabbed a tempura roll from a bar off to the side. Not more than twenty seconds later, a guy who looked a lot like John King passed right in front of me, then angled off to the right and into the dense crowd. I darted after him, catching another glimpse as he slipped into the main house, which was packed with people. It was King for sure. Though his net worth was rumored to be $2 billion, there was no mistaking his signature outfit: 501 jeans and Rush concert T-shirt.

我饿了，便从旁边的小吧台拿了一份天妇罗卷。不到二十秒，一个长得酷似约翰·金的人从我面前走过，然后斜向右侧，钻进了拥挤的人群。我赶紧追了上去，在他溜进人山人海的主厅时，我又瞥见了他一眼。没错，就是金本人。虽然据说他的身价高达20亿美元，但他标志性的装扮——501牛仔裤和Rush乐队演唱会T恤——却让人一眼就能认出来。

I dashed into the foyer, but King was gone just as fast as he’d come, and I was left scanning a sea of smiling faces. Where did he go? I realized then, it wasn’t going to be easy to find a man who didn’t want to be found.

我冲进门厅，但金消失得无影无踪，只留下我茫然地扫视着一张张笑脸。他去哪儿了？我这才意识到，要找到一个不想被人找到的人，可不是件容易的事。

I kicked myself as I thought about the drawer of concert T’s I had back home and was wishing I’d brought one of my own Rush shirts. It would have been an easy icebreaker for the eventual moment I would come face to face with John. But it’s critical to keep in mind that shallow similarities and shared interests do not deliver the powerful kind of status alignment you need to create influence, persuasion, and inception.

我懊恼地想着家里那抽屉的演唱会T恤，真希望当时带了一件自己的Rush乐队T恤。如果带了，下次见到John的时候就能轻松打开话匣子了。但必须记住，肤浅的相似之处和共同的兴趣爱好并不能带来你所需要的那种强大的地位认同，而这种认同是建立影响力、说服力和促成合作所必需的。

ACHIEVING STATUS ALIGNMENT

实现地位一致性

If you want to understand the power of status alignment, a good place to start is at the opposite, or status mis-alignment. For example, have you ever put in a call to customer service (maybe for a credit card charge you didn’t recognize) and found yourself on the phone with an agent who doesn’t have enough power to solve your problem? As your frustration grows, you insist, once again, that you be transferred to a manager. Nothing else will do.

如果你想了解职权一致性的力量，不妨从其反面——职权不一致性入手。例如，你是否曾经致电客服（可能是因为一笔你不认识的信用卡消费），却发现接电话的客服人员权限不足，无法解决你的问题？随着你的沮丧情绪不断加剧，你再次坚持要求转接给经理。除此之外，别无他法。

Sure, you could just keep talking to the helpful-sounding agent who is patiently listening to your situation, earnestly trying to solve your problem. But you won’t stay on with them long, because the moment you realize this person is not going to be able to help you, they become irrelevant. Even if they’re trying to make helpful suggestions, dutifully explaining the company’s policy, you tune them out completely, staying on the line for only one reason: to get bumped up to a manager who has some real juice and can quickly fix your problem.

当然，你可以继续和那位听起来很热心、耐心倾听你情况、真心实意想帮你解决问题的客服人员沟通。但你不会和他们耗太久，因为一旦你意识到这个人帮不了你，他们就变得无关紧要了。即使他们试图提出有用的建议，尽职尽责地解释公司政策，你也会完全充耳不闻，继续在线只有一个目的：那就是联系上真正有权有势、能迅速解决你问题的经理。

This is a very specific kind of failure where a person of high status and one of low status try to work together, and it doesn’t work at all. It’s the feeling you experience whenever you’re talking to someone who is in the wrong part of the dominance hierarchy, either too low or too high. At first, it’s frustrating. The more you talk to them, the better you come to understand they will not be able to help you. As frustration mounts, you reach a point where you tune them out and look instead for someone at the right part of the food chain to connect with.

这是一种非常特殊的失败：地位高的人和地位低的人试图合作，结果却完全失败。当你和处于等级制度错误位置的人交谈时，就会产生这种感觉——要么太低，要么太高。起初，你会感到沮丧。但你和他们交谈得越多，就越明白他们帮不了你。随着挫败感不断累积，你会逐渐不再理会他们，转而寻找等级制度中更合适的人来建立联系。

That frustrated feeling you experience on the phone with a customer service representative who can’t help you is the same feeling someone else gets about you when they feel you’re not on their level and you don’t understand their issues.

当你打电话给客服代表，对方却无法帮你解决问题时，你感受到的那种沮丧感，和别人觉得你跟他们不在一个层次，无法理解他们的问题时，他们对你的感觉是一样的。

You cannot get the full attention of a decision maker to listen to your idea if they think you’re on a different level of the dominance hierarchy than they are. When you’re going to press someone toward an important decision, you first need to be sure he or she feels they are in the right place at the right time with the right person. To accomplish this, you must create Status Alignment.

如果决策者认为你和他们在权力等级上处于不同的位置，你就无法让他们全神贯注地倾听你的想法。当你试图说服某人做出重要决定时，首先要确保他们觉得自己在正确的时间、正确的地点遇到了正确的人。要做到这一点，你必须建立地位一致性。

Status Alignment comes when you’re in front of a decision maker and you have perfectly raised or lowered your own status to match the decision maker’s view of himself. Armed with this understanding of how the dominance hierarchy works, I make sure to carefully staff each of my business deals with a talent stack that any other dealmaker can recognize and easily plug into. My talent stack usually looks like this, starting at the top and in order of importance:

地位一致性是指当你面对决策者时，你恰到好处地提升或降低自身地位，使其与决策者对自身的认知相匹配。基于对支配等级运作方式的理解，我会在每次商务洽谈中精心挑选合适的人才，确保任何其他洽谈者都能轻松识别并融入其中。我的人才架构通常如下，从上到下按重要性排序：

  1. Me (the dealmaker)
    我（交易撮合者）
  2. Financial Officer
    财务主管
  3. Marketing Officer
    市场营销专员
  4. Sr. Analyst
    高级分析师
  5. Legal
    合法的
  6. Client Relations
    客户关系
  7. Jr. Accountant
    初级会计师
  8. Assistant
    助手

Eight people for one deal. Why stack up all this headcount and expense? Because when the deal is underway, it’s essential to get my team members to match up correctly with the other side’s team. I need my analyst to talk to their analyst, my lawyer to talk to their lawyer, and my finance person to talk to their finance person, leaving me to talk directly to their CEO or decision maker—as equals. These are the correct matchups. It has to be this way because “bad matchups” create an out-of-whack dominance hierarchy where the wrong people are covering one another, assuring the deal will go sideways and eventually blow up.

八个人只为完成一笔交易。为什么要投入这么多人力和财力？因为交易进行时，确保我的团队成员与对方团队对接至关重要。我需要我的分析师与对方的分析师沟通，我的律师与对方的律师沟通，我的财务人员与对方的财务人员沟通，这样我才能直接与对方的CEO或决策者平等对话。这才是正确的对接方式。必须如此，因为“错误的对接”会造成权力等级失衡，导致不合适的人互相包庇，最终使交易偏离轨道，甚至彻底失败。

The idea of bad matchups couldn’t be more true in business than it is in sports, military, or other professions. So it’s useful to think about this in context of making a deal or orchestrating any high-stakes sale. Even if you’re a salesperson or a one-man shop, you still will benefit from having a working team of virtual assistant, technical person, and an accountant. Not to impress others. Not to showboat or hotdog. The simple purpose is to lighten your workload and most importantly to create alignment.

在商业领域，劣势对决的危害不亚于在体育、军事或其他行业。因此，在洽谈交易或策划任何高风险销售时，思考这个问题都至关重要。即使你只是个销售员或单打独斗，拥有一个由虚拟助理、技术人员和会计组成的高效团队也会让你受益匪浅。这并非为了炫耀或卖弄，而是为了减轻你的工作负担，更重要的是，为了确保团队协作顺畅。

To maintain Status Alignment, put yourself in the lead position, keep yourself scarce, and only do things that are consistent with your status on the team and as the one in charge. The easiest and best way to influence a decision maker is when you are in Status Alignment.

为了保持地位一致性，你需要让自己处于领导地位，保持低调，并且只做与你在团队中的地位以及作为负责人的身份相符的事情。影响决策者最简单有效的方法就是保持地位一致性。

Here’s another example to help make the point. Imagine you’re visiting your brother in the hospital. You don’t have to know the nurse’s name and life story in order to understand her position in the dominance hierarchy, because she has a uniform and badge to signify it. When she asks you to step outside the room so that a medical procedure can happen, you obey. Humans have no trouble accepting that something symbolic, such as the uniform and ID card, can signify position and power in the hierarchy.

这里还有一个例子来说明这一点。想象一下，你去医院探望你的兄弟。你不需要知道护士的名字和人生经历就能明白她在等级制度中的地位，因为她穿着制服，佩戴徽章，这些都表明了她的身份。当她请你到病房外去进行医疗操作时，你会照做。人们很容易接受这样一种象征性的东西：制服和身份卡，可以代表等级制度中的地位和权力。

But could a nurse ever tell you what to think or what you should or shouldn’t believe in? In other words, would you change your attitude about something important because a nurse ordered you to? Probably not. Only someone on your level, such as a close coworker or friend, can truly and deeply influence you in a way the nurse never can.

但护士能告诉你该怎么想，该相信什么或不相信什么吗？换句话说，你会因为护士的命令而改变对某件重要事情的态度吗？恐怕不会。只有与你地位相当的人，比如亲密的同事或朋友，才能真正深刻地影响你，而这是护士永远无法做到的。

This is the difference between obedience and influence.

这就是服从和影响之间的区别。

When the nurse orders you to head to the waiting room, you do it—you’re obedient. When a judge tells you to report for community service, you do as you’re told. In these situations it’s easy to see how the other person is above you in the dominance hierarchy. Accordingly, you follow their orders. But neither the nurse nor the judge has really influenced you or changed your beliefs in any meaningful way.

当护士让你去候诊室时，你会照做——你很听话。当法官让你去参加社区服务时，你也会服从命令。在这些情况下，很容易看出对方在等级制度中处于更高的地位。因此，你会服从他们的命令。但无论是护士还是法官，都没有真正影响你，也没有从根本上改变你的信念。

Influence, and particularly Inception, is most effective when the person you are speaking to feels like he or she is on the same level of the hierarchy as you. This is where Inception is strongest and works the best. Before you can implant an idea in someone else’s mind, you need to create a feeling of Status Alignment. That’s what happened with the valet at the front gate of Altitude. In less than thirty seconds I realized he wasn’t an average parking attendant; he was a car enthusiast and at my level in the sports car world. I immediately felt he could be trusted. It’s a simple example, but perfectly illustrates the feeling of Status Alignment. And that’s exactly what I was about to do to one of the biggest real estate investors on the planet.

影响力，尤其是“植入式影响”，在你与对方交谈时最为有效，因为对方会感觉与你处于同一等级。这正是“植入式影响”最强、最有效的地方。在将想法植入他人脑海之前，你需要营造一种地位认同感。我在Altitude酒店门口遇到的代客泊车员就是如此。不到三十秒，我就意识到他并非普通的停车管理员；他是一位汽车爱好者，在跑车领域与我水平相当。我立刻觉得他值得信赖。这是一个简单的例子，却完美地诠释了地位认同感。而这正是我即将对一位全球最大的房地产投资者所做的事情。

But first I had to find him.

但首先我得找到他。

IS ANYONE IN CHARGE HERE?

这里有人负责吗？

As “cool” and “hip” and “unique” as the vibe was at the Altitude Series, it was still a business conference, and conferences are never great places for getting deals done because there are so many distractions going on from minute to minute. You barely have anyone’s attention for thirty seconds before they are pulled away to the next most important conversation. But there is one huge advantage to conferences: Your target is always easy to find because everyone wears a brightly colored name tag highlighting their name, industry, and position.

尽管Altitude Series的氛围“酷炫”、“时尚”、“独特”，但它终究是一场商务会议。而商务会议从来都不是达成交易的好地方，因为每时每刻都有各种各样的干扰。你几乎无法吸引任何人的注意力超过30秒，他们就会被下一个更重要的话题吸引过去。不过，商务会议也有一个巨大的优势：你的目标客户总是很容易找到，因为每个人都佩戴着醒目的名牌，上面标明了他们的姓名、行业和职位。

I quickly ran into a problem at Altitude, however: There were no name tags, there was no information booth, and nobody seemed to be in charge. Now, I was standing stiffly, like a big confused dummy looking for “Hello My Name Is” tags or colored badges on lanyards or just a shirt that said STAFF . But there was nothing even close. I was starting to get frustrated because John had to be nearby—after all, I’d just seen him a few minutes earlier.

然而，我在Altitude很快就遇到了麻烦：没有名牌，没有咨询台，似乎也没有负责人。我像个傻瓜一样僵硬地站在那里，到处寻找“你好，我的名字是”之类的名牌，或者挂在挂绳上的彩色徽章，又或者只是一件印着“员工”字样的衬衫。但什么都没有。我开始感到沮丧，因为约翰肯定就在附近——毕竟，几分钟前我还见过他。

I stood on a small ledge to get above the crowd, scanning for John a little too conspicuously by moving my head back and forth like a broken radar dish. I was soon drawing attention from some other conference goers. An attractive woman said, “You look so tense.” Her companion said, “Relax . . . Altitude is a special place to meet new friends, find empowerment, and connect with yourself.”

我站在一小块凸起的平台上，以便能俯瞰人群，像个坏掉的雷达天线一样来回晃动着脑袋，显得有些太显眼，四处搜寻约翰的踪迹。很快，我就引起了其他一些与会者的注意。一位漂亮的女士说：“你看上去很紧张。”她的同伴说：“放松点……高海拔是个结识新朋友、获得力量、与自我对话的特别地方。”

I didn’t want to connect with myself. I only wanted to connect with John King.

我不想与自己建立联系，我只想与约翰·金建立联系。

The women locked their arms with mine and swung me firmly in the wrong direction toward a bar in the corner of a patio. They insisted I have a drink, so I asked the bartender what beers she was serving. “Heineken, Budweiser, Corona,” she said. “What’ll you have?” Well, that was definitely not the greatest selection. “C’mon,” I said, leaning in closer. “Did I walk into a bar mitzvah by mistake?”

女人们挽着我的胳膊，用力把我往错误的方向拽，拽到露台角落的吧台。她们非要我喝一杯，于是我问酒保有什么啤酒。“喜力、百威、科罗娜，”她说，“你要什么？” 好吧，这选择可真够少的。“拜托，”我凑近了些说，“我这是不小心闯进犹太教成人礼了吗？”

“Yeah, tell me about it,” she said, rolling her eyes. “Not my call.”

“是啊，可不是嘛，”她翻了个白眼说，“这不由我决定。”

I’ve found that if you accuse a bartender of serving “bar mitzvah beer” you’ll get one of two reactions. About half will stare at you blankly; they have no idea what you’re talking about. In this case your bartender is a college kid picking up some extra change by working a conference. But the other half will roll their eyes and say, “Yeah, tell me about it . . . this beer selection was not my call.” These are real bartenders who know their stuff.

我发现，如果你指责调酒师卖的是“成人礼啤酒”，你会得到两种截然不同的反应。大约一半的人会一脸茫然地看着你，完全不知道你在说什么。在这种情况下，你的调酒师可能只是个大学生，在会议上打工赚点零花钱。但另一半人会翻个白眼说：“是啊，别提了……这啤酒可不是我选的。” 这才是真正懂行的调酒师。

As my bartender rolled her eyes, I said to her, “I’m always looking for a low-sediment hop in a skunked mash, high final gravity with long head retention. Last event I went to they had a few bottles of Tactical Nuclear Penguin. Probably the last few bottles on earth.”

我的调酒师翻了个白眼，我对她说：“我一直在寻找那种沉淀少、麦芽汁浓稠、最终比重高、泡沫持久的啤酒花。我上次参加的活动上，他们有几瓶战术核企鹅啤酒花。可能是地球上仅存的几瓶了。”

“No way!” The bartender’s pupils dilated.

“不可能！”酒保的瞳孔放大了。

Tactical Nuclear Penguin, or TNP, sounds like a joke, but it’s one of the top ten beverage brands in the world and a holy grail of the beverage industry—in other words, the rarest and hardest-to-find beer on the planet and completely unforgettable by name and reputation. At 64 proof, TNP is the strongest beer ever made, and just 500 bottles were produced in 2009. Today, each bottle goes for more than $1,000 on the black market.

战术核企鹅（Tactical Nuclear Penguin，简称TNP）听起来像个玩笑，但它却是世界十大饮料品牌之一，也是饮料行业的圣杯——换句话说，它是地球上最稀有、最难找到的啤酒，其名字和名声都令人过目难忘。TNP的酒精度高达64度，是史上最烈的啤酒，2009年仅生产了500瓶。如今，每瓶在黑市上的价格都超过1000美元。

Now the bartender’s eyes were locked with mine. “How was it?” she asked.

这时，酒保的目光与我的目光交汇。“感觉怎么样？”她问道。

“Truthfully,” I replied, “it tastes like shit. But that’s not the point. I had to honor the fact they even had it!” Then I asked conspiratorially, “Hey, you’re not holding one back there are you?”

“说实话，”我回答道，“这玩意儿真难吃。但这不重要。我得承认他们居然有这东西！”然后我故作神秘地问道：“嘿，你没藏着掖着吧？”

There was a moment of silence in which the bartender looked at me in a new way—then she broke into a laugh almost as if I really existed to her now for the first time. She leaned in toward me, as if to reveal a new conspiracy. I had achieved Status Alignment with a Los Angeles bartender at a busy event, an almost impossible task under any conditions.

一阵沉默之后，酒保用一种全新的眼神看着我——然后她突然笑了起来，仿佛我此刻才真正出现在她的视野里。她向我靠近，仿佛要揭露什么新的秘密。我竟然在洛杉矶一场繁忙的活动中，和一位酒保达成了“身份认同”，这在任何情况下都几乎是不可能完成的任务。

“I’ll tell you what,” she whispered. “I’ve got something for you in the kitchen, be right back.”

“我告诉你，”她低声说，“我在厨房给你准备了点东西，马上回来。”

A minute later I had in my hands a bottle of Founders Breakfast Stout, a truly fantastic drink, just as my new friends pulled me away toward an alcove where a group was gathering.

一分钟后，我手里拿着一瓶 Founders Breakfast Stout，这真是一款非常棒的饮料，这时我的新朋友们拉着我走向一个壁龛，那里有一群人正在聚集。

We sat on some logs on the grass in a mini-amphitheater as a guitarist took the stage to play with a small celebrity trio. This guy was artful. He pulled off the most insane crosspick I’d ever heard—which is the fine art of using a tortoiseshell pick to create a distinctive and beautiful cascading musical effect. He down-picked from the bottom string, ascended, playing three notes at a time, and then immediately up-picked. I had to admit, the guy was beyond good. But what I was really focused on was what he was wearing: a Rush T-shirt. There was no doubt: I had found my Guitar Hero and his name was John King.

我们坐在小型露天剧场草地上的几根圆木上，一位吉他手登台与一个小型明星三重奏乐队合作演出。这家伙技艺精湛。他使出了我听过最疯狂的交叉拨弦——这是一种用玳瑁拨片创造出独特而优美的层叠音效的艺术。他从最下面的弦向下拨弦，然后向上拨弦，一次弹奏三个音符，接着立即向上拨弦。我不得不承认，这家伙的水平简直超乎想象。但我真正关注的却是他穿的衣服：一件Rush乐队的T恤。毫无疑问：我找到了我的吉他英雄，他的名字叫约翰·金。

THE SCIENCE OF THE STATUS TIP-OFF

身份泄露的科学

If you were a gorilla, there would be only one way for you to achieve Status Alignment with a fellow member of your species. You would have to be roughly the same size and age and physical condition. That’s because in the old dominance hierarchy your position was determined entirely by who could physically dominate who.

如果你是一只大猩猩，想要与同类达到地位一致，只有一种方法：你们的体型、年龄和身体状况必须大致相同。这是因为在旧有的等级制度中，地位完全取决于谁能在体能上压制谁。

The new dominance hierarchy doesn’t work this way. Humans respond to status indicators so small they are nearly imperceptible to outsiders. In fact, we quickly and easily respond to invisible status indicators that are entirely verbal, like “I’m agent Smith, LAPD.” Those four words will make you pay attention quickly.

新的等级制度并非如此运作。人类会对一些细微的地位信号做出反应，这些信号对于局外人来说几乎难以察觉。事实上，我们能够迅速而轻易地对完全由语言表达的无形地位信号做出反应，比如“我是洛杉矶警局的史密斯探员”。这四个字就能让你立刻注意到对方。

After noticing this phenomenon, I’ve spent years investigating it with my private research team, and we have discovered the most efficient way to achieve Status Alignment at the start of any conversation or negotiation with any other person. I’ve gradually honed this approach, using it in many large deals across various industries. It works perfectly every time when you follow a specific pattern using a three-sentence phrase called a Status Tip-Off.

注意到这种现象后，我和我的私人研究团队花了数年时间进行研究，最终发现了一种在与任何人的对话或谈判开始时实现地位一致性的最有效方法。我不断完善这种方法，并将其应用于各个行业的许多大型交易中。只要遵循特定的模式，使用一个叫做“地位提示”的三句话短语，它就能每次都完美奏效。

Think about high-stakes situations in movies—for example, a first meeting between two spies in Moscow’s Red Square, exchanging stolen missile blueprints. One spy will ask a question of the other that nobody else could possibly know the answer to—for example, “Do you know the way to the Blind Monk Tavern?” when no such tavern exists. The right answer is like a password.

想想电影里那些高风险的场景——比如，两名间谍在莫斯科红场初次会面，交换窃取的导弹蓝图。其中一名间谍会问另一名间谍一个只有他自己知道答案的问题——例如，“你知道盲僧酒馆怎么走吗？”而实际上根本没有这家酒馆。正确的答案就像一个密码。

The same strategy is also used in body-swap stories in TV or film, when characters become trapped in completely unrecognizable bodies. For instance, in the original Star Trek series, episode 24, Dr. Janice Lester, who was once Kirk’s lover, traps the captain into a life-entity transfer, allowing her to take over his body and leave him trapped in her body. Janice (in Kirk’s body) becomes captain of the ship, leaving Kirk (in Janice’s body) locked in sick bay trying to convince Spock that he’s actually Kirk. What does he say to prove to Spock that he is the real Kirk?

同样的策略也常用于影视作品中的灵魂互换故事，让角色陷入完全陌生的身体中。例如，在初代《星际迷航》第24集中，柯克的前情人詹妮丝·莱斯特医生利用生命体转移陷阱控制了舰长，使她得以占据他的身体，并将他困在自己的身体里。詹妮丝（占据了柯克的身体）成为了舰长，而柯克（占据了詹妮丝的身体）则被关在医务室里，试图说服斯波克他才是真正的柯克。他究竟说了些什么来向斯波克证明自己才是真正的柯克呢？

“Spock,” he says, “when I was caught in the interspace of the Tholian sector, you risked your life and the Enterprise to get me back. That’s when the Vians of Minara demanded that we let Bones die,” if you remember. This line is a Tip-Off. When Spock hears it, he immediately realizes that this is the real Kirk. This Tip-Off—like the directions to the Blind Monk Tavern—functions just like a police officer’s badge, a firefighter’s uniform, a doctor’s stethoscope, or a gangster’s distinctive tattoos. If you’re a leader in that group, you can recognize another leader immediately. And you’ll listen to them, trust them, and choose to work with them over someone who is not in your group.

“斯波克，”他说，“我被困在索利安星区的星际空间时，你冒着生命危险，甚至牺牲了企业号才把我救回来。当时米纳拉的维安人要求我们让博恩斯死掉，”如果你还记得的话。这句话是个线索。斯波克听到后，立刻意识到眼前这个人就是真正的柯克。这个线索——就像盲僧酒馆的路线指引一样——就像警徽、消防员制服、医生听诊器或黑帮分子的标志性纹身一样。如果你是某个群体中的领导者，你就能立刻认出另一个领导者。你会听从他们的意见，信任他们，并选择与他们合作，而不是与圈外人合作。

In the early days of the Italian Mafia, bosses in the Mazzarella clan in Naples wore distinctive rings in the shape of a lion’s head. They were ruthless and universally feared, and so when you saw a lion’s head ring coming your way, it was best to step aside. Mafia informer Nicola Cangiano once told prosecutors how to identify members of the Sagaria clan: “They all wear Samsonite shoes and cashmere socks.” Best to stay out of their way, too.

在意大利黑手党早期，那不勒斯马扎雷拉家族的头目们都佩戴着狮头形状的独特戒指。他们冷酷无情，令人闻风丧胆，所以如果你看到有人戴着狮头戒指朝你走来，最好赶紧躲开。黑手党线人尼古拉·坎贾诺曾告诉检察官如何辨认萨加里亚家族的成员：“他们都穿着新秀丽皮鞋和羊绒袜。” 最好也离他们远点。

Most of us don’t have a secret code or distinctive outfit to signal to others whether they should approach or stay clear. But we can easily use verbal tip-offs. Whether you’re a barista or an account executive at a bank, you have a certain domain of expertise that won’t mean a thing to outsiders but that insiders will understand immediately. It’s easy to think of a statement that would allow someone else to assess whether you’re in their group and at their level. These are Status Tip-Offs, or pieces of information that, in the eyes of others in the know, immediately cement your status as an in-group member. A Status Tip-Off is like a password muttered through a slit in the door that signals you are OK to be let inside.

我们大多数人没有秘密暗号或独特的着装来向他人发出是否应该靠近或远离的信号。但我们可以轻松地利用口头暗示。无论你是咖啡师还是银行的客户经理，你都拥有某种专业知识，这些知识对于局外人来说毫无意义，但内部人士却能立刻明白。很容易就能想到一些话，让别人判断你是否属于他们的圈子，是否与他们级别相当。这些就是身份暗示，或者说，在知情者眼中，这些信息能立即巩固你作为圈内成员的地位。身份暗示就像从门缝里低声说出的密码，表明你可以进去了。

When you bump into someone who grew up in your hometown, they don’t need to say much for you to feel an instant sense of connection. “Remember when Eskimo Joe’s burned down back in ’97?” is usually enough for you to be fully convinced that the two of you have tons in common.

当你偶遇一个和你家乡同乡时，他们无需多言，你就能立刻感受到一种亲切感。“还记得1997年爱斯基摩乔餐厅被烧毁的事吗？”这句话通常就足以让你确信，你们俩有很多共同点。

But keep in mind that if all you have in common is Eskimo Joes or that you both are fans of the Dallas Cowboys or have visited the same small town in Switzerland, you may have a pleasant connection but you do not have the kind of alignment you need to do a business deal.

但请记住，如果你们的共同点仅仅是都喜欢 Eskimo Joes 啤酒，或者都是达拉斯牛仔队的球迷，或者都去过瑞士同一个小镇，那么你们可能会有愉快的交往，但你们并不具备达成商业交易所需的契合度。

In business, you need a specific type of Status Tip-Off, one that reveals a certain series of ideas that could only be known by an in-group member. Once you have the right Tip-Off, the right doors will open for you. The best way to find a Status Tip-Off is to interview three people who are the same level as the person you are trying to influence. What would they say to each other, to catch up on each other’s business, peer-to-peer?

在商业领域，你需要一种特定的“身份信息”，它能揭示只有内部成员才知道的一系列想法。一旦你掌握了正确的信息，机会之门就会为你敞开。寻找这种“身份信息”的最佳方法是采访三位与你想要影响的人级别相同的人。他们会如何以同级的方式交流彼此的业务近况呢？

Memorize your Tip-Off and find an opportunity to deliver it to a decision maker. Then sit back and watch doors start to spring open for you—because you will have just separated yourself from all the other people trying to get this person’s attention. When this is complete, you will be in ideal Status Alignment with your target, ready to take the next step toward Inception.

记住你的关键信息，并找到机会将其传递给决策者。然后，你就可以坐等机会之门为你敞开——因为你已经从所有试图引起此人注意的人中脱颖而出。完成这一步后，你将与目标人物达到理想的地位契合，准备好迈出下一步，进入项目启动阶段。

Over the years my team and I have learned to use the three key elements that make up a successful Tip-Off:

多年来，我和我的团队学会了如何运用构成成功开球仪式的三个关键要素：

  1. Use Specific Industry Lingo
    使用行业专业术语
  2. Describe a Recent Action You Have Taken
    描述一下你最近采取的一项行动
  3. Mention a Real Situation Everyone in the Industry Cares About
    举一个业内人士都非常关心的真实案例

Back in North Beverly Hills, watching the man in the Rush T-shirt cross-picking with his tortoiseshell, I was in deep thought as I pondered how to deliver the right Status Tip-Off to John King.

回到北比佛利山庄，看着那个穿着 Rush T 恤的男人用他的玳瑁琴进行交叉拨弦，我陷入了沉思，思考着如何向约翰·金提供正确的身份提示。

A STATUS TIP-OFF WORTH $25 MILLION

价值2500万美元的身份泄露

I had my target in sight, but while he strummed onstage in front of dozens of adoring listeners, he was clearly unapproachable. I settled in and tried to have a pleasant evening among the wealthy elite; I had no choice in the matter.

我的目标已经锁定，但他在台上弹奏着吉他，台下有几十位崇拜他的听众，他却明显难以接近。我别无选择，只能安顿下来，试图在这些富裕精英中度过一个愉快的夜晚。

At the end of the music set, row after row of admirers and attendees descended upon John and the other celebrity musicians. In this “feel-good moment,” common sense told me there was a near-zero chance of getting John’s attention to talk about a business deal.

演出结束后，一排排的仰慕者和观众涌向约翰和其他明星音乐家。在这“欢乐时刻”，我的直觉告诉我，几乎不可能引起约翰的注意，和他谈生意。

But I was confident that I had the one thing that will get anybody’s attention in any situation: the Status Tip-Off.

但我很自信，我拥有在任何情况下都能引起任何人注意的一件事：身份提示。

Earlier in the day I’d gotten into Status Alignment with the valet and then the bartender, but it was going to be a big step-up to do the same with the elusive billionaire. I still knew my deal was something he’d want to invest in, but I also knew now was clearly not the time to go into details. If I started telling him all about the deal without first aligning myself as an equal, he’d categorize me as an annoying outsider and I would never get his full attention again. So as the crowd thinned, I stood off to the side talking to another guest. Finally, it was time. John was practically alone. As he leaned down to pack up his instrument, I knew I wouldn’t get a better chance than this to introduce the deal.

当天早些时候，我成功地与代客泊车员和调酒师建立了地位上的平等关系，但要与那位行踪飘忽的亿万富翁达成同样的目标，难度可想而知。我仍然相信他会对我的方案感兴趣，但我也清楚现在显然不是详述细节的时候。如果我没有先建立起平等的关系就贸然向他介绍方案，他只会把我当成一个令人讨厌的外人，以后就再也无法引起他的全部注意力了。于是，趁着人群渐渐散去，我走到一旁，和另一位客人聊了起来。终于，时机成熟了。约翰几乎独自一人。当他弯腰收拾乐器时，我知道这是我介绍方案的最佳时机。

“Hey, John King, right?” I said casually, keeping my hands at my side. “Don’t think we’ve formally met but I helped you guys close the ski mountain deal for Altitude.” That gave us something in common, and a reason for John to pay attention for another few seconds.

“嘿，你是约翰·金，对吧？”我漫不经心地说道，双手垂在身侧。“我们好像还没正式见过面，不过我帮你们敲定了Altitude滑雪场的交易。”这让我们有了共同话题，也让约翰多听了我几秒钟。

Now I was set up to use the Status Tip-Off formula. First, I would have to use industry-specific lingo. Second, I needed to discuss a respected action I was taking within the industry. Third, I needed to refer to an open issue everyone in the industry was talking about.

现在我已经准备好使用“状态预警”公式了。首先，我需要使用行业术语。其次，我需要讨论我在业内正在采取的一项受人尊敬的行动。第三，我需要提及业内人士都在讨论的一个公开议题。

“I’m betting that Grid Connected Micro Inverters are the next billion-dollar market. Anyway, that’s why I helped State Bill 350 get through the senate, to get rid of the caps on meter credits. I think it will be good for all of us when waiver on Assembly Bill 802 gets through in September. . . . Money is going to start pouring into the market.”

“我敢打赌，并网微型逆变器将成为下一个十亿美元市场。总之，这就是我帮助州参议院通过第350号法案的原因，该法案旨在取消电表补贴上限。我认为，如果众议院第802号法案的豁免条款在9月份获得通过，对我们所有人都有好处……资金将会大量涌入市场。”

John looked up. Those 68 words had snagged his interest.

约翰抬起头。那68个字引起了他的注意。

“I’m headed to Arizona tomorrow to lock-up a new solar deal,” I continued. “You probably saw the presentation already? Not as exciting as buying a whole mountain but pretty good for the investors, it pays a 12 percent coupon during the first twelve months. Anyway, maybe we can chat sometime.”

“我明天要去亚利桑那州敲定一项新的太阳能交易，”我继续说道。“你可能已经看过演示文稿了吧？虽然不如买下一座山那么令人兴奋，但对投资者来说相当不错，前十二个月的票息高达12%。总之，也许我们可以找个时间聊聊。”

I chose those words carefully, so John could see we were at the same level of status, authority, and power. People in the same position of the dominance hierarchy are drawn to each other magnetically.

我斟酌用词，是为了让约翰明白我们地位、权威和权力相当。处于同一支配等级的人之间，会像磁铁一样相互吸引。

“Wait,” John said, “I didn’t catch your name.”

“等等，”约翰说，“我还没问你叫什么名字呢。”

Bingo. That was the sign the Status Tip-Off had worked. John turned toward me with new interest and alertness, our status now perfect in alignment.

没错。这说明身份提示奏效了。约翰转过头来，神情专注而专注，我们之间的关系现在完全吻合了。

“Oren Klaff,” I replied. “Aren’t you on the board here? We probably know ten people in common. Anyway, good to meet in person.”

“奥伦·克拉夫，”我回答道。“你不是董事会成员吗？我们大概认识十个共同的人。总之，很高兴见到你本人。”

“Yes,” he said, sounding unsure but interested. “Your name does sound familiar. What’s this solar deal?”

“是的，”他说道，语气有些犹豫，但又很感兴趣。“你的名字听起来很耳熟。这个太阳能项目是怎么回事？”

Boom. Deal junkies always want to know what their peers are working on and hate missing out. I paused and looked at him carefully. Most salespeople would have taken this as an invitation to pitch their whole deal, uncomfortably trapping their prospect in an awkward social situation for twenty minutes or more. But I knew his question only meant one thing: “I’m a little busy right now, so I’ll give you a few seconds to show me you’re someone worth taking a call with.” John and I shared some contact information—and he later that week invested big in my solar deal.

砰！那些热衷于交易的人总是想知道同行们在忙些什么，而且最怕错过机会。我停顿了一下，仔细地打量着他。大多数销售人员会把这当成推销整个项目的邀请，让潜在客户尴尬地陷入长达二十分钟甚至更久的社交困境。但我知道他的问题只有一个意思：“我现在有点忙，所以给你几秒钟时间，让我看看你是不是值得我接听电话的人。”我和约翰交换了联系方式——就在那周晚些时候，他为我的太阳能项目投入了一大笔资金。

Everything was stacked against me that day, but I was able to get the full attention of my last-ditch investor because I worked hard delivering a compelling Status Tip-Off, and securing Status Alignment.
