One example of this today is with self-driving cars.

如今的一个例子就是自动驾驶汽车。

For the first time in history, we are seeing the commercial release of the fully autonomous drive-you-anywhere-you-want-to-go car. General Motors makes one, and Ford and Tesla do too. So do Toyota, Nissan, Porsche, and Mercedes, and even Kia will have one soon. Let’s assume the cars work like any other, except the one I’m suggesting you buy has no steering wheel you can turn, no brakes you can push, no turn signals or any other controls. The only thing you can touch is the radio knob. So now let me ask—when are you going to buy one?

历史上首次，我们见证了全自动驾驶汽车的商业化上市。通用汽车、福特和特斯拉都在生产这种车。丰田、日产、保时捷和奔驰也都在生产，甚至起亚也即将推出。假设这些车的工作原理与其他汽车一样，只不过我建议你买的这辆车没有方向盘可以转动，没有刹车可以踩，没有转向灯或其他任何控制装置。你唯一能碰的就是收音机旋钮。那么现在我想问问——你打算什么时候买一辆？

Your answer to this question will tell me what risks you’re willing to take in life. If your reply is, “Did you say no steering wheel or brakes? No way, I’m not buying that until hell freezes over,” then you are probably a late adopter, an average consumer who buys around the same time everyone else does. You got an iPhone when the hundredth person in a week pulled one out to show you what they had for breakfast.

你对这个问题的回答将告诉我你愿意在生活中承担多大的风险。如果你回答说：“你说没有方向盘和刹车？不可能，除非太阳从西边出来，否则我绝不买。”那么你很可能是一个后知后觉的人，一个和其他人差不多时间购买产品的普通消费者。比如，你买iPhone的时候，一周内已经是第一百个人掏出iPhone给你看他们早餐吃了什么。

Maybe your answer is “I have to have the very first self-driving car available.” There aren’t a lot of you guys out there, because you people are the crazy ones Jobs was talking about. The crazy ones pursue new technology products aggressively and buy the moment they hear “We have two available—want one?”

也许你的答案是“我必须拥有第一辆自动驾驶汽车。” 像你这样的人不多，因为你们正是乔布斯所说的“疯子”。这些“疯子”会疯狂追逐新技术产品，一听到“我们有两辆现车——要不要一辆？”就立马下单。

But this early versus late adopter market segmentation concept falls apart when the stakes go up. Time and time again my team has found that the bigger and more important a decision is, the more likely it is to be made based on conservative criteria. When lives are at stake, jobs are on the line, and the company has to meet its goals to pay the bills, new and exciting ideas will almost always be considered but passed up. Ask someone who is into driverless cars what they think about fully automated surgeon-less heart surgery. Oh, they’ll be interested to hear about it, and they’ll approach, but when it’s time to commit, the avoidance behavior is going to win out.

但这种早期采用者与后期采用者市场细分的概念，在风险增大时便不再适用。我的团队一次又一次地发现，决策越重大、越重要，就越有可能基于保守的标准来做出。当生命攸关、工作岌岌可危、公司必须完成目标才能维持运营时，那些新颖而令人兴奋的想法几乎总是会被考虑，但最终却会被放弃。问问那些对无人驾驶汽车感兴趣的人，他们对全自动、无需外科医生的心脏手术有何看法。哦，他们会很感兴趣，也会主动了解，但到了真正需要做出决定的时候，回避心理就会占据上风。

This leaves us with a problem. The best method to get people to listen and pay attention to our ideas is to make what we are saying seem new and exciting. But doing so can trigger anxiety and avoidance, and they won’t be likely to take action when it counts later on. On the other end of the spectrum, if we make our message seem normal and nonthreatening from the beginning, it’s possible nobody will listen to it.

这就给我们带来了一个难题。让人们倾听并关注我们的想法的最佳方法是让我们的言论显得新颖有趣。但这样做可能会引发焦虑和回避，导致他们在关键时刻不太可能采取行动。另一方面，如果我们从一开始就把信息说得平淡无奇、毫无威胁，那可能根本就没人会听。

Where’s the balance?

平衡点在哪里？

The trick is to use a technique called Novelty Chunking to make it seem like your deal is different from “normal” in just one key way, while everything else about the deal is completely Plain Vanilla. Then you show the buyer that what’s normal is shifting, and the one key, different thing is really popular today. There is a new normal .

诀窍在于运用一种叫做“新颖点块”的技巧，让你的交易看起来只在某一关键方面与“常规”有所不同，而其他方面则完全平淡无奇。这样，你就能向买家展示，所谓的“常规”正在发生变化，而这关键的、与众不同的一点如今却非常流行。新的常态已经出现。

Unfortunately, I hadn’t yet discovered this foolproof formula when I got stuck staring down the Kobayashi Maru that was Mahalo Marketplace.

不幸的是，当我被困在 Mahalo Marketplace 那艘像小林丸号一样的庞然大物中时，我还没有发现这个万无一失的办法。

A NOVEL IDEA ON MAHALO

关于“MAHALO”的一个新颖想法

Two weeks had passed since Logan signed us up for the suicide mission of selling Mahalo for $50 million. I started sleeping at my desk. I was eating there too. The workload and stress were taking a toll on my health.

自从洛根让我们执行以五千万美元出售马哈洛公司的自杀式任务以来，已经过去了两个星期。我开始在办公桌上睡觉，甚至在那里吃饭。工作量和压力严重损害了我的健康。

Our entire plan for selling Mahalo centered on a single man: Mitch Preston, a prominent real estate investor in Hawaii who basically had a hand in every large real estate deal being done at the time. Mitch was so respected in the market, I knew other investors would follow his lead if I could get him to buy into Mahalo.

我们出售Mahalo的整个计划都围绕着一个人：米奇·普雷斯顿，他是夏威夷一位声名显赫的房地产投资者，当时几乎所有的大型房地产交易都有他的参与。米奇在市场上备受尊敬，我知道如果我能让他入股Mahalo，其他投资者也会效仿。

But after running my research on this deal and glancing through the specifications of Mitch’s most recent investments, I knew exactly what his reaction was going to be: “Yes, it’s super profitable, but it’s just too different. ” He had a formula that was making him a lot of money. Like all good investors, he would want to stick with what he knew. Mitch’s formula was pretty simple: He ran a portfolio of large commercial properties; he held on to buildings for a few years, slowly found creative ways to raise rents, then sold at a profit.

但在我研究了这笔交易并浏览了米奇最近几笔投资的具体情况后，我立刻就知道他的反应会是什么：“没错，这笔投资利润丰厚，但跟我以前做的完全不一样。”他有一套让他赚得盆满钵满的秘诀。像所有优秀的投资者一样，他肯定会坚持自己熟悉的领域。米奇的秘诀很简单：他管理着一系列大型商业地产；他持有这些房产几年，慢慢地想办法提高租金，然后卖掉获利。

With the clock ticking, we didn’t have many choices of serious people at Mitch’s level. If he said no, we would have blown our best shot at getting the deal on track.

时间紧迫，像米奇这样有能力的人选并不多。如果他拒绝，我们就错失了促成这笔交易的最佳机会。

The fastest way to get Mitch to buy into my deal was to convince him that Mahalo was just like the other properties in his portfolio at the time—that his standard formula would work perfectly on this one. But the more closely I looked at Mahalo, the more problems began to emerge. No way around the facts; this place was nothing like his other properties!

让米奇接受我的交易最快的方法就是说服他，马哈洛和他当时投资组合里的其他房产没什么两样——他惯用的套路对这栋楼也完全适用。但我越是仔细研究马哈洛，问题就越多。事实摆在眼前：这栋楼和他其他的房产完全不一样！

Here was the cold hard reality:

这就是残酷的现实：

  1. We had sixty-eight tenants, almost none of whom had good credit, and they were all on short-term, one-year leases instead of more desirable ten-year leases of the kind you might get from Starbucks.
    我们有 68 位租户，几乎没有一个信用良好，而且他们签订的都是短期一年租约，而不是像星巴克那样更理想的十年租约。
  2. Many tenants were small vendors taking up less than 250 square feet.
    许多租户都是面积不足 250 平方英尺的小商贩。
  3. Tenants did business mostly in cash, which invites IRS auditors to stick their noses in everything.
    租户们大多用现金交易，这很容易引起美国国税局审计人员的注意。
  4. The property wasn’t much to look at and lacked what developers call “curb appeal.”
    这处房产外观并不出众，缺乏开发商所说的“街景吸引力”。
  5. These vendors sold food that was so fresh, a lot of it was still moving when they handed it to you. Nothing was frozen, packaged, or processed.
    这些摊贩卖的食物非常新鲜，很多食物递给你的时候还在动。没有冷冻的、包装的或加工过的。

So what we had was not ideal, and it didn’t fit what investors were normally looking for.

所以，我们当时的情况并不理想，也不符合投资者通常的需求。

It was time to hit the phones and start some additional research. I was making call after call, searching desperately for a way to highlight Mahalo as the new normal.

是时候拿起电话，开始进一步的调查了。我一个接一个地打电话，拼命寻找能够凸显“Mahalo”这一新常态的方法。

“Hey, Chad,” I would say when I got a real estate analyst on the phone. “Just wanted to see what the latest trends are that you’re seeing in large commercial real estate deals. What have you come across lately?”

“嘿，查德，”我打电话给房地产分析师时会这样说，“我想了解一下你最近在大型商业地产交易方面观察到的最新趋势。你最近都遇到了些什么？”

“Beverly, quick question,” I said to a leading real estate broker. “If you had to guess, what would you say the next ten big deals will look like in the market?”

“贝弗利，问你个问题，”我对一位资深房地产经纪人说，“如果你要你猜测，你认为接下来市场上的十笔大交易会是什么样的？”

“Brett, my main man, what’s new in your market right now?”

“布雷特，我的好兄弟，你们市场现在有什么新鲜事吗？”

I jotted any interesting responses down on Post-it notes and whiteboards. The key would be to find a trend that I could use to put this new deal in context. Meanwhile, Logan hired a couple of analysts named Jon and Mike, and I had them reading through mountains of paperwork on other big real estate deals currently on the market around the world.

我把所有有趣的回复都记在便利贴和白板上。关键在于找到一个可以用来解读这笔新交易的趋势。与此同时，洛根聘请了两位名叫乔恩和迈克的分析师，我让他们仔细阅读了堆积如山的关于世界各地其他大型房地产交易的文件。

We kept asking the same two questions: What parts of our deal would attract Mitch and what parts would push him away? In other words, “How is this deal the same as Mitch’s other deals?” and “How is this deal very different and unique?” The plan was to find the perfect way to explain Mahalo as the new normal.

我们反复问自己两个问题：我们协议中的哪些部分会吸引米奇，哪些部分会让他望而却步？换句话说，“这项协议与米奇之前的交易有何相同之处？”以及“这项协议有何独特之处？”我们的计划是找到一种完美的方式来阐释Mahalo，使其成为新的常态。

But as the days ticked by and the meeting drew closer Jon and Mike grew increasingly agitated. “This is a waste of time!” Mike exploded at me with about twenty hours left until the meeting. “We need to be writing the offering memorandum, not looking for a needle in a haystack with all this psychological BS.”

但随着时间推移，会议临近，乔恩和迈克变得越来越焦躁不安。“这简直是浪费时间！”距离会议还有大约二十个小时时，迈克冲我吼道，“我们应该抓紧时间撰写招股说明书，而不是在一堆心理学废话里大海捞针。”

“Yeah,” Jon chimed in. “This is a joke. We’ve spent the last week reading about all-glass malls and malls with luxury apartments in them and Disney malls and that insane mall in Dubai with a ski slope in it. We should have been focusing on the mall we’re actually trying to sell.”

“是啊，”乔恩插嘴道，“这简直是个笑话。过去一周我们都在看关于全玻璃幕墙购物中心、带豪华公寓的购物中心、迪士尼购物中心，还有迪拜那个带滑雪场的疯狂购物中心的文章。我们应该把精力放在我们真正想卖的那个购物中心上才对。”

“OK,” I said, nodding. “You guys are right. Why don’t you both get a few hours of sleep while I look over all of this once more? Then we’ll throw the proposal together in the morning.” They agreed and left the room in a huff.

“好吧，”我点点头说，“你们说得对。不如你们俩先睡几个小时，我再把这些都过一遍。明天早上我们再把提案整理出来。”他们同意了，然后气呼呼地离开了房间。

I sighed. As much as I hated to admit it, Jon and Mike had a point. We had wasted a ton of time researching other deals and now had no time left to create our pitch deck. To make matters worse, we hadn’t uncovered any brilliant insights during the research that we could use to get Mitch on board. None of the lucrative malls of the past few years looked anything like Mahalo.

我叹了口气。虽然我很不情愿承认，但乔恩和迈克说得有道理。我们浪费了大量时间研究其他项目，现在根本没时间制作我们的推介材料了。更糟糕的是，我们在研究过程中并没有发现任何能说服米奇加入的独到见解。过去几年里那些利润丰厚的购物中心，没有一个跟马哈洛购物中心很像。

My knees ached and I had to slide into a nearby chair. My breaths came quick and shallow. For the first time ever I had genuinely gotten myself in too deep. Or Logan had. I wasn’t even sure whose fault it was anymore. And now I was just hours away from completely embarrassing myself, sinking our firm while broadcasting to the banking community that we couldn’t close deals or meet commitments on time.

我膝盖酸痛，只好滑到旁边的椅子上坐下。呼吸急促而浅短。有生以来，我第一次真的陷得太深了。或许是洛根陷得太深了。我甚至不确定这到底是谁的错。而现在，我离彻底出丑只差几个小时了，我不仅会拖垮公司，还会让整个银行界都知道我们无法按时完成交易或履行承诺。

Jon’s and Mike’s words echoed in my head.

乔恩和迈克的话语在我脑海中回荡。

“Waste of time.”

“浪费时间。”

“Needle in a haystack.”

“大海捞针。”

“This is a joke.”

“这简直是个笑话。”

And for some reason, I kept thinking about the last thing Jon had said: “. . . all-glass malls and malls with luxury apartments in them and . . . a ski slope.”

不知为何，我一直想着乔恩最后说的话：“……全玻璃结构的购物中心，里面有豪华公寓的购物中心，还有……滑雪场。”

Wait a minute. A number of the large deals on the market at the time were malls with some type of big differentiator. These weren’t your regular malls; they all had something to set them apart. Malls with a theme . I looked up that mall in Dubai, and implausibly it did have its very own ski slope. It’s called Mall of the Emirates, and it has a hundred restaurants and eighty luxury stores, and is home to Ski Dubai, the Middle East’s first indoor snow park. It had recently been named the World’s Leading Shopping Mall at the World Travel Awards. And it was profitable too. Investors had put $218 million into it and were taking a lot more out.

等等。当时市场上很多大型交易都是一些具有独特卖点的购物中心。这些可不是普通的购物中心；它们都有各自的特色。这些购物中心都有自己的主题。我查了一下迪拜的那个购物中心，难以置信的是，它竟然拥有自己的滑雪场。它叫阿联酋购物中心（Mall of the Emirates），拥有上百家餐厅和八十家奢侈品商店，也是中东首个室内滑雪场——迪拜滑雪场（Ski Dubai）的所在地。它最近在世界旅游大奖中被评为“世界领先购物中心”。而且它还盈利颇丰。投资者已经投入了2.18亿美元，并且还在不断套现。

I shot to my feet and started rifling through a stack of papers on my desk, pulling files that fit with this potential theme. There was a mall under construction in Thousand Oaks, California, that the developers were calling a village—which just meant that they had built some residences in addition to the shops. There was the mall Jon had mentioned, Westfield Century City, which had the same shops as a normal mall but had an outdoor bazaar look and feel. There was a mall that just sold in Canada where the theme was pirates, and there was even a large pool in the center with a giant pirate ship in it.

我猛地站起身，开始翻阅桌上的一叠文件，找出与这个潜在主题相符的资料。加州千橡市正在兴建一个购物中心，开发商称之为“村庄”——其实就是除了商店之外，他们还建了一些住宅。还有乔恩提到的那个购物中心，韦斯特菲尔德世纪城，它和普通购物中心一样，但整体风格更像一个露天集市。加拿大最近也卖掉了一个以海盗为主题的购物中心，中心甚至还有一个大型游泳池，里面停泊着一艘巨大的海盗船。

All big deals, all malls with a theme.

所有大型活动，所有主题商场。

This was exactly what would make Mahalo work. I could easily show Mitch that this property was themed as an authentic Chinese open-air market. I could chunk the many novel features surrounding Mahalo as belonging within this same category. Then I could suggest that this was the new normal for shopping centers. Many of the big malls on the market today are themed as well.

这正是Mahalo项目成功的关键所在。我可以轻易地向米奇证明，这个项目是以正宗的中国露天市场为主题的。我可以将Mahalo的诸多创新之处归入这一范畴。然后，我可以指出，这才是购物中心的新常态。如今市场上许多大型购物中心也都是主题式的。

If you’ve ever had the experience of seeing the answer you seek crystallize in front of you just in the nick of time, you know how I felt at this moment— ecstatic . I turned the song “Eye of the Tiger” on full blast and discoed around the office for about three minutes. Then I buckled down. I now had a few hours to actually write the pitch and get it ready to deliver to Mitch.

如果你也曾有过那种在千钧一发之际，苦苦寻觅的答案突然出现在眼前的感受，你就能明白我当时的心情——欣喜若狂。我把《虎眼》（Eye of the Tiger）的音量开到最大，在办公室里跳了大约三分钟的迪斯科。然后，我才开始认真起来。现在我只有几个小时的时间来撰写提案，并准备好交给米奇。

CHUNK THE NOVELTY INTO ONE CATEGORY

将新奇事物归为一类

Every buyer has a slightly different level of tolerance for risk, or what I call a novelty preference point. Once you push a buyer past this preference point, anxiety, stress, and a host of problems start to occur and he or she will begin to back off.

每个买家对风险的承受能力略有不同，或者我称之为“新奇偏好点”。一旦买家的接受程度超过这个偏好点，焦虑、压力以及一系列问题就会随之而来，他们就会开始退缩。

My team and I have found that the best way to introduce new features, sexy concepts, wild ideas, and forward thinking without going past the novelty preference point (so that it will appeal to virtually any buyer) is to use Novelty Chunking. As I’ve mentioned, this is the practice of grouping everything new and potentially scary about your deal into a single category and then telling the buyer that your deal is just like every other deal in your industry, except for one key aspect that’s totally new.

我和我的团队发现，在不超出买家对新奇事物的偏好范围（从而吸引几乎所有买家）的情况下，引入新功能、吸引眼球的概念、大胆的想法和前瞻性思维的最佳方法是使用“新奇分块”策略。正如我之前提到的，这种策略是将交易中所有新颖且可能令人担忧的元素归为一类，然后告诉买家，除了一个关键的全新方面之外，你的交易与行业内的其他交易并无二致。

The idea is to carefully control how new and risky your deal seems to the buyer, because buyers add up risks, almost like a point system. If you have many new and unproven features and ideas, then you have many risks. It’s as if it doesn’t matter how big the risk is; it matters how many risks there are. To control the way risk is perceived, create a list of all the novel or scary things about your idea. Then figure out some way all these items are related to each other. This becomes the “chunk” that you’ll use to explain how your idea is different in one key way from the status quo.

关键在于谨慎控制买家对你的项目的新颖性和风险感知，因为买家会像积分制一样累积风险。如果你有很多新颖且未经验证的功能和想法，那么风险自然就很多。似乎风险的大小并不重要，重要的是风险的数量。为了控制风险的感知方式，列出你的想法中所有新颖或令人担忧之处。然后，找出这些要素之间的关联。这便构成了你用来解释你的想法与现状在关键方面有何不同的核心论点。

For instance, Microsoft Word is by far the most widely used word processing program today. In fact, one of the top ten phrases used in business is “I sent you the Word doc.” It’s hard to get more Plain Vanilla than that. But let’s say you were trying to get someone to switch from Word to a newer word processor, like Google Docs.

例如，微软 Word 是目前使用最广泛的文字处理程序。事实上，商务场合最常用的十大短语之一就是“我把 Word 文档发给你了”。这简直再简单不过了。但假设你想让别人从 Word 切换到更新的文字处理软件，比如 Google Docs。

There are plenty of things about Google Docs that are different from Word. It is accessed through a web browser; you don’t download it or start it up . Documents are saved to your Google account, not your hard drive. In Google Docs, multiple people can be working on the same document at the same time, a feature Word does not support very easily. But Google Docs didn’t become popular because Google promoted these and seventeen other new things about it. Instead they built buzz on just one: Everyone works in one document; see changes immediately.

Google Docs 与 Word 有许多不同之处。它通过网页浏览器访问，无需下载或启动。文档保存到您的 Google 帐户，而不是硬盘驱动器。在 Google Docs 中，多人可以同时编辑同一文档，而 Word 对此支持并不完善。但 Google Docs 的流行并非源于 Google 大力宣传这些以及其他十七项新功能，而是源于一项核心优势：所有人都可以在同一文档中协作，并立即看到更改。

So to write a Plain Vanilla script for Google Docs you would first focus on how similar it is to Microsoft Word. “Hey, look, Microsoft Word is fantastic. It’s the perfect desktop word processor, and I would never change a thing about it. The simple interface with the ruler and toolbar at the top of the screen makes word processing a breeze. Google Docs keeps everything that makes Word great. The text editor feels almost identical. You can save, edit, spell-check, word-count, comment, and even track changes.”

所以，要编写一个适用于 Google Docs 的 Plain Vanilla 脚本，首先要关注它与 Microsoft Word 的相似之处。“嘿，瞧，Microsoft Word 太棒了。它是完美的桌面文字处理器，我一点都不想改动它。屏幕顶部的标尺和工具栏让文字处理变得轻而易举。Google Docs 保留了 Word 的所有优点。文本编辑器几乎一模一样。你可以保存、编辑、拼写检查、字数统计、添加注释，甚至还能跟踪更改。”

Once you’ve established the many aspects of the product that haven’t changed, it’s a simple matter to introduce the Novelty Chunk: “But there is one key difference that sets Google Docs apart from Word. It is cloud based. This means the document lives in the cloud and multiple people can access it through a web browser from anywhere on the planet simultaneously.”

一旦你确定了产品中许多未改变的方面，引入新颖之处就变得很简单了：“但有一个关键区别使 Google Docs 与 Word 截然不同。它是基于云的。这意味着文档存储在云端，多人可以通过网络浏览器从地球上的任何地方同时访问它。”

In essence, you combine everything new about your idea into one Novelty Chunk. Then you explain to your buyer that the status quo is great and works just fine. Acknowledge that they probably aren’t looking for a replacement. Finally, introduce the one way your idea is novel and show why this novelty is good—and how it’s the same thing nearly everyone is doing (collaborating on projects in the cloud is the new normal).

本质上，你要把你的想法中所有新颖之处都整合到一个“新颖点”中。然后，你要向买家解释现状很好，运行良好。承认他们可能并不需要替代方案。最后，介绍你的想法中唯一新颖的地方，并说明这种新颖之处的优势——以及它与几乎所有人都在做的事情（在云端协作开发项目已成为新常态）之间的相似之处。

And that was exactly my plan for selling Mahalo Marketplace. Except I only had a few hours to pull it all together.

而这正是我出售Mahalo Marketplace的计划。只不过我只有几个小时的时间来把所有事情安排妥当。

THE MAHALO MARKETPLACE PITCH

MAHALO 市场推介

By the time Jon and Mike showed back up at six a.m., I’d already figured out most of the details. “It isn’t enough to just build a regular mall anymore,” I said when they walked in. “You need a big extra feature, a theme.” I spread six files on the table. Jon and Mike looked on, eyes bleary. “Here’s our examples. We frame this as the trend right now. Then we show that Mahalo is no different from any other new mall. By the numbers it is a standard mall. The theme is that it is an open-air market with fresh seafood and authentic Chinese small goods.” They weren’t happy about the early call time, but they got to work right away. We buckled down for four hours and pumped out a pitch deck.

早上六点，当乔恩和迈克回来时，我已经把大部分细节都敲定了。“现在仅仅建一个普通的购物中心已经不够了，”他们进来时，我说道，“你们需要一个大的特色，一个主题。”我把六份文件摊在桌上。乔恩和迈克看着，眼神有些惺忪。“这是我们的案例。我们先把这个概念包装成当前的趋势。然后我们展示，Mahalo 和其他新建的购物中心并没有什么不同。从数据上看，它就是一个标准的购物中心。它的主题是：一个露天市场，提供新鲜的海鲜和正宗的中国小商品。”他们不太乐意这么早集合，但还是立刻投入工作。我们埋头苦干了四个小时，迅速完成了演示文稿。

Then Logan and I, extremely sleep-deprived, showed up at Mitch’s office to meet with the one man who could save us from our Kobayashi Maru. There hadn’t been any time to write a complicated pitch, so what we ended up telling him was very simple.

然后，我和洛根严重睡眠不足，就去了米奇的办公室，去见那个能把我们从“小林丸号”困境中拯救出来的人。我们根本没时间写一份复杂的方案，所以最后跟他说的内容非常简单。

“You’ve probably noticed the latest trend in large commercial real estate,” I started. “Shopping malls with a theme. There’s this ski resort mall in Dubai, this pirate ship mall in Canada, this all-glass mall in L.A.” I casually tossed the files for these projects onto Mitch’s desk as I referenced each one. “These projects all sold in the last year for over a hundred million each.”

“你可能已经注意到大型商业地产的最新趋势了，”我开口说道，“主题购物中心。比如迪拜的滑雪度假村购物中心，加拿大的海盗船购物中心，还有洛杉矶的全玻璃购物中心。”我一边说着，一边漫不经心地把这些项目的文件扔到米奇的桌子上。“这些项目去年都以超过一亿美元的价格售出。”

“And we’ve got the next one,” said Logan enthusiastically. “It’s right here in Hawaii. By the numbers, it’s a standard, Plain Vanilla shopping mall like you might find anywhere. It’s insured, bonded, up to spec on health code, and seismically sound. It checks all the liability boxes from an investor standpoint.”

“我们又找到了下一个项目，”洛根兴奋地说。“它就在夏威夷。从数据上看，它就是一个标准的、千篇一律的购物中心，跟你在其他地方看到的没什么两样。它有保险、有担保，符合卫生规范，而且抗震性能良好。从投资者的角度来看，它满足了所有责任方面的要求。”

“ But there’s something very unique about this property,” I continued. “It doesn’t feel like a regular old mall when you step inside. It feels exactly like an authentic Chinese open-air market. The vendors are all small and quirky, selling exotic and fresh items from all over the world. The layout is based on an actual market in China that dates back to two hundred BC. But the location is smack in downtown Honolulu and all the permits are good for at least another twenty years, just like the other properties in your portfolio.”

“但这处房产确实有其独特之处，”我继续说道，“你一走进去，就不会觉得像个普通的购物中心，而会感觉像是一个地道的中国露天市场。摊贩个个都很小，风格各异，出售来自世界各地的新鲜奇特商品。它的布局仿照了中国一个可以追溯到公元前200年的真实市场。但它的地理位置却位于檀香山市中心，而且所有许可证至少还有20年的有效期，就像您投资组合中的其他房产一样。”

“Yep,” Logan repeated. “Plain Vanilla. No frills. Straight up the middle.”

“没错，”洛根重复道。“原味香草。没什么特别的。就是最普通的。”

“We’re selling it in the next five days,” I said with as much confidence as I could muster.

“我们会在接下来的五天内卖掉它，”我尽可能自信地说。

And we stopped talking.

我们停止了交谈。

Mitch leaned back in his chair and stroked his chin. He was over seventy years old, and now that I was up close, he almost looked frail. But he clearly had an incredible mind for real estate. “Financial projections?” he asked.

米奇向后靠在椅子上，摸了摸下巴。他已经七十多岁了，现在我走近了，他看起来几乎有些虚弱。但他显然对房地产有着惊人的洞察力。“财务预测？”他问道。

“Page thirty-four,” I said.

“第三十四页，”我说。

He flipped through the pitch deck and examined the page where we’d laid out the revenue pipeline, rent roll, annual bumps of 5 percent, and low monthly expenses, and we were even up front about the HVAC needing an update within five years. The guy didn’t even get out a calculator. He just started crunching numbers in his head and muttering to himself.

他快速翻阅了我们的演示文稿，仔细查看了我们列出的收入来源、租金收入、每年5%的租金增长以及较低的月度支出等信息，我们甚至还坦诚地说明了暖通空调系统五年内需要更新。那家伙连计算器都没拿出来，只是在心里默默地计算着，嘴里还不停地念叨着什么。

I looked at Logan, who shrugged at me.

我看向洛根，他耸了耸肩。

Finally, after what seemed like ten minutes during which none of us uttered a single word, Mitch broke his state of trance and looked back up at us.

最后，在仿佛过了十分钟，我们谁也没说一句话之后，米奇终于从恍惚中回过神来，抬起头看着我们。

“I like it,” he said.

“我喜欢，”他说。

My natural instinct was to say, “ Great! We can take you down and show you the property immediately.” In other words, to suggest a next step and try to lock him into a yes. That’s how sales works, right? You always have to be in control and push the buyer to do things on your agenda, right?

我的第一反应是说：“太好了！我们可以马上带您去看房。”换句话说，就是暗示下一步该怎么做，并试图让他答应。销售就是这样，对吧？你必须始终掌控局面，引导买家按照你的计划行事，对吧？

Except I resisted that urge. All I said was: “How do you see us working together on this?”

但我克制住了这种冲动。我只是说：“你觉得我们该如何合作完成这件事？”

Later that afternoon Mitch wired us $10 million. He never even walked the property; our third-party independent reports were good enough. With Mitch on board and his money in escrow, we hit our Rolodex hard and easily had the remaining investors lined up within a week.

当天下午晚些时候，米奇给我们汇了1000万美元。他甚至都没去看过那处房产；我们委托的第三方独立评估报告就足够了。米奇加入后，他的钱也存入了第三方托管账户，我们便迅速联系了其他人脉，一周之内就轻松搞定了剩余的投资者。

A happy ending for everyone, kind of. I had a wife and kid back at home who hadn’t seen me in two weeks. On the plus side, they would still have a house to live in, thanks to my share of the $6 million from the deal.

对每个人来说，这算是一个皆大欢喜的结局吧。我的妻子和孩子还在老家，已经两周没见到我了。不过，好处是他们还有房子住，这要感谢我从这笔交易中分到的那600万美元。

As Logan’s jet took off and we headed back toward California, I couldn’t help but breathe a huge sigh of relief. That was way too close a call.

当洛根的私人飞机起飞，我们返回加利福尼亚时，我不禁长舒了一口气。真是太惊险了。

I pulled out my phone to check a few of the temperature zones in our new refrigerator and make sure the beer was going to be ice cold when I got home. Yep, 34 degrees, just the way I like it. “This isn’t so fancy,” I thought to myself. Just a regular fridge like everyone uses in my neighborhood . . . Plain Vanilla.

我拿出手机查看新冰箱的几个温度区间，确保回家时啤酒是冰镇的。没错，34度，正合我意。“这也没什么特别的，”我心想。不就是个普通的冰箱吗，跟我邻居家用的一样……平平无奇。

#↩

CHAPTER 6

第六章

Leveraging Pessimism

利用悲观情绪

I t was 2:41 a.m. The caller ID read ZERO GRAVITY . My phone was supposed to be in airplane mode because we were on vacation, but I’d left it on because of the fires burning in California near our home, and now, at a time of night that I generally find to be the most tranquil, it was vibrating and ringing like an air-raid siren.

凌晨2点41分，来电显示是“零重力”。因为我们正在度假，我的手机本应该开启飞行模式，但因为加州我家附近发生了火灾，所以我忘记关机了。现在，在这个我通常觉得最安静的夜晚，我的手机却像空袭警报一样震动和响个不停。

It was February. A heavy snow was falling. We were in Vail, Colorado, with our four-year-old son, enjoying a family ski trip. “No calls, for sure,” I had promised. Just me, you, and the baby.

那是二月，大雪纷飞。我们带着四岁的儿子在科罗拉多州的韦尔滑雪，享受着家庭滑雪之旅。“绝对不会打电话的，”我答应过你。只有我、你和宝宝。

But at two a.m. I had to pick up this call because I had three million bucks riding on Zero Gravity.

但凌晨两点，我不得不接这个电话，因为我把三百万美元都押在了《零重力》这部电影上。

“Oren, I need you to help. I am ready take company public but need sniper right now. You help me get best one OK?”

“奥伦，我需要你的帮助。我准备让公司上市，但现在急需一名狙击手。你帮我找到最好的那一个，好吗？”

“Wait a sec,” I whispered, trying not to disturb the beautiful woman sleeping next to me (as if the phone erupting into a chorus of “Barracuda” a few moments earlier had not already done so). I threw on shorts and quietly headed down the hallway toward the living room in our suite, with a view of the slopes. I had a feeling I wasn’t going to be carving fresh powder in the morning as planned.

“等一下，”我轻声说道，尽量不吵醒睡在我身旁的美丽女子（仿佛刚才手机里突然响起的《梭鱼》歌声还不够吵醒她似的）。我套上短裤，悄悄地沿着走廊走向套房的客厅，那里可以俯瞰雪道。我预感明天早上恐怕无法像计划的那样去滑雪了。

Now I was ready to ask some questions of my own. “Anton, is your hundred thousand dollar watch broken again?”

现在我也准备问几个问题了。“安东，你那块价值十万美元的手表又坏了吗？”

“Ha ha. No time for you funny guy, Oren.”

“哈哈，没空搭理你这搞笑的家伙，奥伦。”

This was Zero Gravity’s real name, Anton Kolisnychenko. A few years ago I had met Anton in a bar in his native Ukraine when I had lost my guide earlier in the day and was stumbling around downtown Kiev without a translator, a charged cell phone, or a clue. As day turned to night, I was getting very, very thirsty, so I slipped into a modern-looking bar. They served vodka and just one type of beer—Genesee Cream Ale (worst beer on the planet).

这就是“零重力”乐队的真名，安东·科利斯尼琴科。几年前，我在乌克兰的一家酒吧里遇到了安东。那天早些时候，我跟向导走散了，在基辅市中心跌跌撞撞地闲逛，既没有翻译，手机也没电，什么都不知道。夜幕降临，我渴得厉害，于是溜进了一家看起来很现代的酒吧。他们只供应伏特加和一种啤酒——吉尼斯奶油艾尔（世界上最难喝的啤酒）。

Anton was the only other soul in the bar who spoke any form of English. He helped me translate the menu and he ordered potatoes and some weird dish called golubtsi, which I quickly discovered does not mean “delicious hamburger.” We shared a meal of golubtsi, selyodka, and kishke. And formed a friendship.

安东是酒吧里唯一一个会说英语的人。他帮我翻译了菜单，然后点了土豆和一道叫golubtsi的奇怪菜，我很快发现它并不是“美味汉堡”的意思。我们一起吃了golubtsi、selyodka和kishke，也因此结下了友谊。

But now that friendship was being tested.

但现在这段友谊正面临考验。

“You told me call if I need you. Well, now need you. You meet me tomorrow,” said Anton.

“你跟我说过有事就打电话给你。好吧，现在我需要你了。你明天来见我。”安东说道。

This wasn’t a question. And as usual with Anton, there were no pleasantries, no apologies for calling at two a.m. Just typical straight-to-the-point Anton, with whom an early-morning call always ended with “You need to meet me in a Soviet Bloc country twelve thousand miles away for such-and-such random emergency situation.”

这并非一个问题。和往常一样，安东没有寒暄，也没有为凌晨两点打电话道歉。他一贯直截了当，每次清晨的电话最后都会以这样一句话结束：“你需要去一万两千英里外的某个苏联集团国家和我碰面，处理这样那样莫名其妙的紧急情况。”

But sometimes there was three million dollars at the end of that twelve-thousand-mile trip. And sometimes there was just a hard-to-pronounce cabbage roll. In the future, I had to get better at figuring out which was which.

但有时候，一万两千英里的旅程结束后，你会得到三百万美元。而有时候，你得到的却只是一个拗口难念的卷心菜卷。以后，我得学会分辨它们。

“I am lost my prize sniper right before yesterday. Without superstar number one sniper, I can’t win XXL tournament.”

“就在昨天，我的头号狙击手丢了。没有这位超级巨星头号狙击手，我赢不了XXL锦标赛。”

That hit the fear center of the brain, and for good reason. XXL was a gaming tournament in which $3 million in prize money could be won by the best teams, and until a moment ago, Anton had one of the best teams. In fact, I had recently made a large business bet that he would win this very tournament.

这直接触动了我大脑的恐惧中枢，而且理由充分。XXL 是一项电子竞技锦标赛，奖金高达 300 万美元，只有最优秀的队伍才能赢得。而就在刚才，安东还拥有一支顶尖的队伍。事实上，我最近还下了个大注，赌他会赢得这场比赛。

“If I don’t win, can’t fund my software company, can’t take company public like we plan.” While Anton rambled, I flipped on the light, temporarily blinding myself, and began fumbling with the hotel’s in-room coffee maker.

“如果我输了，就没法为我的软件公司筹集资金，也没法像我们计划的那样让公司上市。”安东喋喋不休的时候，我打开了灯，刺得自己睁不开眼，然后开始笨手笨脚地摆弄酒店房间里的咖啡机。

“Oren, you tell me, please,” he said more desperately than I’d ever heard him sound. “What am I do now? This is what you say, situation crazy .”

“奥伦，你告诉我，求你了，”他绝望地说，语气比我以往听过的任何一次都要急切。“我现在该怎么办？你说得对，情况糟透了。”

I slid a cup under the coffee maker. In just a few minutes I had gone from fast asleep to hearing the words “Hey man, you need to find me a world-class sniper or we’re going to lose a shot at three million bucks.”

我把杯子滑到咖啡机下面。仅仅几分钟后，我就从睡梦中惊醒，听到有人说：“嘿，伙计，你得帮我找个世界级的狙击手，不然我们就错失三百万美元的机会了。”

And there was even more riding on it than $3 million. You see, we needed that money to buy another company, and take the combined companies public on the Nasdaq stock exchange—another way of saying we needed $3 million to get $20 million and hopefully make $100 million. The exact details of how this works aren’t important; what matters is that we had a plan, and we needed the XXL tournament winnings to get the whole process started. It was XXL or die.

而且，这笔钱的意义远不止300万美元。你知道，我们需要这笔钱来收购另一家公司，并将合并后的公司在纳斯达克上市——换句话说，我们需要300万美元来筹集2000万美元，并希望最终能赚到1亿美元。具体操作细节并不重要；重要的是我们有一个计划，而我们需要XXL锦标赛的奖金来启动整个流程。要么赢下XXL，要么就此作废。

“Wait a second, you already have a sniper,” I said, starting to wake up as caffeine made its way into my central nervous system. “What happened to the fat Asian kid in the Van Halen shirt? He’s awesome.”

“等等，你们已经有狙击手了，”我说，咖啡因开始发挥作用，让我清醒过来。“那个穿范·海伦乐队T恤的胖亚洲小子呢？他超厉害的。”

“Oh, you mean GummiBear? Yes of course, he’s best in world. But Oren, I quit that team. ”

“哦，你是说小熊软糖？当然，他是世界第一。不过奥伦，我已经退出那个队伍了。”

“Wait. What? ” Anton leaving his team was like Tom Brady in his prime quitting the Patriots. This was indeed situation crazy. “Why would you leave your team, Anton?”

“等等，什么？”安东离开球队，就像巅峰时期的汤姆·布雷迪离开爱国者队一样。这简直太疯狂了。“安东，你为什么要离开你的球队？”

He gave me a long, rambling rant about unfair treatment at the hands of the company that managed his team, while I placed him on mute and cursed him loudly. Finally, he reached the end of his monologue and I took the phone off mute to get down to business.

他滔滔不绝地抱怨公司对他团队的不公平待遇，我则把他静音，大声咒骂他。最后，他终于说完，我才解除静音，开始谈正事。

“OK, let me see if I’ve got this straight,” I said, rubbing my forehead and trying to piece together the various strands of Anton’s story. “You got sick of management putting you on a constant game rotation with no rest, so you organized a mutiny but it backfired, and your contract got terminated, so you pulled together a new team . . . but you don’t have a sniper. Without a good sniper the whole deal is up in smoke. And now, at two-thirty a.m. on a Tuesday while I am in Colorado on a family vacation, you want me to find you a sniper?”

“好吧，让我看看我有没有理解错，”我揉着额头，努力把安东说的那些话拼凑起来。“你受够了管理层让你不停地轮换上场，没有休息时间，所以你组织了一场兵变，结果适得其反，合同被终止了，于是你组建了一支新队伍……但是你没有狙击手。没有一个好的狙击手，一切都将付诸东流。现在，周二凌晨两点半，我正在科罗拉多州和家人度假，你却要我帮你找个狙击手？”

“I know you can do it, Oren Klaff. You are the only person I can call. I am so much believing in you. And it will only take you few hours. Then you go back to happy snow vacation. I can’t win without best sniper. If I don’t win XXL money, it all goes up in gas.”

“我知道你能做到，奥伦·克拉夫。你是唯一一个我能求助的人。我对你充满信心。这只需要你几个小时的时间。然后你就可以回去享受快乐的雪地假期了。没有最佳狙击手，我赢不了。如果我赢不到巨额奖金，一切都白费了。”

“Smoke,” I corrected him.

“是烟，”我纠正他。

“I quit smoke last year,” Anton said.

“我去年戒烟了，”安东说。

“Never mind. So who’s the best sniper in the world?” I asked.

“算了。那么，世界上最好的狙击手是谁？”我问道。

“Mac Jones ‘Bulletz for Breakfast,’” he replied. I waited for him to laugh or somehow indicate that he was joking, but he didn’t.

“麦克·琼斯的《早餐子弹》，”他回答道。我等着他笑出来或者以某种方式表明他是在开玩笑，但他没有。

“So he’s the guy we need?”

“所以他就是我们需要的那个人？”

“Absolutely. It’s Bulletz or we definitely lose.”

“当然。要么是Bulletz，要么我们肯定输。”

I wasn’t quite understanding. “Why don’t you just ask him to play with you? I mean, you’re an eSports celebrity. And you make millions for your teammates. Everybody in the world wants to play on your team. Why would he say no?”

我不太明白。“你为什么不直接邀请他一起玩呢？我的意思是，你可是电竞明星，你给队友赚了数百万美元，全世界的人都想加入你的队伍，他为什么要拒绝呢？”

“I already ask him,” said Anton. “He says already on good team. He is celebrity with very good contract and not want to change middle of season. Maybe next year, maybe not.”

“我已经问过他了，”安东说。“他说他现在在一支不错的球队。他是个明星球员，合同也很好，不想赛季中途换队。也许明年会，也许不会。”

It was now Tuesday morning at 3:15 a.m. I was not too happy. “Just tell me how to find him. That’s all I need to know,” I said flatly, hiding my frustration.

现在是周二凌晨3点15分。我心情很不好。“告诉我怎么找到他，我就想知道这些。”我语气平淡地说，努力掩饰着内心的沮丧。

“He’ll be at Gamecon tomorrow in Las Vegas,” said Anton, excited to have me once again solving his problems. “This is why I say, please come; it’s only short flight. I’ll send the 604-LX.”

“他明天会在拉斯维加斯的游戏展上，”安东兴奋地说，很高兴我又能帮他解决问题了。“所以我才说，请务必来；飞行时间很短。我会派604-LX过去。”

That meant a Bombardier Challenger 604 aircraft was headed my way. At 48,000 pounds, 20 seats, a small bedroom, with shower, and 600 mph cruising speed, that’s as good as it gets.

这意味着一架庞巴迪挑战者604型飞机正朝我飞来。这架飞机重48000磅，有20个座位，一个带淋浴的小卧室，巡航速度可达600英里/小时，这已经是极致了。

“OK, comrade,” I said. “I’ll meet you there for a few hours, and then it’s back to the slopes for me, got it?”

“好的，同志，”我说。“我会在那儿和你待几个小时，然后我就得回滑雪场了，明白吗？”

“No, but thank you,” said Anton, a.k.a. Zero Gravity, misunderstanding me on purpose (his way of doing things). “See you in few hours because plane there soon. It is just easy; meet pilot at Beaver Creek. OK very good.” Click.

“不，谢谢，”安东（又名“零重力”）故意误解我的意思（这是他惯用的伎俩）。“几个小时后见，因为飞机很快就到了。很简单，在比弗克里克和飞行员碰面。好的，没问题。”咔哒一声。

I sighed. Anton, if nothing else, was definitely an optimist.

我叹了口气。安东就算别的方面不突出，也绝对是个乐观主义者。

THE PESSIMISM PROBLEM

悲观主义问题

Everyone loves an optimist. A positive outlook is one of the most important traits we look for in friends, employees, leaders, and especially salespeople. We teach our kids that a can-do attitude is the key to success. And almost every self-help book starts with the mantra “You can do it!” (once you meditate, visualize what you want, and eliminate all forms of negativity). After all, positive thinking works wonders, right? We actualize what we visualize. Maybe and maybe not.

人人都喜欢乐观的人。积极乐观的态度是我们择友、择业、择业，尤其是择业时最看重的品质之一。我们教导孩子，积极进取的态度是成功的关键。几乎每一本自助书籍都以“你能做到！”这句口号开头（前提是你要冥想、想象你想要的东西，并消除所有消极情绪）。毕竟，积极思考真的有奇效，不是吗？我们想象的东西就会变成现实。也许会，也许不会。

It’s certainly enjoyable to talk about what will happen once the deal is closed, the money is in the bank, and the business plan starts happening. It’s fun to imagine a future where our problems are long gone, we live in a dream house, everyone adores us, and we are showered with praise. Psychologists simply call this the Optimism Mind-set: the belief that generally speaking, good things are going to happen soon, very soon.

当然，谈论交易完成、资金到账、商业计划开始实施后会发生什么，确实令人愉悦。想象未来，所有问题都迎刃而解，我们住进梦想中的房子，人人都爱我们，赞誉如潮，这种感觉也十分美好。心理学家将这种心态称为“乐观心态”：相信好事很快就会发生，而且会非常快。

A positive outlook can motivate people toward incredible accomplishments. Optimists are the ones who put a man on the moon last century, and in this century, they’ll put another one on Mars. Optimists climbed Mount Everest, created nuclear energy, and sequenced the human genome. Optimists are good at motivating and attracting others to join their cause.

积极乐观的态度能够激励人们取得非凡的成就。正是乐观主义者在上个世纪将人类送上月球，而在这个世纪，他们还将把另一位宇航员送上火星。乐观主义者攀登了珠穆朗玛峰，创造了核能，并完成了人类基因组测序。乐观主义者善于激励和吸引他人加入他们的事业。

So if you had to guess, what types of professionals are the most optimistic?

那么，如果你要猜测的话，你认为哪些类型的专业人士最乐观？

There’s no question about it: entrepreneurs and salespeople. By definition, their job is to seed optimism. They’re programmed to promote a vision of the future in which your biggest problems are solved, your life becomes easier, and your dreams are checked off one after the next. Just buy now and you will look better, feel better, make more money, get the girl, be parent of the year, and rise in the social hierarchy to become a beloved role model for the regular citizens to admire.

毫无疑问，企业家和销售人员就是幕后推手。从本质上讲，他们的工作就是散播乐观情绪。他们被灌输了一种未来愿景：你最大的问题都能迎刃而解，生活会变得轻松无比，梦想也会一个接一个地实现。现在就买，你就能容光焕发、神采奕奕、财源滚滚、抱得美人归、成为年度最佳父母，并在社会阶梯上步步高升，成为普通民众敬仰的榜样。

Given the nature of their profession, salespeople are programmed to be optimistic and push you in that direction too. But does projecting optimism work as well as we think?

鉴于销售人员的职业性质，他们往往被训练得乐观，并试图让你也朝着这个方向发展。但是，展现乐观真的像我们想象的那样有效吗？

Just consider how the typical sales sequence goes:

想想典型的销售流程是怎样的：

  1. Introduce the product; explain the offer.
    介绍产品；解释优惠内容。
  2. Be exceedingly optimistic; encourage the buyer to feel good about the product.
    要非常乐观；鼓励买家对产品感到满意。
  3. Try to close: “So what do you think? Do we have a deal today?” At which point the buyer raises his or her concerns and objections.
    尝试促成交易：“怎么样？今天成交吗？”此时买家会提出自己的疑虑和反对意见。
  4. Work hard to crush each objection, one by one. Tell the buyer none of his fears will materialize, and all of her dreams will come true.
    努力逐一消除每一个异议。告诉买家，他所有的担忧都不会成为现实，她所有的梦想都会实现。
  5. Try to close again—and keep trying (try till you die).
    再试一次——然后继续尝试（直到你死为止）。

The problem with this pattern is it is closer to debate and argumentation than it is to selling and convincing. The result? Even if the buyer relents and says yes, he hasn’t really bought in; most likely he didn’t have the time or energy to debate the purchase any further with you, so he said yes to end the standoff and get out of the conversation. But he may or may not have had any real intention of going through with it. This is why it’s such a common occurrence for salespeople to think they’ve closed a deal, only to watch it fall apart as time goes on.

这种模式的问题在于，它更接近于辩论和争论，而非销售和说服。结果呢？即使买家最终让步答应了，他其实并没有真正购买；很可能他没有时间和精力再跟你争论购买事宜，所以为了结束僵局、结束对话而答应了。但他可能根本没有真正打算完成交易。这就是为什么销售人员常常以为自己已经达成交易，结果却眼睁睁看着它随着时间的推移而告吹的原因。

Pure optimism—the kind that bubbles up from the emotional core of salespeople—actually creates stress for the typical buyer. Bursting enthusiasm and excessive positivity can disrupt the buyer’s decision-making process and violate his or her sense of autonomy—something you never want to do.

纯粹的乐观——那种源自销售人员内心深处的乐观——实际上会给普通买家带来压力。过分的热情和过度的积极态度会扰乱买家的决策过程，侵犯他们的自主权——这是你绝对不想看到的。

Let me flip the script for you: It’s pessimism, not optimism, that is the formula for success in sales.

让我换个角度来说：销售成功的秘诀是悲观，而不是乐观。

Pessimism gets a bad rap as the evil opposite of optimism. It’s not. What pessimism actually does is provide an alternative point of view, and it’s one the buyer has to consider before making a purchase decision that sticks and doesn’t result in buyer’s remorse.

悲观主义常被妖魔化，被视为乐观主义的反面。其实不然。悲观主义实际上提供了一种不同的视角，买家在做出最终购买决定之前必须考虑这种视角，这样才能避免日后后悔。

When it comes to making a deal in which there’s a lot on the line, buyers always go through a period of skepticism and unease before they ultimately decide they feel good enough to move forward. They must consider how the partnership with you might fail; how things might not work out the way you say; and how, by choosing you over someone else, they may actually lose some (or all) of their money. You should not fight this process, but instead guide them through it.

在进行一笔涉及重大利益的交易时，买家总会经历一段怀疑和不安的时期，最终才会决定是否继续推进。他们必须考虑与你合作可能失败的情况；事情可能不会像你承诺的那样发展；以及选择你而不是其他人，他们实际上可能会损失部分（甚至全部）资金。你不应该阻挠这个过程，而应该引导他们顺利度过。

I realize this might seem counterintuitive and self-destructive. After all, it doesn’t exactly sound like the positive thinking they teach at a “Win Friends and Influence People” seminar. To influence people, we’re supposed to minimize all negative thoughts, leaving buyers excited and enthusiastic about investing in us and our ideas, right? Not exactly. The possibility of failure enhances a buyer’s motivation to act.

我知道这听起来可能有点反直觉，甚至有损自身利益。毕竟，这听起来和“人性的弱点”研讨会上教授的积极思考方式不太一样。要想影响他人，我们应该尽量减少负面想法，让买家对我们和我们的想法充满热情，对吗？其实不然。失败的可能性反而会增强买家采取行动的动力。

There is a kind of self-satisfaction to pessimism. Thinking about obstacles and the many things that might go wrong in a deal is healthy and reassuring, because nothing in life is perfect, and buyers are searching for that imperfection to decide if they can live with it or not. If you hide the negatives, the sale cannot proceed. Until the negatives are out in the open, the buyer’s spoken or unspoken state of mind is “What’s the catch?” Therefore, pessimism is not a type of negative thinking that needs to be argued with, overcome, and destroyed. Instead, it should be invited and cultivated.

悲观主义中蕴含着一种自我满足感。思考交易中可能遇到的障碍和各种问题其实是有益且令人安心的，因为人生没有完美，买家正是在寻找这些瑕疵，以此来决定是否接受。如果隐瞒负面因素，交易就无法进行。在负面因素被公开之前，买家内心深处（无论是否明说）都会想着“这里面有什么猫腻？” 因此，悲观主义并非一种需要与之争论、克服或消除的消极思维，相反，它应该被接纳和培养。

Think about it this way. When you pressure a buyer to express optimism and move ahead with your deal before they feel ready, it threatens their feeling of autonomy. People react negatively when their autonomy is restricted in any way, because, as I established early in this book, we are hardwired to want to feel we are making our own decisions through a period of personal reflection, on our own time, and without pressure by others. You must give the person you are doing business with a feeling of autonomy so they feel totally free to object, demur, and disagree, knowing that you aren’t going to be jumping on their case to overcome objections.

不妨这样想。如果你在买家还没准备好之前就催促他们表达乐观态度并推进交易，就会威胁到他们的自主感。人们一旦自主权受到任何限制，都会产生负面反应，因为正如我在本书开头所述，我们天生就渴望在经过一段时间的个人反思后，在自己的时间安排下，不受他人压力地做出决定。你必须给予与你做生意的人一种自主感，让他们可以完全自由地提出异议、犹豫和反对意见，而不必担心你会为了消除他们的异议而强行介入。

Giving a buyer autonomy doesn’t mean giving up control, but most people feel they have to choose one or the other. Have you ever seen a good presentation that is well organized, insightful, and persuasive but at the last moment fizzles like a damp match that won’t light, failing to close the deal? The last few seconds probably involved one of these statements:

给予买家自主权并不意味着放弃控制权，但大多数人觉得他们必须在两者之间做出选择。你是否见过这样的演示：组织有序、见解深刻、极具说服力，却在最后关头像一根熄灭的火柴一样哑火，最终未能达成交易？最后几秒钟很可能出现了以下几种情况：

  • “So . . . what do you think? Is this something you would be interested in?”
    “那么……你觉得怎么样？你对此感兴趣吗？”
  • “That’s my pitch, so let me turn it over to you, are there any questions?”
    “我的演讲就到这里，现在交给你们了，有什么问题吗？”
  • “Does all this make sense? What are your thoughts and feelings about moving ahead with the purchase?”
    “这一切是否合理？您对继续推进此次购买有何想法和感受？”

These are common ways to end a presentation—I’ve seen it a thousand times over. The problem with these kinds of statements is that they do nothing but put absolute control in the hands of the buyer. Next, the astute buyer will supply a laundry list of reasons why he can’t go any further today, and say exactly what every buyer is preprogrammed to say: “This looks good. We don’t have any more questions right now, but if you give us all the information by email, we’ll discuss it internally and get back to you in the next few weeks.”

这些都是常见的演示结束方式——我见过无数次了。这类陈述的问题在于，它们除了把绝对的控制权拱手让给买家之外，没有任何其他作用。接下来，精明的买家会列出一大堆理由说明今天无法继续推进，然后说出每个买家都会说的那句话：“看起来不错。我们现在没有其他问题了，但如果您能把所有信息通过邮件发给我们，我们会内部讨论一下，并在接下来的几周内回复您。”

A few weeks? And who exactly is “we”?

几周？而且“我们”究竟指的是谁？

Clearly, you cannot give the buyer complete control to decide how to proceed with you and your deal, because it may well be the last you hear from them. The goal is not to have weeks of follow-up calls and frustrating interactions. The goal is to create Inception today . . . Now .

显然，你不能让买家完全掌控后续事宜，因为这很可能就是你最后一次听到他们的消息。我们的目标不是让你陷入长达数周的后续电话和令人沮丧的沟通中。我们的目标是今天就启动“启动”项目……现在就启动。

I’ve found that the solution is pretty simple: Give a buyer permission to start questioning you and your deal, but first teach them exactly what to question about it .

我发现解决办法很简单：允许买家开始质疑你和你的交易，但首先要教会他们应该问些什么。

Pessimism + Autonomy + Expertise = Inception

悲观主义 + 自主性 + 专业知识 = 创世纪

You have to be careful, however, because telling anyone what to question and what not to question can be viewed as if you’re telling them what to think. And when a buyer sees an obvious manipulation, he or she starts to back away.

但是，你必须小心，因为告诉别人该问什么、不该问什么，可能会被视为你在告诉他们该怎么想。而当买家察觉到明显的操纵时，他们就会开始退缩。

Evidence of this comes from the auto industry, which historically used high-pressure tactics and trained their salespeople to never take no for an answer. Today, it’s quite different. Every major auto manufacturer has gone to standardized pricing published online, and low-pressure deal making. They have learned that pressure backfires.

汽车行业就是一个例证。过去，汽车行业常常采用高压销售策略，并训练销售人员永不接受拒绝。而如今，情况已大不相同。所有大型汽车制造商都已转向在线公布的标准化定价和低压力的销售方式。他们已经认识到，施压只会适得其反。

Buyers want control (or at least the illusion of it) over the buying process. When a buyer feels controlled by you, he takes a step back, or leaves the negotiation entirely. Any feeling of psychological control, time pressure, scarcity pressure, social pressure, or other typical sales tools causes buyers to simply back away.

买家希望掌控（或者至少是掌控）购买过程。如果买家感觉被你控制，他就会退缩，甚至直接退出谈判。任何心理控制感、时间压力、稀缺性压力、社会压力或其他常见的销售手段都会导致买家退缩。

But you wouldn’t need to control anyone if you had a way to put in place a sort of hidden boundary, so the conversation stayed focused on what’s important and stayed away from distraction. Imagine an invisible fence, like the ones used to keep a dog in the yard, which would contain a buyer’s questions about what really matters. Inside the invisible fence are all the facts that need to be accepted, topics open for discussion, issues you are happy to discuss. Outside the fence are off-limits topics, things that don’t matter, and time wasters. And if you set this invisible fence properly, the buyer won’t realize you’ve erected the boundaries and will accept them as a natural part of the conversation.

但如果你能设置一种隐形的边界，让谈话始终聚焦于重要事项，避免被其他事情分散注意力，你就无需控制任何人了。想象一下，就像用来圈养狗狗的那种隐形围栏，它能将买家真正关心的问题限制在内。围栏之内是所有需要接受的事实、可以讨论的话题，以及你乐于探讨的问题。围栏之外则是禁忌话题、无关紧要的事情和浪费时间的事情。如果你能正确设置这道隐形围栏，买家不会意识到你设置了这些边界，而是会自然而然地接受它们，将其视为谈话的一部分。

In Las Vegas for the big tournament, I was about to use this approach to help Anton recruit a world-class sniper for his Counter-Strike team. But there were a few twists in store I didn’t see coming.

在拉斯维加斯参加大型锦标赛期间，我正打算用这种方法帮助安东为他的反恐精英战队招募一位世界级的狙击手。但事情的发展却出乎我的意料。

PICKING OFF A STAR SNIPER

狙击一名明星狙击手

“There he is,” said Anton, taking my arm and pointing in the direction of a kid who fit the perfect gamer stereotype: dyed blond hair with a few purple streaks, three-hundred-dollar sneakers, black hoodie, drinking a Mountain Dew. A group of fans surrounded this eSports “athlete,” pushing for autographs as they might a football or baseball star. It seemed a bit much, because, after all, these were just video game players.

“他在那儿，”安东说着，拉起我的胳膊，指着一个完全符合游戏玩家刻板印象的男孩：染成金色的头发，还挑染了几缕紫色，脚蹬价值三百美元的运动鞋，身穿黑色连帽衫，手里拿着一罐激浪汽水。一群粉丝围着这位电子竞技“运动员”，像追捧足球明星或棒球明星一样，争相索要签名。这似乎有点过头了，毕竟，他们只是电子游戏玩家而已。

To be fair, if any video game player deserved this star treatment at any tournament ever, it was this one. Mac “Bulletz4Breakfast” Jones was one of the best snipers in the world. He was a master of efficiency and knew where to be in the game at every instant and what to do from any spot on the map. If you needed to destroy enemy positions, win games, and rack up tournament points, you needed Bulletz or someone like him.

平心而论，如果说有哪位电子游戏选手配得上在任何锦标赛中获得如此明星般的待遇，那非他莫属。Mac “Bulletz4Breakfast” Jones 是世界上最优秀的狙击手之一。他效率极高，深谙游戏中每个时刻的最佳位置，以及在地图上任何位置该如何行动。如果你需要摧毁敌方阵地、赢得比赛、并积累锦标赛积分，那么你需要 Bulletz 或者像他一样的选手。

All this is to say: There wasn’t a team that didn’t want Bulletz. If we were going to have any hope of convincing him to come play for us, we’d have to offer him something other teams simply couldn’t—or weren’t thinking about. But what could that possibly be?

总而言之：没有哪支球队不想要布莱茨。如果我们想说服他来为我们效力，就必须给他提供其他球队根本无法提供——或者根本没想到——的东西。但这究竟是什么呢？

Anton and I spent a few energy-drink-fueled hours cooking up the best pitch we could come up with. The plan was to focus on how we could provide for him in the long term, whereas his current team was thinking only about the short term. We thought it was compelling and had a chance to sway him. Now we were going to find out as we elbowed through the semicircle of fans and presented ourselves.

我和安东花了几个小时，靠着能量饮料提神，绞尽脑汁地想出了我们能想到的最佳方案。我们的计划是着重强调我们如何能为他提供长期的保障，而他现在的团队却只考虑短期利益。我们觉得这个方案很有说服力，有机会打动他。现在，我们挤过球迷们围成的半圆形人群，准备向他展示自己，看看结果如何。

“What do you guys want?” Bulletz asked as soon as we got within eyesight. “You’re poison right now, Anton. Don’t even stand near me. I could get fired just for talking to you.” Bulletz looked nervously around the lobby to see who might be watching or recording this conversation. “I already have a team,” he added with a tone of finality, and started to move away from us.

“你们想干什么？”我们刚一进入布莱茨的视线，他就问道。“安东，你现在就是个毒瘤。别靠近我。我跟你说话都可能丢掉饭碗。”布莱茨紧张地环顾四周，看看有没有人正在监视或录音。“我已经有团队了。”他语气斩钉截铁地说完，便转身离开。

“Thought you might be able to use a couple of friends like us, given your current situation and what people are saying—because it’s not all good stuff,” I said, shrugging casually. It was crucial that we didn’t look needy. Whiz kids like Bulletz could smell desperation a mile away.

“鉴于你目前的处境和人们的议论——因为那些议论可不全是好话——我想你或许需要我们这样的朋友，”我漫不经心地耸了耸肩说道。我们必须表现得不那么需要人帮助。像布莱茨这样的神童一眼就能看出谁在苦苦哀求。

“Maybe you not so secure as you think if you no even allowed to talk to us,” said Anton. “We came because have something you want, you need, something you can use . . . if you’re going to keep playing the game.”

“如果你连跟我们说话的权利都没有，那或许你并没有你想象的那么安全，”安东说。“我们来是因为我们这里有你想要的、你需要的、你能用得上的东西……如果你还想继续玩这场游戏的话。”

We had just said to Bulletz, in effect, “Industry people are talking about you and there’s a problem brewing. We can help get ahead of it—and even solve it.”

我们当时实际上是对布莱茨说的：“业内人士都在谈论你，而且一个问题正在酝酿之中。我们可以帮助你提前应对——甚至解决问题。”

The idea was to cause an inkling of impending doom to creep into Bulletz’s thinking. With these two statements, we had used the twin psychological hooks that will always get the attention of a star competitor, whether an athlete, surgeon, entrepreneur, or executive. While almost nothing works on everyone, you’ll be surprised how effective this can be to get someone’s attention: arousing their curiosity by threatening their social ranking and then offering a valuable secret. When these elements are combined, no one can resist at least taking a look. It’s as close to a universal curiosity formula as you can get.

我们的目的是让布莱茨心中萌生一丝厄运的预感。通过这两句话，我们运用了两种心理策略，它们总能吸引明星竞争对手的注意力，无论他们是运动员、外科医生、企业家还是高管。虽然几乎没有什么方法对每个人都有效，但你会惊讶于这种方法吸引他人注意力的效果：先用威胁他们的社会地位来激起他们的好奇心，然后再提供一个有价值的秘密。当这些要素结合在一起时，没有人能抗拒至少一探究竟。这几乎是你能找到的最接近万能好奇心公式的东西了。

When you imply that someone’s position in the dominance hierarchy and social order is changing, they snap to attention. It’s the first rule of stardom that every celebrity desperately needs to know what is being said about him or her by others, and is highly tuned to gossip coming from fans and peers. Second, every star knows intuitively that you’re only as good as your last win, so they are on the constant lookout for valuable information provided by a competitor. Quarterbacks want to know what other quarterbacks are doing to prevent injury in running plays. CEOs of Fortune 500 companies want to know what other CEOs are doing to keep stock prices stable while interest rates are rising. And gamers want to know how other gamers are making money in the emerging eSports industry.

当你暗示某人在等级制度和社会秩序中的地位正在发生变化时，他们会立刻警觉起来。明星的第一条铁律是：每个名人都迫切想知道别人对自己的评价，并且对粉丝和同行的八卦消息格外关注。其次，每个明星都凭直觉知道，你的价值取决于你最近的胜利，所以他们会时刻留意竞争对手提供的任何有价值的信息。四分卫想知道其他四分卫是如何避免在跑动进攻中受伤的。财富500强公司的CEO想知道其他CEO是如何在利率上升的情况下保持股价稳定的。而游戏玩家则想知道其他玩家是如何在蓬勃发展的电子竞技行业中赚钱的。

We had taken the first step in the recruitment of Bulletz, but we couldn’t push him to switch teams at that moment; he was barely willing to talk to us. This was going to be a slow boil. In the end, it would have to be his decision, or at least feel like it was. We needed Inception.

我们已经迈出了招募布莱茨的第一步，但当时我们无法强迫他转投其他队伍；他几乎不愿意和我们交谈。这将会是一个循序渐进的过程。最终，这必须由他自己决定，或者至少让他感觉是这样。我们需要“盗梦空间”。

“What are you talking about?” he said. “I don’t need anything. I’m at the top of my game. Look around—I’ve got the best contract of any player at this tournament.” His pride was a little too defensive. He wasn’t used to thinking about his future pessimistically, and doing so had rattled him enough to get him to pay attention to us and start talking.

“你在说什么？”他说道，“我什么都不需要。我现在状态正佳。看看周围——我的合同是本次锦标赛所有球员里最好的。”他的自尊心让他显得有些过于敏感。他并不习惯悲观地看待自己的未来，而这种想法让他感到不安，以至于他开始注意到我们，并和我们聊了起来。

We had moved away from the crowd as security guards pushed the fans off and they scattered, looking for easier autographs.

保安人员将粉丝们推开，粉丝们四散奔逃，寻找更容易获得签名的人，我们便离开了人群。

“That contract of yours isn’t going to last another year,” said Anton, because he couldn’t help adding an extra jab. “You’re twenty-five years old, that’s the expiration date for a gamer.”

“你的合同不会再持续一年了，”安东忍不住又挖苦了一句，“你都二十五岁了，游戏选手的职业生涯到此就结束了。”

He was right. As living proof, Anton was already thirty-five and hadn’t been a competitive player for years.

他说得没错。安东就是活生生的例子，他当时已经35岁了，而且多年没有参加过竞技比赛了。

“Your numbers are down,” I said, leaning in conspiratorially, like a good cop giving him advice for his own good. “Nobody’s winning streak lasts as long as they think it will.

“你的胜率下降了，”我凑近他，神秘兮兮地说，就像一个好警察为了他好而给他提建议一样。“没有人的连胜纪录会像他们想象的那样长久。”

“Let us show you what we have and you can decide for yourself if it’s valuable,” I continued. “We are building a gaming team that makes money year after year, and we don’t worry about winning or losing this tournament or that one. Look at Zero,” I said, pointing to Anton. “He’s a mediocre player compared to these kids, right? What would you pay him, seventy-five thousand? Or less?”

“让我们给你看看我们有什么，你自己判断它值不值钱，”我继续说道。“我们正在打造一支年年盈利的电竞战队，我们不在乎这场比赛的输赢。看看Zero，”我指着Anton说。“跟这些孩子比起来，他水平一般，对吧？你愿意给他多少钱？七万五千？还是更少？”

Bulletz nodded and winced at the same time, as if this was a very low salary to do the “hard work” of playing video games—but it was also the right number.

Bulletz 点了点头，同时皱起了眉头，仿佛这份薪水对于从事玩电子游戏这种“艰苦工作”来说太低了——但同时，这个数字也正合适。

“Well, this year he’s going to make three million. We could help set you up like this—a better long-term picture for yourself, something that will work when you’re as old as Zero here. We have a different way of looking at things for players like you, a way that builds a lot of wealth, win or lose.”

“嗯，他今年能赚三百万。我们可以帮你打造这样的未来——为你规划一个更美好的长远蓝图，即使你像Zero一样老了，也能从中受益。我们对像你这样的玩家有不同的看法，无论输赢，都能帮你积累财富。”

“OK, I’ll listen, but it has to be fast ,” Bulletz said, suddenly looking a little nervous. I almost felt bad for him. When you took away all those digital guns and grenades, he was just an uncertain kid who was always one big loss away from moving back to his hometown in the Midwest to work at an Apple store. “You want me to leave my management and take a shot with you? That’s professional suicide. If your team fails, no one will touch me.”

“好吧，我听你的，但得快点，”布莱茨突然显得有些紧张。我几乎有点同情他了。抛开那些数字时代的枪炮和手榴弹，他不过是个迷茫的年轻人，随时可能因为一次重大失败而回到中西部老家，去苹果专卖店打工。“你想让我放弃现在的管理工作，跟你一起冒险？这简直是职业自杀。如果你们团队失败了，没人会再用我。”

“No, you’re wro—” Anton started, and stopped when he felt me stepping on his foot to keep him from talking. If he started countering every one of Bulletz’s objections, he would just turn it into a battle of two big egos, and in that scenario Bulletz would never agree to join Anton’s team. The only way to get this kid to come on board was to let him feel all the negative thoughts he was experiencing and process them, and help him realize our deal was better for him. It had to be his own decision, without Anton bullying him into anything at all. I had to cut this short until I could talk to Anton about the importance of pessimism.

“不，你错了——”安东刚开口，就感觉到我踩了他一脚，阻止他继续说下去。如果他开始反驳布莱茨的每一个反对意见，那只会演变成两个自尊心极强的人之间的较量，那样的话，布莱茨肯定不会同意加入安东的团队。要想让这孩子加入，唯一的办法就是让他感受并消化他所有的负面想法，帮助他意识到我们的方案对他更有利。这必须是他自己的决定，安东绝对不能强迫他做任何事。我必须尽快结束这场争论，等我跟安东谈谈悲观主义的重要性。

“Listen, kid, you’ve had a great five-year run,” I said. “You’re a legend. You know the game better than anyone. I mean, you’re right, you don’t need us right now. But you still need to see what we have.”

“听着，小子，你这五年打得太棒了，”我说。“你是个传奇。你比任何人都更懂球。我的意思是，你说得对，你现在不需要我们。但你还是应该看看我们有什么。”

“OK,” he said quietly, “I’ll meet you during the preliminary round one.”

“好的，”他平静地说，“第一轮预赛的时候见。”

DROP THE DOME TO CONTAIN THE PESSIMISM

放下穹顶以遏制悲观主义

Autonomy and pessimism is a dangerous combination. The problem is that once your buyer starts thinking about negative aspects of you and your deal, he might start to question things you don’t want him questioning, for which there are no good answers and which don’t matter anyway. After you grant the buyer full autonomy to think, do, and say anything that comes to mind, you can no longer control him. The solution is to set up invisible boundaries ahead of time and get your buyer to accept them. Then, when you do grant him autonomy, he will naturally confine himself within the “do not cross” lines you created, without even realizing he is doing it.

自主性和悲观主义是危险的组合。问题在于，一旦买家开始思考你和交易的负面因素，他可能会质疑一些你不希望他质疑的事情，而这些问题既没有好的答案，也无关紧要。一旦你赋予买家完全的自主权，让他想什么就做什么，想说什么就说什么，你就无法再控制他了。解决办法是事先设定一些无形的界限，并让买家接受这些界限。这样，当你真正赋予他自主权时，他自然而然地就会将自己限制在你设定的“禁止越界”范围内，甚至不会意识到自己正在这样做。

Watching a classic Jim Carrey movie can teach us something about how this works. In the film The Truman Show , the main character, Truman Burbank, played by Carrey, comes to realize he has been living his entire life beneath a giant dome constructed by television producers. Everyone Truman has ever known turns out to be an actor, and he has unwittingly been the star of a TV show his entire life. It takes him decades to realize he has been living under a dome, discovering it finally when his sailboat crashes into plywood painted to look like the distant horizon.

观看一部金·凯瑞的经典电影或许能让我们了解其中的奥秘。在电影《楚门的世界》中，由凯瑞饰演的主角楚门·伯班克逐渐意识到，他一生都生活在一个由电视制作人建造的巨大穹顶之下。楚门认识的所有人原来都是演员，而他自己也一直浑然不知地成为了电视节目的明星。他花了数十年才意识到自己一直生活在穹顶之下，直到他的帆船撞上一块涂成远方地平线形状的胶合板，他才最终发现了真相。

This, of course, is a dramatic Hollywood example, but it illustrates a fundamental truth: Humans are generally slow to question boundaries if we don’t notice them being set.

这当然是一个戏剧性的好莱坞例子，但它说明了一条基本真理：如果我们没有注意到界限的设定，人类通常不会很快质疑这些界限。

If you have ever flown on a commercial airliner, you have heard the safety instructions at the beginning of the flight. One instruction concerns the oxygen masks, which will drop down from the overhead compartment in the event of a sudden depressurization at altitude. In that talk, you are warned to put on your own mask before trying to assist someone else. Do you know why? It doesn’t matter why , because they aren’t asking you to debate this topic. They’re telling you how it works and if you don’t like it, feel free to get off the plane. (Of course, the answer is that at high altitude there is very little oxygen in the air, and the brain can survive for only a few seconds without supplemental oxygen, so in the time it takes to help someone else who is confused and struggling, you could both pass out and die and will be of no help to others.)

如果你坐过商业航班，肯定听过起飞前的安全须知。其中一条是关于氧气面罩的，如果飞机在高空突然失压，面罩会从头顶行李舱落下。在安全须知中，你会被告知，在帮助他人之前，务必先戴好自己的面罩。你知道为什么吗？其实原因并不重要，因为他们并不是要你讨论这个问题。他们只是告诉你氧气面罩的使用方法，如果你不喜欢，可以随时下飞机。（当然，答案是：在高空，空气中氧气含量极低，大脑在没有氧气的情况下只能存活几秒钟。因此，在你帮助一个神志不清、挣扎求生的人的这段时间里，你和他都可能昏迷不醒，甚至死亡，也就帮不上其他人的忙了。）

When boundaries are already in place ahead of time, or explained as the industry norm, we don’t question them. But when someone tries to push a seemingly arbitrary limit upon us out of the blue, we resist. If you want to change the rules, no problem—you simply have to do it very slowly, little by little, so your buyer doesn’t notice. Experimental psychologists describe this with names like “change blindness,” “choice detection,” or “the flicker paradigm.” No matter what you call it, study after study has shown that if the rules are imposed on us slowly enough, we don’t even notice. If control is taken away in a certain pattern and at a slow-enough pace, it is invisible to us.

当界限事先设定好，或者被解释为行业惯例时，我们通常不会质疑。但当有人突然强加给我们看似武断的限制时，我们会抗拒。如果你想改变规则，没问题——你只需要循序渐进，慢慢来，让你的买家察觉不到。实验心理学家用“变化盲视”、“选择检测”或“闪烁范式”等名称来描述这种现象。无论你怎么称呼它，无数研究表明，如果规则的实施足够缓慢，我们甚至不会察觉。如果控制权以某种模式、以足够缓慢的速度被剥夺，我们根本察觉不到。

So when it’s time to let buyers talk about the ideas you’ve presented and consider the implications for themselves, it’s important that they feel unhindered and able to steer the conversation in any direction they want. At the same time, you need to set invisible boundaries that contain their questions within a certain area. But you have to do this gradually so that the buyer doesn’t feel constrained by you.

因此，当需要让买家讨论你提出的想法并思考其对自身的影响时，重要的是让他们感到不受阻碍，能够自由地引导谈话朝着他们想要的方向发展。同时，你需要设定一些无形的界限，将他们的问题限制在一定的范围内。但你必须循序渐进地进行，以免买家感到受到你的限制。

My team and I have discovered how to impose boundaries on your buyer before you turn the conversation over to them to talk about whatever they want. If you do this in just the right way, they won’t notice any limitation at all. Then, when you grant them autonomy, they’ll stick to the areas you’ve already outlined and will not deviate.

我和我的团队发现了一种在将对话交给买家之前，先为他们设定界限的方法。如果方法得当，他们根本不会察觉到任何限制。这样，当你赋予他们自主权时，他们就会严格遵守你事先设定的范围，不会偏离。

Why would a buyer accept conversational boundaries that are imposed by you? Well, of course, you aren’t going to make it quite so obvious. You aren’t going to just come right out and tell the buyer that you’d like them to avoid certain topics. If you did that, they wouldn’t be able to think of anything but the off-limits areas; you will have created a Do Not Touch button that everyone will immediately reach for.

买家为什么要接受你设定的谈话界限呢？当然，你不会直接这么做。你不会直接告诉买家你希望他们避免谈论某些话题。如果你那样做，他们满脑子想的就只有那些禁区；你相当于设置了一个“请勿触碰”按钮，每个人都会立刻按下去。

Instead, we need a more subtle way to impose boundaries.

相反，我们需要一种更巧妙的方式来划定界限。

THE BUYER’S FORMULA

买方公式

In my deals, I use a seven-step Buyer’s Formula to lay down “do not cross” lines. It’s important to understand that not every fact, item, subject, and issue a buyer wants to talk about is worth discussing. For example, let’s say he found another person who offers a much lower price than you. Well, that’s great; he should go buy from them. I say this because nearly every professional salesperson I know refuses to have a price held over their head in a negotiation. Most of the time price is the least important part of the deal, because it’s the terms of the deal that really matter like financing, delivery timeline, and length of contract. And have you ever heard a potential buyer say, “Of course, I can’t make a decision now because I’ll have to convince my partner first”? OK, but why should I present my offer, negotiate the terms, and bargain in good faith knowing there’s a shadowy partner out there whom I haven’t met, am not going to talk to, and don’t know anything about, or who may not even exist? In the final analysis, every buyer wants to discuss and debate a wide range of topics, most of which are time wasters and don’t help anyone get to a decision. But we can’t ignore the buyer completely, and we do have to give them the opportunity for open discussion and debate—so it’s best to set up boundaries. In other words, set up the invisible fence to include the topics that matter. Anything outside the fence doesn’t matter.

在我的交易中，我使用一套七步买家法则来划定“不可逾越”的底线。重要的是要明白，并非买家想要谈论的每个事实、项目、主题和问题都值得讨论。例如，假设他找到了另一个出价远低于你的人。那很好；他应该从他们那里购买。我这么说是因为我认识的几乎所有专业销售人员都拒绝在谈判中被价格所束缚。大多数情况下，价格是交易中最不重要的部分，因为真正重要的是交易条款，例如融资方式、交货时间和合同期限。你有没有听过潜在买家说：“当然，我现在不能做决定，因为我得先说服我的合伙人”？好吧，但是，既然我知道有一个我从未见过、也不会与之交谈、甚至可能根本不存在的神秘合伙人，我为什么要提交我的报价、协商条款并真诚地讨价还价呢？归根结底，每个买家都想讨论各种各样的话题，但其中大多数都是浪费时间，对做出决定毫无帮助。我们不能完全忽视买家，必须给他们公开讨论和辩论的机会——所以最好设定一些界限。换句话说，设置一道无形的围栏，把真正重要的话题圈在内。围栏之外的内容无关紧要。

At the end of my presentation, when it’s time to decide on next steps, I don’t ask for the sale. Instead, I reaffirm my status as an independent expert, and then I set up the invisible fence. How? I teach the buyer how to evaluate whether my deal is right for them. Then, when I’m done, the deal naturally comes together.

在我的演示结束时，当需要决定下一步行动时，我不会直接提出成交。相反，我会重申我作为独立专家的身份，然后设置一道无形的屏障。具体做法是：我会指导买家如何评估我的方案是否适合他们。之后，当我完成演示后，交易自然而然就会达成。

1. Introduce the Buyer’s Formula

1. 介绍买方公式

To start, I’ll say something like, “I deal with this kind of thing all the time. Let me try and help.”

首先，我会说类似这样的话：“我经常处理这类事情。让我来帮帮你吧。”

As an example, consider walking into a bike shop looking to get a solid bicycle for some light weekend mountain biking. The bike mechanic who helps you out will say something like, “Look, I’ve helped a thousand people buy a mountain bike. Let me tell you what I’ve found works best for a weekend warrior.” Statements like “I’ve done this a thousand times” always reinforce one’s status as an independent expert.

举个例子，假设你走进一家自行车店，想买一辆结实耐用的自行车，准备周末进行一些轻松的山地骑行。接待你的自行车技师可能会说：“听着，我帮过上千人买过山地车了。让我告诉你，我发现哪种最适合周末骑行爱好者。” 诸如此类的“我做过上千次了”的说法，总是能强化自己作为独立专家的地位。

2. Outline Obvious Ways to Fail

2. 列出显而易见的失败方式

Next, start to create boundaries that your buyer will not venture outside of, by highlighting the obvious ways to fail.

接下来，通过强调明显的失败方式，开始设定买家不会越过的界限。

The bike mechanic might say, “Most amateur athletes who are just getting into trail riding will assume price is a way to measure the quality of a bike. In reality, higher price just means it’s more specialized for one certain type of riding—and useless for others. So don’t go by price. And don’t buy the frame online because it’s a mess out there on the internet: a fifty-four Trek is a fifty-two in Shimano and is a fifty-six in Colnago—nothing matches up from one brand to the next! There are no real standards in this industry like you might have with terabytes for a hard drive, miles per gallon for a car, or percent interest on a loan. With a bike, you sit on it, pedal a few times, and get the feel of it. And you have someone like me standing by so you don’t make an obvious wrong choice.”

自行车技师可能会说：“大多数刚开始骑山地车的业余爱好者都会认为价格是衡量自行车质量的标准。但实际上，价格高仅仅意味着它更适合某种特定的骑行方式，而对其他骑行方式则毫无用处。所以，不要只看价格。也不要在网上买车架，因为网上的信息五花八门：54寸的Trek车架，在Shimano系统下可能是52寸，在Colnago系统下可能是56寸——不同品牌之间根本没有统一的标准！这个行业不像硬盘容量（TB）、汽车油耗（英里/加仑）或贷款利率那样有明确的标准。买自行车，你坐上去，骑几下，感受一下。而且，像我这样的人会在旁边指导你，避免你做出明显的错误选择。”

3. Highlight Counterintuitive Ways to Fail

3. 强调反直觉的失败方式

From there, you should move on to the less obvious, or counterintuitive, ways to fail. These are traps that most people fall into, things that your buyer surely believes he already knows, but really he doesn’t. You are going to expertly point a few of these out and teach your buyer at least one valuable insight.

接下来，你应该着手讲解那些不太明显或违反直觉的失败方式。这些是大多数人都会掉入的陷阱，你的买家可能自认为已经了解，但实际上并非如此。你要巧妙地指出其中的一些陷阱，并至少教会买家一个有价值的见解。

The mechanic could say, “When you check the bikes out, it’s going to seem like carbon fiber and Kevlar are incredibly cool and the right way to go, high tech is best, right? Wrong. Unless you’re a pro, those materials are just too fragile. You drop it once, it cracks, and the bike is toast. Sexy materials only benefit riders trying to shave two seconds off a Tour de France time trial. But helmets are exactly the opposite of frames. For helmets, the more expensive they are, the more exotic the material, the safer and higher quality they will be.”

技师可能会说：“当你检查自行车时，你会觉得碳纤维和凯夫拉纤维酷炫无比，是最佳选择，高科技就是最好的，对吧？错！除非你是职业车手，否则这些材料太脆弱了。摔一下就裂，车就报废了。那些花哨的材料只对那些想在环法计时赛中节省两秒的车手有用。但头盔的情况恰恰相反。对于头盔来说，越贵，材料越稀有，安全性和质量就越高。”

Once you’ve shown your buyer five or six things that can easily go wrong in his decision (starting with the obvious and moving to the less obvious), it’s time to shift into the positive actions he can take, so he feels he’s in control and is making informed choices.

当你向买家展示了他在做决定时容易出错的五六件事（从显而易见的开始，逐步过渡到不太明显的），就该转向他可以采取的积极行动，让他感到自己能够掌控局面，并做出明智的选择。

4. List Obvious Actions

4. 列出显而易见的行动

Now you can tell your buyer what actions he should take to get started. Again, start with a few no-brainers, or things your buyer already knows in the back of his mind and will definitely agree with.

现在你可以告诉买家他应该采取哪些行动来开始。同样，先从一些显而易见的事情开始，或者说是买家心里已经知道并且肯定会同意的事情。

“Obviously, you want to remember the bike is only seventy percent of the total cost,” the mechanic would continue. “You’ll need another six hundred dollars for helmet, pedals, shoes, gloves, and gear, so leave some cash in your pocket. I’d say don’t spend more than twenty-five hundred bucks for your first bike—total, for everything, then blow another six hundred on gear.”

“显然，你要记住自行车只占总成本的百分之七十，”技工继续说道，“你还需要六百美元买头盔、脚踏、鞋子、手套和装备，所以最好留点现金。我的建议是，你的第一辆自行车——包括所有东西——的总花费不要超过两千五百美元，然后再花六百美元买装备。”

5. Less Obvious “Hacks”

5. 不太明显的“黑客”手段

Then move into the less obvious tips and insights, or the “hacks” (these are the things you would only figure out by doing it at least 100 times).

然后，我们来看看一些不太明显的技巧和见解，或者说是“秘诀”（这些技巧你至少要做 100 次才能领悟）。

“What I’d do,” the bike mechanic says, “is start with basic Shimano 105 components. They’re great, that’s what I ride. You won’t need anything more than that for now. Get yourself a cheap Trek or Giant frame, all metal, a solid helmet like Giro Vanquish MIPS, and some high-quality shoes—SIDI Defender’s will work. Then, if you’re going to be riding more than ten miles a week, definitely spend a few bucks on a comfortable seat—go for the Eron, it’s bombproof. Trust me on the seat. After you get a hundred plus rides in on this bike, sell it and upgrade to XTR components and then spend five thousand on something you love that will keep you happy for the next five years.”

“我的建议是，”自行车技师说，“先从基本的 Shimano 105 套件开始。它们很棒，我自己也骑这个。你现在不需要更高级的。买个便宜的 Trek 或 Giant 全金属车架，一个像 Giro Vanquish MIPS 那样结实的头盔，再配上一双高品质的骑行鞋——SIDI Defender 就不错。如果你每周骑行超过十英里，一定要花点钱买个舒服的车座——Eron 的就不错，非常耐用。相信我，车座很重要。等你骑这辆车超过一百英里后，就把它卖掉，升级到 XTR 套件，然后花五千美元买一辆你真正喜欢的、能让你在未来五年都满意的车。”

6. Hand Over Autonomy

6. 交接自主权

Finally, hand over autonomy with a shrug and a line that detaches you from the outcome, like, “Yeah, well, that’s just what I’d do, having done it at least a hundred times already. I’m not the boss of you. You can do whatever you want.”

最后，耸耸肩，用一句让你感觉与结果无关的话，把自主权交出去，比如：“是啊，我就是这么做的，我已经这么做过至少一百次了。我不是你的老板。你想做什么就做什么。”

If you’ve done everything right, the buyer will enter a stage of pessimism and will start seriously considering the positives and negatives of your deal and asking questions—but it’s more likely those questions will all stay within the boundaries you set up in your Buyer’s Formula.

如果你做的一切都正确，买家就会进入悲观阶段，开始认真考虑这笔交易的利弊并提出问题——但更有可能的是，这些问题都会留在你在买家公式中设定的范围内。

7. Redirect to Keep the Buyer “In Bounds”

7. 重定向以确保买家“在范围内”

From time to time the buyer will venture outside the boundaries you have set and ask about something that you already said was a rookie mistake in your Buyer’s Formula. The better you get at delivering the formula, the less often you’ll have to field rogue questions, but here’s how to deal with them when they do come up.

买家有时会超出你设定的范围，问一些你已经在“买家公式”中明确指出是新手常犯的问题。你越熟练地运用“买家公式”，就越少会遇到这种莫名其妙的问题，但以下是如何应对这些问题的方法。

First, let the buyer fully object. Hear him out, then redirect firmly to stay within the boundaries you previously set. “People are always worried about that issue, and in the end, it’s never even an issue at all,” the bike mechanic would say. “There are twenty-five different things to worry about when you’re buying a bike, but there are really only five things that actually matter. Just focus on these five and everything will be perfect. Get distracted by the other twenty and you’ll waste time and money and end up with the wrong thing.”

首先，要让买家充分表达反对意见。认真听取他的意见，然后坚定地引导他回到你之前设定的界限内。“人们总是担心这个问题，但最终，它根本就不是问题，”自行车修理工可能会这样说。“买自行车时，你可能会担心二十五件事，但真正重要的只有五件。只要专注于这五件事，一切都会很完美。如果被其他二十件事分散了注意力，你只会浪费时间和金钱，最终买到不合适的车。”

With the formula, the bike shop mechanic has boiled down and shared with you ten years of bike-buying experience. But what if the buyer doesn’t want to follow the suggested formula? The answer is simple: He doesn’t want to follow an expert’s opinion; he’s a do-it-yourselfer and thinks he knows everything from a few internet searches, he will be a pain in the butt for the bike shop the whole time, and the shop is going to lose money dealing with him and all the nitpicking, time-wasting concerns, and eventual complaints.

这位自行车店的技师将他十年的购车经验总结成一套公式，并分享给了你。但如果买家不想遵循这套公式呢？答案很简单：他不想听取专家的意见；他是个喜欢自己动手的人，觉得只要上网查几下就能什么都懂，他会一直给自行车店添麻烦，而且店里也会因为他的各种挑剔、浪费时间以及最终的投诉而损失金钱。

I’ve seen this a thousand times too. If the buyer won’t respect your expert status and your Buyer’s Formula, he’s never going to be a good customer, partner, or investor. Start backing away from him.

我也见过太多这样的例子了。如果买家不尊重你的专家地位和你的“买家法则”，他永远不会成为你的好客户、好合作伙伴或好投资者。赶紧远离他吧。

But once your buyer has the Buyer’s Formula and does accept your expert status, you have laid an invisible fence. Now you can safely step back and provide autonomy.

但是，一旦你的买家掌握了“买家公式”，并认可了你的专家地位，你就设置了一道无形的屏障。现在，你可以安心地退后一步，给予他们自主权。

As I’ve said previously, don’t beat down every objection or discourage pessimism. Entertain the objections. Welcome the pessimism. Acknowledge the downside of what you offer. Some valid objections will come up in any proposal, and telling your buyer otherwise and shooting down every one of his objections will signal to him that you are being less than authentic, or worse, needy (and difficult to work with).

正如我之前所说，不要一概否定所有反对意见，也不要打击悲观情绪。要认真对待这些反对意见，欣然接受悲观情绪，并承认你所提供方案的不足之处。任何方案都会遇到一些合理的反对意见，如果你否认这些意见，并逐一驳斥，只会让买家觉得你不够真诚，甚至更糟，显得你很需要客户（而且难以合作）。

It’s a good idea to bring to the surface the most obvious flaws in your plan before the buyer does, although most people try to avoid any mention of negatives. You should move in quickly and acknowledge the possibility of failure and the obvious negative features—or he will do so but at the most inconvenient time. Do all this and you will gain your buyer’s trust. When you embrace pessimism along with the buyer, he won’t feel pressured, and he will be the one to say, “Yes, I love it. What’s the best way to work together and get started?”

最好在买家发现之前就主动指出计划中最明显的缺陷，尽管大多数人都会尽量避免提及负面因素。你应该迅速行动，坦诚面对失败的可能性和显而易见的不足之处——否则他虽然也会指出，但往往是在最不方便的时候。这样做能赢得买家的信任。当你和买家一起坦然面对现实时，他不会感到压力，反而会主动说：“是的，我很喜欢。我们该如何合作，才能尽快开始呢？”

—

THAT’S HOW THE Buyer’s Formula works. It’s what I was about to teach Bulletz4Breakfast, the top sniper in the world, in order to recruit him to Zero Gravity’s Counter-Strike team and carry our deal to its rightful conclusion.

这就是买家公式的运作方式。我正准备把这套方法教给世界顶级狙击手 Bulletz4Breakfast，以便把他招入 Zero Gravity 的反恐精英战队，并最终促成这笔交易。

A BUYER’S FORMULA FOR LATE-CAREER ATHLETES

为职业生涯后期运动员制定的购买策略

Bulletz was curious about what I had to say. But he was already making a lot of money, was already a sought-after celebrity signature and playing on a good team. He was so good, in fact, he didn’t have to compete in the preliminary round because his team was already guaranteed a spot in the finals, which gave him some time to sneak away, meeting me in the hotel café as the first round of the tournament was starting. On our side, Anton was going to try and win the preliminary game without a sniper, keeping the slot open in hopes that we would find someone before the finals. Then we could register whoever we landed in the sniper position as a member of our team before game two.

布莱茨很想知道我要说什么。但他当时已经赚了很多钱，是炙手可热的明星签约选手，而且效力于一支强队。事实上，他实力太强了，根本不用参加预赛，因为他的队伍已经锁定了一个决赛席位。这让他有时间溜走，在锦标赛第一轮开始时，我们在酒店咖啡厅碰面。我们这边，安东打算在没有狙击手的情况下赢得预赛，这样就能空出一个位置，希望在决赛前找到合适的人选。然后，我们可以在第二轮比赛前，把找到的狙击手注册成我们队伍的一员。

When we sat down at the conference center Starbucks, Bulletz was barely paying attention, looking around at other small groups to see if there was a better meeting he could bounce out to. I needed a quick Status Tip-Off. “Listen,” I said, before he even uttered a word, “let’s give this situation a name: You’re a late-career athlete. Most late-career athletes melt down in the last year or two. It’s pretty sad because their last media appearance is not on ESPN celebrating a big win; it’s on TMZ revealing divorce, drugs, and disaster. I’ve helped late-career athletes avoid the dustbin of history in professional basketball, football, NASCAR, UFC, even surfing. What do you think I’m doing for Anton? How do you think a retired eSports athlete is still making millions of dollars? I put together the business model, tax strategy, marketing funnel, intellectual property licensing, financial controls, balance sheet, and investor base. I’m going to take his company public in the spring and he’ll make at least ten million. That situation has a name too—it’s called set for life. ”

我们在会议中心的星巴克坐下时，布莱茨心不在焉，四处张望其他小组，看看有没有更好的会议可以让他溜出去。我需要快速了解一下他的情况。 “听着，”我还没等他开口，就说道，“咱们给这种情况起个名字：你是个职业生涯末期的运动员。大多数职业生涯末期的运动员都会在最后一两年里崩溃。这很可悲，因为他们最后一次出现在媒体面前，不是在ESPN上庆祝一场重大胜利，而是在TMZ上爆料离婚、吸毒和各种丑闻。我帮助过很多职业生涯末期的运动员，在职业篮球、橄榄球、纳斯卡赛车、UFC，甚至冲浪领域，他们都避免了被历史遗忘。你觉得我为安东做了什么？你觉得一个退役的电竞选手是怎么赚到数百万美元的？我帮他制定了商业模式、税务策略、营销渠道、知识产权许可、财务控制、资产负债表和投资者基础。我打算今年春天让他的公司上市，他至少能赚到一千万美元。这种情况也有一个名字——叫做‘终身无忧’。”

“How’d he do all that?” Bulletz asked. He was intrigued. These were the exact things he was starting to care about in his own life.

“他是怎么做到的？”布莱茨问道。他很感兴趣。这些正是他开始在意的事情。

“First thing is, you can’t be seen as flipping from being the best sniper in the world to being a nobody . I don’t ever want to read how the great Bulletz faded away, lost his touch, and imploded. Think about Michael Jordan. Only thing people can remember about his retirement is that he switched to baseball but wasn’t very good, then went back to basketball but wasn’t very good there either. Or Brett Favre, the superstar Green Bay Packers quarterback, who moved to the Jets and then the Vikings in his last few seasons. Megastar to benchwarmer—it’s the wrong way to end an incredible career.

“首先，你不能让人觉得你从世界最佳狙击手变成了无名小卒。我永远不想看到伟大的布莱茨（Bulletz）如何黯然失色、失去状态、最终陨落。想想迈克尔·乔丹吧。人们对他退役的唯一印象就是他转战棒球，但表现平平；之后他又重返篮球，但同样表现不佳。还有布雷特·法弗，这位绿湾包装工队的超级巨星四分卫，在他职业生涯的最后几个赛季先后效力于喷气机队和维京人队。从巨星沦为板凳球员——这绝非结束辉煌职业生涯的最佳方式。”

“Right now you have to focus on just a few things that really matter, and ignore everything else,” I continued, jumping straight to my Buyer’s Formula. “Most important: You don’t ever want fans to feel sorry for you, or to pity you. Your name should inspire generations of athletes in every sport to play hard, play fair, and behave like a champion whether winning or losing. Inspiration, not pity—got it?” He nodded. I glanced down at my phone under the table to see how Zero Gravity and the team were doing. Things were absolutely not looking good. His men were easy targets without a sniper to provide cover fire.

“现在你只需要专注于几件真正重要的事情，其他的都不要管，”我继续说道，直接切入我的“买家秘诀”。“最重要的是：你绝对不想让粉丝同情你，或者怜悯你。你的名字应该激励一代又一代的运动员，无论输赢，都要全力以赴，公平竞争，展现冠军风范。激励，而不是怜悯——明白了吗？”他点点头。我低头看了看桌子底下的手机，看看“零重力”和他的团队的情况。情况非常不妙。没有狙击手提供火力掩护，他的队员们成了活靶子。

What I saw on my phone was not making me feel like much of a champion. The mobile app was incredible, and I could see live video of the game play and all the battle specs as easily as I could watch the evening news. Just three minutes into the main battle, our boys were already banged up. They were all low on health and losing ground fast.
