手机上的画面让我感觉自己一点也不像个冠军。手机应用确实很棒，我可以像看晚间新闻一样轻松地观看游戏的实时视频和所有战斗细节。主战场才打了三分钟，我们的队员就已经伤痕累累。他们的血量都很低，而且节节败退。

I tore myself away from the action and back to the conversation with Bulletz. He looked up from whatever he was doing on his phone to listen for a moment.

我从刚才的战斗中回过神来，重新投入到和布莱茨的谈话中。他从手机上抬起头，听了一会儿。

“A lot of retired athletes try to reinvent themselves, and switch to a totally new industry, like restaurants, car dealerships, home building, financial services,” I continued, “but it almost never works out. What does a retired basketball player, hockey player . . . or sniper . . . know about running a car dealership? Nothing. Which is my point. So it begs the question—where do old athletes get work? Yeah, you guessed it. Joe Namath put his name on Beautymist Pantyhose. That’s a true story. A better example, John Madden, video games; Tony Hawk, toy skateboards. But those are the lucky ones. Because if we’re being frank with each other, you aren’t John Madden or Tony Hawk. Most retired athletes end up doing color commentary for the local news on high school football or endorsing some shady bail bond company. So the rule here is, stick with what you know—no reinventing yourself; that is too risky. For you, it means you’re in eSports for the rest of your life. And why not? You love the game and you would be miserable selling salad dressing.”

“很多退役运动员都想转型，转行到全新的行业，比如餐饮、汽车经销、房屋建造、金融服务，”我继续说道，“但几乎从来都行不通。一个退役的篮球运动员、冰球运动员……或者狙击手……懂什么经营汽车经销店？一窍不通。这就是我的观点。所以问题来了——老运动员都去哪儿找工作？没错，你猜对了。乔·纳马斯把自己的名字印在了Beautymist连裤袜上。这是个真实的故事。更好的例子是，约翰·麦登代言电子游戏；托尼·霍克代言玩具滑板。但他们是幸运儿。因为说实话，你不是约翰·麦登，也不是托尼·霍克。大多数退役运动员最终只能在当地新闻里给高中橄榄球赛做解说，或者给一些来路不明的保释公司代言。所以，原则是，坚持你擅长的领域——不要转型；那风险太大了。对你来说，这意味着你这辈子都会从事电子竞技。为什么不呢？你热爱这款游戏，去卖沙拉酱会让你痛苦不堪。

“Yeah, I love the game. But how can I do that?” he asked. His body language was open and he had a thoughtful expression on his face, so I decided to stop focusing on the list of don’ts and instead push forward and reveal the positives, the things he could actually do.

“是啊，我喜欢这个游戏。但我该怎么做呢？”他问道。他的肢体语言很开放，脸上也带着沉思的表情，所以我决定不再纠结于那些禁忌，而是继续引导他，让他看到积极的一面，看到他真正能做的事情。

“Well, obviously you want to announce your retirement in advance, so it doesn’t look like you’re desperate. It’s a planned retirement. You are going out on top, on your own terms . And you also want to announce your new position in the eSports industry. But here’s the important piece: In what capacity? Announcer? Coach? Those jobs are second-string and pay next to nothing. You want to become a team owner. This lets you own something that will grow in value. This way you’ll have leverage in the future. That’s why I was so excited to share this deal with you. Because Anton wants you as a sniper now, but he also sees you as a partner and on the team for years and years. This is the only chance to negotiate hard. Come back in a few years after you’ve washed out—you’ll find out there are no offers out there for has-beens and bail bond salesmen.”

“显然，你想提前宣布退役，免得显得你很急于求成。这是计划好的退役。你要在巅峰时期，按照自己的意愿离开。你也想宣布你在电竞行业的新职位。但关键在于：担任什么职位？解说员？教练？这些工作都是二流的，收入微薄。你想成为战队老板。这样你就能拥有一份会增值的东西。这样你未来就有了谈判的筹码。这就是为什么我如此兴奋地和你分享这个机会。因为安东现在需要你担任狙击手，但他同时也把你视为合伙人，希望你能长期留在战队。这是你唯一一次可以全力谈判的机会。几年后，当你过气之后再回来——你会发现，市场上根本不会给过气选手和保释金推销员提供任何机会。”

The boundaries were set. It was time to invite pessimism. Otherwise it would just creep in later when I wasn’t around to assist in the decision making.

界限已定。是时候接纳悲观情绪了。否则，等我不在场参与决策时，它就会悄悄地溜进来。

“Anyway,” I said, shrugging, “that’s just what I would suggest after working with many other athletes in your position. But everyone’s career is different, and there are some very real risks to switching teams while you’re still active in the game. I absolutely understand that. I’m not the boss of you and can’t tell you what to do. Only you can decide what’s right. ” And then I stopped talking.

“总之，”我耸耸肩说，“这是我在和很多和你情况类似的运动员共事后给出的建议。但每个人的职业生涯都不一样，在职业生涯仍在继续的时候更换球队确实存在一些非常现实的风险。我完全理解这一点。我不是你的老板，不能告诉你该怎么做。只有你自己才能决定什么是正确的。”说完，我就没再说话了。

For a few painful moments, neither of us said a word. Bulletz was deep in thought. He looked back at his phone and I thought to myself, “These darn millennials are always distracted by something!” Then suddenly he jumped up, excusing himself for a moment to use the restroom. They also have small bladders.

尴尬的几秒钟里，我们俩一句话也没说。布莱茨陷入了沉思。他低头看了看手机，我心想：“这些该死的千禧一代总是被各种事情分心！” 突然，他猛地站起来，借口去洗手间。他们的膀胱也太小了吧。

While he was gone, I pulled out my phone again to check on the raging battle between Anton and the insurgents. The situation was worse than before. The video feed showed our machine gunner, Smith, lying prone in the courtyard, totally exposed to whoever was shooting at him. Bullets sparked all around him. But the kid was an iceberg. Ignoring the incoming 9 mm rounds, he shouldered his M249 squad automatic weapon (SAW) and tore off a blistering burst of return fire.

他离开的这段时间，我又拿出手机查看安东和叛军之间的激烈战斗。情况比之前更糟了。视频画面显示，我们的机枪手史密斯趴在院子里，完全暴露在敌人的枪口下。子弹在他周围飞溅。但这小子却像冰山一样。他无视飞来的9毫米子弹，扛起M249班用自动武器，猛烈地还击起来。

I could see on the screen that Anton peeked around the wall into the courtyard where the main fighting was taking place. “Give me another weapon system!” he screamed in frustration. “I need another 240 SAW!” Unable to see the enemy, Anton was going to die if he stayed in that doorway.

我从屏幕上看到安东从墙后探出头，往院子里看，那里正是战斗的主要战场。“再给我一套武器系统！”他沮丧地喊道，“我需要另一把240型SAW！”安东看不到敌人，如果他继续待在门口，肯定会死。

Outside, in the courtyard, Smith was hit and he did die. Dammit, he hadn’t taken down a single enemy! His screen turned to digital snow and he was out. It was the same story for Brown, Davis, and Miller, all out of the fight.

在外面的院子里，史密斯中弹身亡。该死，他一个敌人都没打倒！他的屏幕突然出现雪花，他倒下了。布朗、戴维斯和米勒的遭遇也一样，他们都退出了战斗。

This was the end of the road for our squad. We were pinned down, surrounded, and left with no other option than to jump into the narrow courtyard and face the firepower of their enemy’s tripod-mounted PKM and AK-47s head-on. We wouldn’t have much of a chance to survive that kind of firepower, but it was the only move we had.

我们小队已经走投无路了。我们被敌人压制，四面楚歌，别无选择，只能跳进狭窄的院子里，正面迎击敌人架在三脚架上的PKM和AK-47的火力。面对如此猛烈的火力，我们几乎没有生还的可能，但这却是我们唯一的选择。

A full five minutes had passed in game time. Anton “Zero Gravity” was out front, taking fire and low on health. Cooper, Murphy, and Jenkins were low on ammo. Just then, a string of 7.62 x 54 mm tracer rounds were blasting from above into the already chaotic firefight, blowing out the glass; someone was pouring high-caliber suppressing fire straight onto the other team’s position. Suppressing fire is the good kind of shooting that goes past you, straight into the enemy, pinning them down, and gives you a chance to move around. Suddenly, it was the other side, the red team, who was in trouble. Whoever was shooting from behind us had our enemies scrambling, abandoning their positions, ducking for cover. Two red team members went down in a splatter, and now . . . four were down. What the . . . ? For the moment, our enemies stopped firing at us. This was our chance to get out of the kill zone. Anton and team made a break into the courtyard and started unloading everything we had in the enemy’s direction. Now five of red team were down. Another one killed by our team made six. On our side, Anton was hit as he scrambled through the courtyard, but still alive.

游戏时间已经过去了整整五分钟。安东“零重力”冲在最前面，承受着枪林弹雨，生命值也所剩无几。库珀、墨菲和詹金斯的弹药也所剩无几。就在这时，一连串7.62×54毫米曳光弹从上方呼啸而下，冲进了原本就混乱的交火中，震碎了玻璃；有人正用高口径火力压制对方阵地。压制射击是一种有效的射击方式，子弹会从你身边掠过，直接射向敌人，将他们压制住，让你有机会移动。突然间，情况变成了对方，也就是红队，陷入了困境。不知是谁从我们身后开火，敌人顿时慌了神，纷纷放弃阵地，寻找掩体。两名红队队员应声倒地，现在……已经倒下了四人。这……怎么回事？敌人暂时停止了射击。这是我们逃离杀伤区的绝佳机会。安东和他的队友冲进院子，开始把我们所有的物资都倾泻到敌人身上。现在红队五人倒下了。我们队又击毙一人，红队六人全部阵亡。安东在院子里四处逃窜时被击中，但还活着。

A blizzard of metal and glass fragments exploded next to the last red team insurgent, who was running for cover, and I followed the red tracer fire backward to its point of origin on the screen. Behind Anton, about two hundred feet back, up on a neighboring rooftop, I could now make out the form of a sniper barrel clicking off high-impact 7.62 rounds and taking out the red team insurgents methodically, accurately, with one impossible shot after the next.

一阵金属和玻璃碎片如暴风雪般在最后一名正试图寻找掩体的红队叛乱分子身旁爆炸，我循着屏幕上的红色曳光弹回溯到它的源头。在安东身后大约两百英尺远的邻近屋顶上，我隐约看到一支狙击步枪的枪管，它正咔哒咔哒地发射着高威力的7.62毫米子弹，有条不紊、精准无比地一枪又一枪地击毙着红队叛乱分子，简直不可思议。

At that moment I knew we were going to make it to the next round in the tournament and probably win the whole thing—Bulletz had joined the fight, and the team.

那一刻我知道我们肯定能晋级下一轮比赛，甚至可能赢得整个冠军——Bulletz 加入了战斗，加入了球队。

#↩

CHAPTER 7

第七章

How to Be Compelling

如何才能引人入胜

I love speed. Speed is a lifestyle. Cars, trucks, motorcycles, you name it—there’s something profound and thrilling about being so close to a road, pushing the man-machine limit. I’ve blazed through back roads and open roads, fast lanes and country lanes, lonesome roads, happy trails, and highways to hell. By the time I was in my late twenties, I’d stockpiled Porsches, muscle cars, and about fifty motorcycles. Cars are good. Motorcycles are better.

我热爱速度。速度是一种生活方式。汽车、卡车、摩托车，等等——与道路如此紧密地贴合，挑战人机极限，这种感觉既深刻又刺激。我曾驰骋于乡间小路和开阔公路，穿梭于高速公路和乡村小道，走过寂静的道路、快乐的小径，也走过通往地狱的高速公路。到了二十七八岁的时候，我已经拥有了保时捷、肌肉车和大约五十辆摩托车。汽车不错，但摩托车更胜一筹。

Nearly all my motorcycles came from the same dealer—Elias, the coolest ride captain who ever carved a canyon. Elias didn’t just sell motorcycles, he was motorcycles. From his all-Japan racing jacket to his series of smoking hot girlfriends covered in anime tattoos to his twenty-mile stare that pierced through any roadblock, Elias screamed speed. He graduated from the University of Motorcycles and he just looks fast, even when he’s standing still. But more than being good-looking and popular, below the surface he’s imaginative, perceptive, and two steps ahead of everyone else. A guy like this was irresistible to an axle addict like me.

我的摩托车几乎都来自同一个经销商——伊莱亚斯，他是史上最酷的骑行队长，驰骋峡谷如飞。伊莱亚斯不只是卖摩托车，他本身就是摩托车的化身。从他那件全日本产的赛车夹克，到他身边那些浑身动漫纹身的性感女友，再到他那能穿透一切障碍的目光，伊莱亚斯浑身上下都散发着速度的气息。他毕业于摩托车大学，即使静止不动，也给人一种速度感。但他的魅力远不止于外表和人缘，他的内心充满想象力，洞察力敏锐，总是能先人一步。像他这样的人，对我这样的摩托车狂热爱好者来说，简直无法抗拒。

Elias had a hardscrabble upbringing in San Jose, California. He owed his mastery of motorcycles to an errant childhood and an insightful cop who urged him to ease his adolescent angst on the racetrack. He was fast and when it came to winning a race, he was the real deal.

埃利亚斯在加州圣何塞的贫寒家庭长大。他精湛的摩托车技艺要归功于一段放荡不羁的童年，以及一位富有洞察力的警察，这位警察鼓励他通过赛道来排解青春期的烦恼。他速度很快，而且在比赛中，他绝对是冠军的有力争夺者。

He owned a successful boutique motorcycle dealership in West Hollywood, which was, like him, the height of cool. You needed to be a millionaire to get in the door. To get back out, you’d leave with a lot less. I loved hanging out with Elias and his posse, drinking tequila and talking bikes. We’d go out for sushi, and except for me, everybody looked like the bass player from Scorpions—especially the actual Scorpions bass player, who would join us whenever he was in town. The guest roster included Gucci models, Nicolas Cage, and world champion racer John Kocinski, and I was the finance guy (read: the nerd who paid for everyone’s drinks). Just to fit in and hang out with these dudes, I bought the actual Camaro from the Metallica video for “I Disappear.” But still, they’d all shake their heads, point to me, and ask Elias, “Who’s the suit?” Even with ripped jeans and a 1968 Camaro, I looked corporate.

他在西好莱坞拥有一家生意兴隆的精品摩托车经销店，和他本人一样，这家店也是酷炫的代名词。想进店，你得是个百万富翁。想出来，你可就损失惨重了。我喜欢和伊莱亚斯以及他的一帮朋友混在一起，喝着龙舌兰，聊着摩托车。我们经常一起去吃寿司，除了我以外，每个人看起来都像蝎子乐队的贝斯手——尤其是真正的蝎子乐队贝斯手，他每次来城里都会加入我们。我们的客人名单里有古驰的模特、尼古拉斯·凯奇，还有世界冠军赛车手约翰·科辛斯基，而我则是负责财务的（说白了就是那个负责请大家喝酒的书呆子）。为了融入他们，和这些家伙们一起玩，我甚至买了一辆Metallica乐队《I Disappear》MV里出现的那辆雪佛兰Camaro。即便如此，他们还是会摇摇头，指着我问伊莱亚斯：“谁穿西装？” 即使穿着破洞牛仔裤，开着1968年的Camaro，我看起来也像个公司高管。

I may have been utterly uncool next to these guys but I didn’t mind. I was just happy and grateful to be invited into the real Hollywood Hills and its loud, exciting, reckless world of motorcycle racers, models, and rock stars. I was riding high. It was over one of these sushi dinners that Elias and I started talking about going into business together.

和这些人相比，我可能显得格格不入，但我并不在意。我很高兴也很感激能被邀请进入真正的好莱坞山，体验那里喧闹、刺激、又充满摩托车赛车手、模特和摇滚明星的世界。我当时兴奋极了。正是在一次寿司晚餐上，我和伊莱亚斯开始讨论合伙做生意的事。

“I’d like to scale the business,” he said with his characteristic unaffected directness. “I was thinking about starting an apparel line. You know, Hollywood Hills meets Formula 1. Von Dutch for speed. A true speed lifestyle company. What do you say, Oren? Let’s do this together and have some fun.”

“我想扩大业务规模，”他用他一贯坦率真诚的语气说道。“我正在考虑推出一个服装系列。你知道，好莱坞山庄遇上F1赛车。Von Dutch代表速度。打造一个真正的速度生活方式品牌。怎么样，奥伦？咱们一起做，好好玩玩。”

“Of course. I’d love to,” I said breathlessly, because that’s just what happens if you’re a guy like me being offered the opportunity to go into the speed business with a titanium piston god.

“当然，我非常乐意，”我气喘吁吁地说，因为如果你像我一样，有机会与钛合金活塞之神一起进入速度行业，就会发生这样的事。

Elias ended up being a piston god who could sell like a demon . What a natural. Our company never had sales meetings or pipeline reports, and we never gave a thought to any kind of sales methods because, well, we had the Elias method. He knew everything about speed. Ferrari street special? Ducati race bike? Porsche Le Mans winner? He could tell you what it was worth and why, and follow up with two stories about it, one involving some wild engineering facts and the other involving two alcohol-fueled nights in the seedy part of Monte Carlo. Elias’s stories sold vehicles, and these sales were worth millions to our business.

埃利亚斯最终成了销售界的“活塞之神”，销售能力更是惊人。他简直就是个天生的销售高手。我们公司从来不开销售会议，也不做销售报告，更别提什么销售方法了，因为，我们有埃利亚斯的方法。他对速度了如指掌。法拉利街车？杜卡迪赛车？保时捷勒芒冠军？他能告诉你它的价值和原因，还能接着讲两个相关的故事：一个是关于一些匪夷所思的工程技术，另一个则是关于他在蒙特卡洛夜店里两个醉醺醺的夜晚。埃利亚斯的故事能把车卖出去，而这些销售额为我们公司带来了数百万美元。

As fantastic as the stories were, you never questioned them, because they were also grounded in fascinating facts. Elias had a vast working knowledge of his industry and his products, which he bought and sold like pieces of art. And he wouldn’t sell to just anybody. If you wanted to buy a motorcycle from him—or a motorcycle part, for that matter—you had to convince him to sell it to you.

那些故事虽然精彩绝伦，但你从不质疑，因为它们都建立在引人入胜的事实之上。埃利亚斯对他的行业和产品了如指掌，他买卖这些东西就像买卖艺术品一样。而且他不会随便把东西卖给任何人。如果你想从他那里买一辆摩托车——或者摩托车零件——你必须说服他卖给你。

But in order to generate the extra revenue we needed to get the apparel line off the ground, Elias and I determined that we’d have to dramatically ramp up the number of motorcycles we were selling. Until now, his business model had been simple: Import exotic motorcycles from Italy and Japan and sell them to rich guys in Beverly Hills. Through Elias’s reputation and personal magnetism, sales happened like magic.

但为了获得启动服装系列所需的额外收入，我和埃利亚斯决定必须大幅提高摩托车的销量。此前，他的商业模式很简单：从意大利和日本进口稀有摩托车，然后卖给比佛利山庄的富豪们。凭借埃利亚斯的名声和个人魅力，销量简直像变魔术一样火爆。

Now that we were in business together, I had to figure out how to scale our operations to meet our new sales targets. We needed to sell our motorcycles to buyers beyond Beverly Hills, in a way that wasn’t dependent on Elias’s natural in-person sales talent. In order to ship faster to both coasts, we decided to open our next facility in Devils Lake, North Dakota. Elias had gotten a killer deal on this warehouse out there, but of course he couldn’t leave Beverly Hills because we needed him to sell the fancy bikes that supported the whole operation. And there was no way I was moving to North Dakota because, well, I was doing just fine, living on Sunset Boulevard, one block from the Whisky a Go Go.

既然我们已经合伙做生意了，我就得想办法扩大运营规模，以达到新的销售目标。我们需要把摩托车卖给比佛利山庄以外的买家，而且不能再依赖伊莱亚斯天生的销售才能。为了更快地把货运到东西海岸，我们决定在北达科他州的魔鬼湖开设下一个仓库。伊莱亚斯在那里以非常优惠的价格租下了一个仓库，但他当然不能离开比佛利山庄，因为我们需要他来销售那些支撑整个运营的高档摩托车。而我，也绝对不可能搬到北达科他州去，因为，嗯，我当时过得挺好的，住在日落大道上，离威士忌酒吧（Whisky a Go Go）只有一个街区。

So we had to hire a local North Dakota sales staff—and that’s where our problems started. We needed to figure out how to teach our people from North Dakota to sell like Elias. We had to make them compelling. This meant I was headed to Devil’s Lake to train the team.

所以我们必须在北达科他州当地招聘销售人员——而这正是我们问题的开始。我们需要想办法教会这些北达科他州的员工像伊莱亚斯那样销售。我们必须让他们充满销售热情。这意味着我要前往魔鬼湖培训团队。

My task? Turn this frozen warehouse in the middle of the country into a high-powered sales office for Italian auto parts. “No problem,” I thought to myself smugly. “What could possibly go wrong?” At that point in my career, I’d sold everything from accounting software to brain aneurysm coils. I’d launched a genetic data company, I could explain in detail how to inject your knee with ortho-guided synovial fluid, and I could chart the subdomains on the dark web where stolen financial data is stored.

我的任务？把这个位于国土中央的冰冷仓库改造成意大利汽车零部件的高效销售中心。“没问题，”我得意地想，“能出什么岔子呢？”那时，我的职业生涯可谓是包罗万象，从会计软件到脑动脉瘤栓塞线圈，我都卖过。我创办过一家基因数据公司，能详细讲解如何给膝盖注射骨科引导滑液，还能绘制出暗网上存储被盗金融数据的子域名。

So seriously, how hard could it possibly be to sell a few Ducati parts?

说真的，卖几个杜卡迪零件能有多难？

As I was about to discover, it was pretty damn hard, because, it turned out, if Elias was the living embodiment of sexiness and speed, this North Dakota sales team was the embodiment of . . . ice.

正如我即将发现的那样，这非常困难，因为事实证明，如果说伊莱亚斯是性感和速度的化身，那么这支北达科他州的销售团队就是……冰冷的化身。

REVERSE ENGINEERING THE ART OF COMPELLINGNESS

逆向工程破解引人入胜的艺术

What does it even mean to be compelled ? In its most basic form, it’s that feeling of being unable to look away from something or someone. It can feel like being caught in a trance or placed under a spell, and it can lead you to a sudden insight in a way that opens the door to Inception. But what is it that actually makes one person more compelling than another?

究竟什么是“被吸引”？最基本的理解是，它指的是一种无法将目光从某人或某事上移开的感觉。这种感觉就像陷入了某种恍惚状态或中了某种魔法，它能让你突然顿悟，如同打开了《盗梦空间》的大门。但究竟是什么让一个人比另一个人更具吸引力呢？

Sure, most of us can easily recognize the basics of a compelling individual: a winning smile, a great sense of humor, an attractive physique, a keen intelligence. Personal charisma is a patchwork of complex and sophisticated social and emotional skills that allow charismatic individuals to affect and influence others without pushing, forcing, or even persuading.

当然，我们大多数人都能轻易识别出魅力人士的基本特质：迷人的微笑、幽默感、健美的体魄和敏锐的智慧。个人魅力是一系列复杂而精妙的社交和情感技巧的综合体现，它使魅力人士能够在不强迫、不劝说，甚至不强迫的情况下影响他人。

I used to think a compelling person was made up of three elements: appearance, intelligence, and enthusiasm. And then I tried backing this up with research, only to find that, while those traits certainly make someone likable, enthusiasm doesn’t contribute to compellingness at all , and it can even cause salespeople to inadvertently scare away customers.

我以前认为一个有魅力的人由三个要素构成：外貌、智慧和热情。后来我试图通过研究来佐证我的观点，结果却发现，虽然这些特质确实能让人讨人喜欢，但热情对魅力却毫无帮助，甚至会让销售人员无意中吓跑顾客。

If enthusiasm isn’t the secret to compellingness, then maybe it’s sex appeal.

如果热情不是吸引人的秘诀，那么或许性感才是。

No, it’s not that either. My research quickly revealed that physical attractiveness isn’t going to move the needle very far in business, politics, or dealmaking. Kim Jong Un, for instance, is decidedly not sexy by our Western standards. You’d have to search far into some weird subcultures to find someone who wants to swipe right for Mr. Un. Despite that, with his finger over the nuke launch button, he is incredibly compelling and a regular feature at the top of the news cycle.

不，也不是那样。我的调查很快发现，外表吸引力在商业、政治或交易中并不能起到多大作用。例如，按照我们西方的标准来看，金正恩绝对称不上性感。你得深入一些奇特的亚文化群体才能找到有人会想在交友软件上给金正恩点赞。尽管如此，他仍然拥有强大的影响力，经常占据新闻头条。

But what about intelligence? That was the last element I looked at, and I was sure it would hold the key. Surely smarter people would be seen as more competent and trustworthy and this would lead others to find them more compelling. But did this theory hold up to research? Not at all. In fact, the smartest people in the world can often put you to sleep the fastest.

但智力呢？这是我最后考虑的因素，我确信它会是关键。聪明的人理应被认为更有能力、更值得信赖，这自然会让其他人觉得他们更有魅力。但这个理论经得起研究的检验吗？完全不是。事实上，世界上最聪明的人往往最容易让人昏昏欲睡。

Take Harry Markopolos, a brilliant quantitative financial specialist with an instinct for the numbers behind complex derivatives. He smelled a rat in the workings of Bernie Madoff Investment Securities as far back as 1999, spotting Madoff’s $65 billion Ponzi scheme years before it came to light. Markopolos lived in fear for his life, spending everything he had trying to convince the world (and the Securities and Exchange Commission) the fraud actually existed. He contacted politicians and badgered journalists to write about Madoff. He even presented the SEC with a detailed dossier in 2005 bluntly titled “The World’s Largest Hedge Fund Is a Fraud.”

以哈里·马科波洛斯为例，他是一位才华横溢的量化金融专家，对复杂衍生品背后的数字有着敏锐的洞察力。早在1999年，他就嗅到了伯纳德·麦道夫投资证券公司运作中的猫腻，在麦道夫650亿美元的庞氏骗局曝光数年前就发现了端倪。马科波洛斯当时生活在恐惧之中，倾尽所有试图说服世人（包括美国证券交易委员会）相信这场骗局的存在。他联系政界人士，并不断敦促记者报道麦道夫的丑闻。2005年，他甚至向美国证券交易委员会提交了一份题为《世界最大对冲基金是个骗局》的详细档案。

So why didn’t anyone pay attention?

那么，为什么没有人注意到呢？

Markopolos should have been extremely compelling to the government, the media, and other investment funds: He was intelligent, had the story of the century, and was screaming through a giant megaphone. Still, nobody found him worth paying much attention to. He wasn’t able to get his idea across when it mattered most. Though he’s brilliant and well-spoken, he lacked something.

马尔科波洛斯本应极具吸引力，能够打动政府、媒体和其他投资基金：他才智过人，掌握着世纪故事，而且拥有强大的宣传能力。然而，却无人问津。在最关键的时刻，他未能成功传达自己的理念。尽管他才华横溢、口才出众，但他似乎缺少了某种东西。

So what sets aside the most compelling people from the rest of us who are “merely” likable, smart, and enthusiastic? It seems impossible to pin down something specific that the rest of us could copy. We can’t all be movie stars, win the Super Bowl, or control a nuclear missile site. I combed through the data and research articles and conducted interviews, but it seemed there was no one who had really tackled this to my satisfaction. So I kept at it, looking for a replicable formula.

那么，究竟是什么让那些最具魅力的人与我们这些“仅仅”讨人喜欢、聪明热情的人区分开来呢？似乎很难找到一些我们其他人可以效仿的具体方法。我们不可能都成为电影明星、赢得超级碗，或者掌控核导弹发射井。我仔细查阅了数据和研究文章，也进行了采访，但似乎没有人真正让我满意地解答过这个问题。所以我继续努力，寻找可复制的成功模式。

And then I had a breakthrough. I eventually figured out how to be compelling by first figuring out how not to be compelling.

然后我有了突破。我最终找到了如何变得有吸引力的方法，而这首先要弄清楚如何才能不具吸引力。

Over the years, I’ve boiled all my research down into a method to skyrocket your ability to be compelling. Unfortunately, I hadn’t discovered any of this yet when I woke up flat on my back on a sheet of ice in Devils Lake, North Dakota.

多年来，我将所有研究成果提炼成一套方法，能大幅提升你的说服力。可惜的是，当我醒来发现自己仰面躺在北达科他州魔鬼湖的冰面上时，我对这一切都一无所知。

MEETING THE TEAM—AT 20 BELOW

与团队见面——在零下20度

I could not feel my left leg. A searing pain was pressing into my neck. My right arm was numb and my ears were ringing. I turned to the side and slowly opened my eyes. The snow was turning to reddish-brown slush under my head. “I must be bleeding,” I thought, trying to remember what had just happened.

我的左腿麻木了。脖子上传来一阵剧痛。右臂麻木，耳朵嗡嗡作响。我侧过身，缓缓睁开眼睛。头下的雪正在变成红褐色的泥浆。“我一定是流血了，”我心想，努力回忆刚才发生了什么。

If you had to pick a place on the map that was the exact polar—and I do mean polar —opposite of my home in Beverly Hills, there’s a good chance you’d choose Devils Lake.

如果你必须在地图上选择一个与我在比佛利山庄的家完全相反的地方——我指的是完全相反的方向——你很可能会选择魔鬼湖。

First of all, it’s always cold there, unless it’s blisteringly hot. Today it was minus 20.

首先，那里总是很冷，除非天气酷热难耐。今天气温是零下20度。

A thermal glove materialized in front of my eyes. “Here, boss,” said Big Danny, the lead supervisor of the warehouse. “Take my hand. You stay down any longer, your head’s gonna freeze to the pavement. Probably have to cut your hair to get you up then. I’ve seen it happen.”

一只保暖手套突然出现在我眼前。“来，老大，”仓库主管大丹尼说道，“抓住我的手。你再趴着，脑袋就要冻在地上了。到时候可能得剪掉你的头发才能把你弄起来。我亲眼见过。”

“Wait,” I said through chattering teeth, trying to piece together the past few minutes. “I think I’m bleeding. Maybe don’t move me.” Was I going into shock from blood loss? Was I going to die, here, in the parking lot of the Dew Drop Inn?

“等等，”我牙齿打颤地说，努力回忆着过去几分钟发生的事情。“我觉得我在流血。也许别动我。”我是不是失血过多休克了？我会不会死在这里，死在露珠旅馆的停车场里？

“That’s not blood, chief; that’s the coffee you spilled. You’re fine; let’s get moving.”

“那不是血，警官；那是你洒出来的咖啡。你没事，我们走吧。”

Danny didn’t wait for me to get up on my own; he bent down, pulled me up by the front of my jacket, and brushed me off like I was five. I struggled to regain my balance, noticing that the parking lot of my motel was on a steep, icy hill. I had just fallen while standing on a literal slippery slope (I was starting to understand why they warn you about those).

丹尼没等我自己站起来，就弯下腰，揪住我的外套前襟把我拉了起来，像拍五岁小孩的灰尘一样拍掉我的脚。我挣扎着站稳，这才发现汽车旅馆的停车场建在一个陡峭结冰的山坡上。我刚才站在一个名副其实的滑坡上，结果摔倒了（我开始明白为什么人们总是警告你注意这种滑坡了）。

At least I wasn’t burned by my full cup of steaming hot coffee as I went down—it froze in midair on the way to my face. On that particular day in January it was so cold you couldn’t even get chocolate—they told me the stuff just explodes into ice crystals at -35 degrees, so they don’t carry it until May at the earliest.

至少我下楼的时候没被那杯热气腾腾的咖啡烫到——它在我脸前就冻住了。那天是1月，冷得连巧克力都买不到——他们告诉我，巧克力在零下35度就会冻成冰晶，所以最早也要到5月份才有货。

“You’re gonna need to get some real boots out here,” Big Danny told me, stating the obvious. He looked me over and clearly didn’t find me very impressive. “And you should get a puffier coat and a warm hat that covers your ears. Remember, out here the native Inuits still use refrigerators so they can keep their food from freezing. You get that, boss? It’s so cold you need a fridge to keep your food from turning into ice vapor . . . and, you know, just to educate you on some key survival strategies up here, you lose eighty percent of your body heat through your head. Can’t afford to do that in North Dakota, no sir. You want me to take you to the Walmart before we head to the shop and get you rigged out?”

“你得弄双像样的靴子，”大丹尼跟我说，这话听起来显而易见。他上下打量了我一番，显然觉得我没什么了不起。“你还得弄件羽绒服，再戴顶能遮住耳朵的帽子。记住，这儿的因纽特人还在用冰箱，这样食物才不会冻住。明白了吗，老大？这儿冷得要命，食物都得用冰箱才能不变成冰水……还有，我得给你普及一下这儿的生存之道，人体80%的热量都是从头部散失的。在北达科他州可受不了这种损失，绝对不行。要不要我先带你去沃尔玛，然后再去店里给你置办点装备？”

“Ah, no thanks, Big Danny,” I said, limping toward his truck. “I don’t want to be late on my first day meeting the team.”

“啊，不用了，大丹尼，”我一瘸一拐地走向他的卡车说，“我可不想在和球队见面的第一天就迟到。”

“Your funeral,” he said with a shrug.

“那是你的葬礼，”他耸了耸肩说道。

I climbed into the passenger’s side of his truck, anxious to get into the heated cab. Except it was freezing inside the truck too.

我爬进他卡车的副驾驶座，急切地想钻进温暖的驾驶室。结果车里也冷得要命。

Big Danny eased onto Highway 20, one of the only two major arteries going through town. He pointed off into the distance, where I could just make out a Walmart sign.

大丹尼缓缓驶入20号公路，这是贯穿小镇的两条主要干道之一。他指着远处，我隐约看到沃尔玛的招牌。

“Are you sure you don’t want to stop off, boss? It’ll only take a minute and you’ll be a whole lot more comfortable. No offense, but dressing like that up here, they’re going to think you’re stupid or crazy or both.”

“老板，您确定不停下来一下吗？只需要一分钟，您就会舒服多了。别介意，但您这样穿在这里，他们会觉得您要么是傻子，要么是疯子，或者两者兼有。”

I had never been to a Walmart. Through chattering teeth I answered, “ Yes please, Walmart. ”

我以前从没去过沃尔玛。我牙齿打颤地回答说：“好的，请去沃尔玛。”

In the store, I quickly grabbed some insulated boots, a workman’s coat, a pair of leather construction gloves, and a hat that Big Danny insisted I buy (even though it looked ridiculous on me).

在商店里，我迅速拿了几双保暖靴、一件工装外套、一副皮质建筑手套，还有一顶大丹尼坚持让我买的帽子（尽管它戴在我头上看起来很滑稽）。

“Great hat,” Dawn, our cashier, said cheerfully as she rang us up. “I bought that same one for my husband last year.” Danny smiled at me and pointed at Dawn, nodding his head. “You going to wear them boots out?” Dawn trained her eyes on me. She was intense and seemed to be letting me know that she’d just made a very helpful suggestion. I changed my boots right there in front of her, embarrassed by my colorful but out-of-place Fred Segal socks.

“帽子真漂亮，”收银员道恩一边给我们结账一边兴高采烈地说，“我去年也给我老公买过一模一样的。”丹尼朝我笑了笑，指着道恩点了点头。“你打算穿这双靴子出门吗？”道恩的目光紧紧地盯着我。她神情专注，似乎在告诉我她刚才的建议非常实用。我尴尬地在她面前换了靴子，因为我那双颜色鲜艳但与整体风格格格不入的弗雷德·西格尔袜子实在太碍眼了。

I glanced up at Dawn and, sure enough, she was eyeballing my socks with the trained eye of a cold weather survivalist. It suddenly occurred to me that I might have a little culture clash problem with the sales team I was about to meet. I was going to be walking into a room full of Dannys and Dawns and trying to command their respect and loyalty. Maybe this was going to be harder than I originally thought.

我抬头瞥了一眼道恩，果然，她正用一种身经百战的御寒专家的眼神打量着我的袜子。我突然意识到，我可能和即将见面的销售团队存在一些文化冲突。我即将走进一间满是丹尼和道恩的房间，努力赢得他们的尊重和忠诚。也许这比我想象的要难得多。

Devils Lake, I realized, was not the kind of place where locals used phrases like “emotionally charged imagery” or “dramatic character arc” or “protagonist-driven plot”—concepts that were the norm back home in Hollywood. How was I going to turn the staff of this town into a team of compelling salespeople?

我意识到，魔鬼湖并不是那种当地人会使用“充满情感的画面”、“跌宕起伏的人物弧光”或“以主角为中心的剧情”这类词汇的地方——这些概念在我的家乡好莱坞却是司空见惯的。我该如何把这个小镇的员工打造成一支极具感染力的销售团队呢？

I had two days with the team before I had to head to New York for another deal. That gave me about forty-eight hours to figure out how to teach Big Danny and Little Danny, Gus “Guzzler” Gussard, Tommy no-last-name, Tiffany, and her daughter Crystal how to sell motorcycles like Elias, legendary motorcycle and Jet Ski racer, airplane racer, and Hollywood Hills rock-and-roll tequila-drinking go-all-nighter.

在前往纽约洽谈另一笔交易之前，我和团队待了两天。这意味着我只有大约48小时的时间来想办法，如何教会大丹尼和小丹尼、格斯·“酒鬼”·古萨德、没有姓氏的汤米、蒂芙尼和她的女儿克里斯托像伊莱亚斯那样卖摩托车。伊莱亚斯是传奇的摩托车和水上摩托艇赛车手、飞机赛车手，也是好莱坞山上通宵达旦喝龙舌兰的摇滚乐手。

As we pulled up in front of the shop a few minutes later, I was getting the jitters. What was I going to tell these people that they would understand and be able to use to improve sales? What could they possibly have in common with a guy like Elias?

几分钟后，当我们把车停在店前时，我开始紧张起来。我该如何跟这些人解释，才能让他们理解并能运用我的方法来提升销售业绩呢？他们怎么可能跟像伊莱亚斯这样的人有共同语言呢？

I stepped into the company office, ready to teach them what I knew. But the first thing I noticed was that it was freezing cold inside. Nobody was wearing a coat. They acted as if it was 72 degrees or something.

我走进公司办公室，准备把我所知道的教给他们。但首先映入眼帘的是里面冷得要命。没人穿外套。他们好像觉得外面有72华氏度似的。

“What’s the temperature in here?” I asked.

“这里温度是多少？”我问。

“Fifty-five,” said Little Danny, Big Danny’s assistant. “If you want something warm, I can make you a cup of coffee in the microwave.”

“五十五，”大丹尼的助手小丹尼说，“如果你想喝点热的，我可以用微波炉给你泡杯咖啡。”

Microwave coffee? No thanks.

微波炉咖啡？不了，谢谢。

I headed straight to the back of the freezing warehouse, where the whole team had assembled to hear me speak. I stepped onto the makeshift stage—a piece of plywood perched atop four paint buckets. The howling wind was banging a drum solo against the corrugated tin walls.

我径直走向冷库后方，整个团队都聚集在那里听我讲话。我走上临时搭建的讲台——一块胶合板架在四个油漆桶上。呼啸的狂风拍打着波纹铁皮墙，发出阵阵铿锵的鼓声。

I could tell by their faces that I didn’t look like anything the Dannys, or Crystal, or Gus, or Tommy, or Tiffany had ever seen before. Despite Big Danny’s best efforts to dress me as a local with boots and my puffy coat and my ridiculous hat, I looked like the Man Who Fell to Earth.

从他们的表情我就知道，我跟丹尼一家、克丽丝塔尔、格斯、汤米还有蒂芙尼以前见过的任何人都不一样。尽管大丹尼竭尽全力想把我打扮成当地人，给我穿上靴子、羽绒服，戴上那顶滑稽的帽子，我看起来还是像个天外来客。

I laid it all out for them. “Despite our best intentions, we’re only selling about seventy-five thousand dollars a week, not nearly enough. This puts our whole company into negative territory, and there’s frustration at the home office. That’s why I’m here today, to help kick things into gear. I’ve been doing this a long time, and here’s how I like to think about our business: Nobody needs an Italian racing motorcycle. Ducati, Guzzi, whatever . . . Compare our customer to a shopper in your local Walmart—he is buying stuff he needs : a snowplow, a generator, a block heater, a jumper cable. But our products are different. Our products serve an emotional purpose. It’s about desire , not necessity . It’s about the opportunity to spend some money needlessly on a desire. So your job is to increase that desire. And how do you do that? By making our products harder to buy.”

我把情况都跟他们说了。“尽管我们尽了最大的努力，但每周的销售额只有七万五千美元左右，远远不够。这让整个公司陷入了亏损，总部也一片愁容。所以我今天来这里，就是为了扭转局面。我从事这行很久了，我是这样看待我们这个行业的：没人需要意大利赛车摩托车。杜卡迪、古兹，随便什么牌子……把我们的客户比作你家附近沃尔玛的顾客——他们买的是必需品：除雪机、发电机、发动机预热器、电瓶线。但我们的产品不一样。我们的产品满足的是情感需求。它关乎欲望，而非必需品。它关乎的是人们有机会把钱花在自己想要的东西上。所以你们的任务就是增强这种欲望。而该怎么做呢？让我们的产品更难买到。”

Blank faces. I couldn’t tell if I had blown their minds or if they were just waiting for me to leave.

他们一脸茫然。我不知道我的话是否让他们大吃一惊，还是他们只是在等我离开。

“So . . . are there any questions on that?” I asked.

“那么……大家还有什么问题吗？”我问道。

Little Danny raised his hand.

小丹尼举起了手。

“Yeah, go ahead, Little Danny.”

“好的，去吧，小丹尼。”

“What’s a Guzzi?”

“Guzzi是什么？”

“Danny, it’s a European motorcycle that we sell parts for. C’mon, man, that’s what we do here . But listen, the point is, you guys are making the sale too easy for the buyer and it’s killing your deals. Neediness! Discounts! Stop doing all that stuff. Make the customer fight for it. Make these products hard to attain, while simultaneously feeding the customer’s desire for them.”

“丹尼，我们卖的是欧洲摩托车的配件。拜托，伙计，这就是我们这儿的生意。但听着，重点是，你们把销售搞得太容易了，这正在毁掉你们的生意。让顾客觉得非买不可！打折！别再搞这些了。让顾客自己去争取。让这些产品难以获得，同时又要满足顾客的渴望。”

Crystal’s hand went up. “So what you’re saying is that we need to try and not sell people things so that they’ll try harder to spend their money on things they don’t need.”

克丽丝塔尔举起了手。“所以你的意思是，我们应该尽量避免向人们推销东西，这样他们就会更努力地把钱花在他们不需要的东西上？”

“That’s right!” I said, delighted that I’d reached at least one member of the team.

“没错！”我说道，很高兴至少联系上了团队中的一位成员。

“I don’t get it,” she said.

“我不明白，”她说。

Oh man, I was so out of my element.

天哪，我当时完全不在状态。

“OK, guys,” I said, clapping my hands together, “that’s probably enough instruction for now. Why don’t you get out there and make some calls? I’ll be listening in to see what you might be doing right or wrong. Then, tomorrow, we can have another meeting like this. Great work, team!”

“好了，伙计们，”我拍着手说，“今天的指导就到此为止吧。你们现在就出去打几个电话试试？我会监听你们的通话，看看哪些地方做得对，哪些地方做得不对。明天我们再开个这样的会。干得好，团队！”

And without waiting for acknowledgment, I hopped off the “stage” and headed straight to my “office,” letting it be known that anyone who wanted to come ask questions was welcome.

不等对方回应，我就跳下“舞台”，径直走向我的“办公室”，并表示欢迎任何人来提问。

Nobody came.

没有人来。

Oh well. I easily spotted my office along the side of the warehouse. It was the rusted metal door with “Oren’s Office” written on a Post-it note with a smiley face. I pushed through the door, wincing at the cold. My eyes immediately went to the tiny space heater in the corner; it was silent, unplugged. There was another Post-it note on it: “This works.” For the first time since arriving in Devils Lake, I burst into a huge smile.

好吧。我很快就在仓库旁边找到了我的办公室。那是一扇锈迹斑斑的金属门，门上贴着一张便签，上面写着“奥伦的办公室”，还画了个笑脸。我推开门，冷得直皱眉。我的目光立刻落在了角落里的小暖风机上；它静悄悄的，没插电。上面还有一张便签：“这玩意儿管用。”自从来到魔鬼湖以来，我第一次露出了灿烂的笑容。

Then I buckled down and got to work.

然后我就埋头苦干了。

I fired up my computer and pressed Play on our sales-management software, which recorded all our calls. It was Gus talking to a UK motorcycle enthusiast. The buyer was looking for a new set of front forks for his Ducati Superleggera and we were one of the few vendors who carried it. “Nice,” I thought to myself, “here’s twelve thousand dollars in the bag before it even started.”

我打开电脑，按下销售管理软件的播放键，这个软件会录制我们所有的通话。是格斯在和一位英国摩托车爱好者通话。买家想为他的杜卡迪Superleggera摩托车找一套新的前叉，而我们是少数几家有货的供应商之一。“不错，”我心想，“还没开始就已经赚到一万两千美元了。”

Except it wasn’t.

但事实并非如此。

Gus scared the client away and the call ended awkwardly: “So what do you think? I can get these shipped out to you tomorrow, be there by Tuesday—do you want to pay by credit card, or . . .” Same thing on the next call with Tiffany and a guy from New York who needed a gas tank for his Moto Guzzi MGS-01. And the one after that between Tommy and a buyer in Arkansas looking for a set of carbon fiber wheels.

Gus把客户吓跑了，通话尴尬地结束了：“怎么样？我明天就能把这些东西寄给你，周二就能到——你想用信用卡付，还是……” 下一次和Tiffany的通话也一样，对方是个纽约人，需要一个Moto Guzzi MGS-01的油箱。再下一次，Tommy和一位阿肯色州的买家通话，他想买一套碳纤维轮毂。

As the tapes rolled and the heater fan whirred quietly, I stripped off one layer of clothing at a time. My down jacket. My windbreaker. My thermal hooded sweatshirt. Eventually my wool hat. The tapes of sales calls kept rolling, one after another, as I paced around the office, thinking. There was something similar happening on every single call, a roadblock that our sales team was hitting. It was weird because we weren’t that bad. We were polite. We asked questions. We gave detailed product descriptions. We explained why this product was better than that product. We tried to explain away objections. We asked for the order a few times. Isn’t that what salespeople do? It didn’t matter which of our salespeople it was or where the buyer was located or what they were trying to purchase—the result was the same. The call ended awkwardly with the buyer making excuses and deferring the decision to later, because he had to “check in” with an unavailable partner or mechanic or wife or brother or a few Teletubbies, or whoever, and then quickly getting off the phone—presumably to go search the internet for a better deal.

录音机不停地播放着，暖风机的风扇也静静地嗡嗡作响，我一件一件地脱掉身上的衣服。羽绒服，防风衣，保暖连帽衫，最后连羊毛帽也脱掉了。销售电话的录音机不停地播放着，我在办公室里踱来踱去，思索着。每一次通话都出现了类似的问题，销售团队都遇到了同样的障碍。这很奇怪，因为我们其实做得还不错。我们很有礼貌，会提问，会详细介绍产品，会解释为什么这款产品比那款产品更好，会努力消除客户的异议，还会几次催促他们下单。销售人员不都是这么做的吗？不管是哪个销售人员，不管买家在哪里，不管他们想买什么——结果都一样。通话尴尬地结束了，买家找了些借口，把决定推迟到以后，因为他要和一位不在场的合伙人、机械师、妻子、兄弟、几个天线宝宝或其他什么人“确认一下”，然后迅速挂断了电话——大概是要去网上寻找更划算的交易。

But I couldn’t put my finger on exactly what it was the sales team was doing wrong. Sure, they could have been more charismatic, or given more technical information, or been less needy, but there was something big going on here.

但我说不清销售团队到底哪里出了问题。当然，他们或许可以更有魅力，或者提供更多技术信息，或者少些急切，但这里面肯定存在一些大问题。

After six hours straight at my desk, I was fried and I didn’t have a definitive answer. I stopped the tapes and leaned back in my chair, thinking. And for some reason, my eyes fell on the mini–basketball hoop in the corner of the office.

在办公桌前连续工作了六个小时后，我筋疲力尽，却仍然没有找到确切的答案。我停下录音带，靠在椅背上思考。不知为何，我的目光落在了办公室角落里的迷你篮球架上。

“Yes,” I thought to myself, “of course. That’s it! ”

“没错，”我心想，“当然是这样！就是这样！”

Just then, a phone rang. Apparently I had an office line. I found an old-school Panasonic cordless phone in the desk drawer and picked it up. “This is Oren,” I said a little hesitantly. Nobody knew where I was. And anyone who did would not be calling me with good news.

就在这时，电话响了。看来我还有条办公电话线。我在办公桌抽屉里找到一部老式的松下无绳电话，拿起来。“我是奥伦，”我有些犹豫地说。没人知道我在哪里。就算有人知道，也不会是给我带来好消息。

“Hi Oren, it’s Elias. Listen, got a call from Danny today. He’s worried about what you’re doing up there. The team doesn’t like you that much. He says they’re ready to dump you into the lake first chance they get to make it look like an accident. I guess we’re going to have to pull you out of there and try something else.” He sounded disappointed.

“嗨，奥伦，我是伊莱亚斯。听着，今天丹尼给我打了个电话。他很担心你在上面干的事。队员们不太喜欢你。他说他们随时准备找机会把你扔进湖里，伪装成意外。看来我们得把你弄出来，另想办法了。”他的语气听起来很失望。

“Hey, I don’t want to be argumentative, but the problem is you , not me,” I said. “Elias, you’re too good—ten people here doesn’t equal one of you. You are a natural-born salesman. You were literally born to sell anything on wheels. Girls love you. Guys love you. Hell, I love you. Compellingness is in your DNA. You instinctively understand how to create beauty, allure, exclusivity, and desire. You know how to sell power and speed, to create an irresistible appeal. For you, things just sell themselves.

“嘿，我不想跟你争论，但问题出在你身上，不是我，”我说。“伊莱亚斯，你太优秀了——这里十个人加起来都比不上你。你天生就是个推销员。你生来就是为了卖任何带轮子的东西。女孩喜欢你。男孩喜欢你。说实话，我也喜欢你。你的基因里就流淌着魅力。你本能地懂得如何创造美感、诱惑力、独特性和欲望。你知道如何推销力量和速度，创造出无法抗拒的吸引力。对你来说，东西根本不用推销。”

“I’ve been listening to tapes of their calls all day and I realized something,” I continued. “These guys have been trying to follow what you do, but it’s not working for them because they aren’t you.”

“我今天一整天都在听他们的通话录音，我意识到了一件事，”我继续说道，“这些人一直在试图模仿你的做法，但这对他们行不通，因为他们不是你。”

I threw the basketball to the mini-hoop and it bounced off the rim. I was never a good shot anyway.

我把篮球扔进迷你篮筐，结果球从篮筐上弹了出来。反正我投篮本来就不好。

“It’s like . . . Remember that scene in White Men Can’t Jump ?”

“这就像……还记得电影《白人不会跳》里的那个场景吗？”

I heard a laugh on the other end of the line because we had watched the movie together at least five times.

我听到电话那头传来笑声，因为我们至少一起看过五遍这部电影了。

“That scene where Wesley Snipes and Woody Harrelson beat this guy Raymond in a five-hundred-dollar winner-take-all pickup game, so Raymond needs more money to keep playing, he gets a gun from his car, walks to the corner liquor store, puts on a ski mask, points that forty-five Magnum at the store owner,” I said. “Remember what the store owner says?”

“就是韦斯利·斯奈普斯和伍迪·哈里森在一场五百美元的赌局中赢了雷蒙德，赢了就全拿。雷蒙德为了继续打下去，需要更多钱，就从车里掏出一把枪，走到街角的酒铺，戴上滑雪面罩，用那把45口径的马格南手枪指着店主，”我说。“还记得店主说了什么吗？”

“Yeah, of course,” said Elias, as he quotes the line from the movie. “‘Raymond, is that you? Take that damn mask off!’”

“当然，”伊莱亚斯说着，引用了电影里的台词，“‘雷蒙德，是你吗？把那该死的面具摘下来！’”

“Exactly!” I was getting to the point now. “And right after he’s recognized by the shopkeeper, Raymond pulls off the ski mask, drops the whole gangster persona, and goes back to being his normal self. He reminds the shopkeeper that he should be protecting his store better because it’s a dangerous neighborhood. Then Raymond sells his gun to the shopkeeper at a good price in a quick negotiation, everyone’s happy, and Raymond gets the cash he needs to keep playing basketball against Wesley Snipes.”

“没错！”我正说到重点。“雷蒙德被店主认出来之后，立刻摘下滑雪面罩，卸下黑帮伪装，变回了原来的自己。他提醒店主应该更好地保护店铺，因为这片街区很危险。然后，雷蒙德迅速与店主讨价还价，以不错的价格卖掉了枪，皆大欢喜，雷蒙德也拿到了继续和韦斯利·斯奈普斯打篮球所需的现金。”

I made my final point: “When Raymond tried to pose as someone he’s not, even with the ski mask, it was obvious. The shopkeeper sees right through it. But when Raymond drops the phony stuff and just acts like his normal self, a wheeler-dealer, he gets the deal done.”

我最后总结道：“当雷蒙德试图伪装成另一个人时，即使戴着滑雪面罩，也显而易见。店主一眼就看穿了。但当雷蒙德卸下伪装，展现出他真实的本性——一个精明的商人——时，交易就达成了。”

I explained how we were making the same mistake in our office by wearing different masks during the sales calls and trying to take on personalities that were not our own. “When I listened to those sales calls today,” I said to Elias, “I looked at it from the customer’s point of view. To the customer, our staff has so many different personalities, it’s sort of a multiple personality disorder. Our salesperson doesn’t feel authentic or real. We’re trying too hard. I think I can fix this problem.”

我解释说，我们在办公室也犯了同样的错误，在销售电话中戴着不同的面具，试图扮演与自己截然不同的角色。“今天我听了那些销售电话录音，”我对伊莱亚斯说，“我从客户的角度审视了这个问题。在客户看来，我们的员工性格各异，简直就像多重人格障碍。我们的销售人员给人的感觉很不真实，不够真诚。我们用力过猛了。我觉得我可以解决这个问题。”

THE FIVE PERSONALITIES OF THE SALES APOCALYPSE

销售末日五大人格

What I had realized in Devils Lake is that the salespeople on our team, much like salespeople everywhere, were struggling to make sales by using a loser’s formula. During nearly every sales call, they shifted from persona to persona, appealing to whatever emotional state the buyer was in at that moment. It boiled down to five different personas, or archetypes. This change from persona to persona confuses buyers, who crave consistency and certainty from people they’re doing business with. These are the five personas that make up the Loser’s Formula, listed in order of their appearance in most sales presentations:

我在魔鬼湖意识到，我们团队的销售人员，和其他地方的销售人员一样，都在使用一种失败的销售模式，却仍然难以达成交易。几乎每次销售拜访中，他们都会不断切换不同的角色，试图迎合买家当时的情绪状态。最终，他们使用的模式可以归纳为五种不同的角色，或者说是原型。这种角色切换会让买家感到困惑，因为他们渴望与自己做生意的人保持一致性和确定性。以下是构成“失败者模式”的五种角色，按它们在大多数销售演示中出现的顺序排列：

  1. The Ultimate Nice Guy
    终极好好先生
  2. The ShamWow Guy
    ShamWow 先生
  3. The Sorcerer
    巫师
  4. The Angel
    天使
  5. The Wolf
    狼

I’ll break these down in a bit more detail.

我将更详细地解释一下。

1. The Ultimate Nice Guy

1. 终极好好先生

At the top of a sales call, most people start by putting on the Ultimate Nice Guy persona. In other words, we play it safe. We want above all else to be liked, and we try to achieve this by seeking common ground. Great to talk to you today! Where are you calling from? Really, my uncle used to live in Houston, hot down there in the summer. Plans for the weekend? Fishing! I love fishing, my grandfather used to . . . Then, shifting to work topics, it goes a little like this: What kind of business are you in? Oh, that’s awesome, I love pest control! The Ultimate Nice Guy is the first archetype or mask that salespeople fall into because it is the easiest and safest approach. No one is going to complain about a pleasant, approachable, friendly start to a call. This leads to surface-level conversation: current news, weather, sports, empty exchanges.

在销售电话的开头，大多数人都会摆出一副“完美好人”的姿态。换句话说，我们选择稳妥的方式。我们最渴望的是被人喜欢，为此，我们会努力寻找共同话题。“很高兴今天能和您通话！您是从哪里打来的？”“真的吗？我叔叔以前住在休斯顿，那里的夏天很热。周末有什么安排？”“钓鱼！我喜欢钓鱼，我爷爷以前也……”然后，话题转向工作，大概是这样的：“您是做什么行业的？”“哦，太棒了，我喜欢害虫防治！”“完美好人”是销售人员最先戴上的面具，因为它最简单也最安全。没有人会抱怨电话开头是友好、亲切、平易近人的。但这往往会导致对话流于表面：时事新闻、天气、体育，以及一些空洞的交流。

What’s wrong with a nice guy? At a basic level, nothing, and it’s certainly true people are more likely to do business with us if they like us. Look, I get it—the impulse at the top of the meeting is to impress upon others we are nice and relatable and have common ground with the buyer. But the real problem with the Ultimate Nice Guy persona is that it signals to the buyer how much power he has over us. Once we have lost status (and given away our power) we shift from the Ultimate Nice Guy archetype into the ShamWow Guy archetype, who will go on to explain all the features of the product or idea.

做一个好人有什么错？从根本上来说，没什么错，而且人们喜欢我们，当然更愿意和我们做生意。我知道，在会议开始时，我们最想做的就是给别人留下好印象，让他们觉得我们友善、容易相处，并且和买家有共同话题。但“完美好人”形象的真正问题在于，它向买家传递了一个信息：他可以掌控我们。一旦我们失去了地位（也交出了自己的权力），我们就会从“完美好人”的原型变成“推销员”的原型，开始滔滔不绝地解释产品或理念的所有功能。

2. The ShamWow Guy

2. ShamWow 先生

People expect to know what it is we’re selling, right? So we start listing the best features of the product, our most famous customers, the five-star ratings, our incredible customer service reputation, and our recent industry awards. This is where we become the ShamWow Guy.

人们想知道我们卖的是什么，对吧？所以我们开始列举产品的最佳功能、我们最著名的客户、五星好评、我们卓越的客户服务口碑以及我们最近获得的行业奖项。这就是我们成为“ShamWow 先生”的地方。

For those who haven’t seen the ShamWow commercials, here’s some background:

如果你还没看过ShamWow的广告，这里简单介绍一下背景：

Over three weekends in the summer of 2007, Israeli-born filmmaker and entrepreneur Offer Shlomi shot a two-minute commercial extolling the virtues of the ShamWow, a cleaning towel that promised to soak up twelve times its weight in spilled liquids and revolutionize your life. Shlomi handled the yellow cloth with the dexterity of a stage magician, wiping up small puddles and blotting soda-soaked carpets, describing an endless list of features for what was basically a thirty-five-cent kitchen cloth. Nobody was better than Shlomi at hyping features.

2007年夏天，以色列电影制作人兼企业家奥弗·什洛米利用三个周末的时间，拍摄了一段两分钟的广告，大力宣传ShamWow清洁巾的种种优点。这款清洁巾号称能吸收自身重量十二倍的液体，彻底改变你的生活。什洛米像舞台魔术师一样灵巧地挥舞着这块黄色抹布，擦拭着小水坑，吸干着被汽水浸透的地毯，滔滔不绝地介绍着这块其实价值35美分的厨房抹布的种种功能。在宣传产品功能方面，什洛米可谓无人能及。

When we’re in the ShamWow archetype, we similarly spring into action listing everything our product can do, has done, and might do in the future. It has a hundred terabytes; we are the only ones with hyper-threading; we’re FINRA compliant; we can do it in four weeks when everyone else takes six weeks or longer. Oh , and did I mention it comes with free shipping, a 15 percent discount, and a money-back guarantee?

当我们效仿 ShamWow 的模式时，我们也会立刻行动起来，列举出我们的产品能够做到、已经做到以及将来可能做到的一切。它拥有 100TB 的存储空间；我们是唯一一家拥有超线程技术的公司；我们符合 FINRA（美国金融业监管局）的规定；我们只需四周就能完成，而其他公司则需要六周甚至更长时间。哦，对了，我有没有提到它还提供免费送货、15% 的折扣和退款保证？

Of course, this information overload usually doesn’t get through to the buyer unless he already has idea receptors built for whatever we’re trying to tell him. Once all the best and brightest features and facts of the product are out on the table we realize, Yikes! I need to explain how these features will actually benefit the buyer. And then, yet another transformation begins.

当然，除非买家已经具备一定的认知基础，否则这种信息过载通常难以被他理解。一旦产品的所有亮点和功能都摆在台面上，我们才意识到：糟糕！我需要解释这些功能究竟如何才能真正让买家受益。然后，又一次转变开始了。

3. The Sorcerer

3. 巫师

The Juiceman juicer was one of the first products to be sold and brands built through the infomercial format. The Juiceman show featured energetic pitchman Jay Kordich, who blends an orange, a carrot, and some parsley, then goes on to explain how fantastic the rest of your life will be once you’re able to do this in your own kitchen. You’ll soon be smarter, more handsome, and more attractive to both men and women. After buying this product, you’ll date and marry the person of your dreams, who is also smart, ravishing, athletic, and rich. You’ll have beautiful children together who will be good at math, play polo with the Rockefeller kids, win national chess competitions, attend Harvard, invent a cryptocurrency, and buy you a retirement mansion in Malibu.

Juiceman榨汁机是最早通过电视购物广告形式销售并打造品牌的商品之一。Juiceman节目中，活力四射的推销员杰伊·科迪奇（Jay Kordich）将橙子、胡萝卜和欧芹放入榨汁机，然后开始滔滔不绝地讲述，一旦你能在自家厨房里轻松榨汁，你的生活将会变得多么美好。你会变得更聪明、更英俊，更受男女欢迎。购买这款产品后，你将与梦寐以求的伴侣约会并结婚，他/她同样聪明、迷人、运动健将且富有。你们将拥有漂亮的孩子，他们数学很好，能和洛克菲勒家族的孩子们一起打马球，赢得全国象棋比赛，考入哈佛大学，发明一种加密货币，并在马里布为你购置一座退休豪宅。

The Sorcerer archetype explains how each of the product’s amazing features will benefit the buyer in many exciting (but unverifiable) ways. He or she spins the features into a set of magical benefits. Depending on individual personality, there may be a little sleight of hand here with the numbers, some showmanship with a demonstration, and possibly the sharing of “secrets.” (“You didn’t hear it from me, but this is the same software Jerry Seinfeld uses to keep track of his ninety-seven Porsches.”) The Sorcerer mask will stay on until the buyer is sold on how great life will be after going into business with us.

“魔法师”原型会解释产品的每一项神奇功能将如何以各种令人兴奋（但无法验证）的方式让买家受益。他/她会将这些功能包装成一系列神奇的好处。根据个人性格的不同，他/她可能会在数字上耍些小花招，通过演示展现一些表演技巧，甚至可能分享一些“秘密”（比如：“你可别说是我告诉你的，这可是杰瑞·宋飞用来管理他那97辆保时捷的同款软件。”）。“魔法师”的面具会一直戴着，直到买家被说服，相信与我们合作后生活将会多么美好。

4. The Angel

4. 天使

Now that we’ve given the buyer all the information he ever wanted (and never wanted) about our products and ideas, and we’ve tried to get him super excited about the benefits our products offer, we really need to know the chances of closing the deal—high or low, good or bad? Now it feels time to do a “trial close” and see how close or far we really are to making some money. Who better to test the waters without causing a ripple in the pond than the Angel persona? She is a sweet, kind cherub who looks and sounds easygoing, wonderful to work with, submissive, and eager to please as she asks, “So what do you think? Is this something you’d be interested in? Any questions before we move forward?”

既然我们已经向买家提供了他想知道（以及他从未想过）的所有关于我们产品和理念的信息，并且努力让他对我们产品的优势感到兴奋，那么我们现在真的需要知道成交的几率有多大——高还是低，好还是坏？现在感觉是时候进行一次“试探性成交”了，看看我们离真正赚钱还有多远。还有谁比“天使”这个角色更适合在不引起任何波澜的情况下试探市场呢？她是一个甜美善良的小天使，看起来和听起来都很随和，合作起来非常愉快，顺从且渴望取悦对方。她会这样问：“你觉得怎么样？你对这个感兴趣吗？在继续之前，你还有什么问题吗？”

By this time in the sale, the buyer has been talking to just one person, but he’s encountered four different characters, each of them formulaic and unimaginative, each completely self-serving and predictable. It’s off-putting and the buyer starts to wonder, “Who are you really? What are your values, what do you stand for, and how far will you go just to make the deal?”

到了这个阶段，买家虽然只跟一个人交谈过，却遇到了四个不同的角色，每个人都千篇一律、缺乏想象力，而且都完全以自我为中心、毫无新意。这让买家感到反感，他开始怀疑：“你到底是谁？你的价值观是什么？你的立场是什么？为了达成交易，你究竟会做到什么地步？”

The buyer’s caution grows as time goes on, even as he is controlling the sale and owning the relationship. He will decide what happens next, how fast things will progress, and ultimately what the final price will be—if a deal is even to be made. But first, he will respond to the Angel’s trial close by introducing objections, himself testing the waters for discounts, free upgrades, and other signs of weakness.

随着时间的推移，买家的谨慎程度会不断加深，即便他掌控着销售的主动权和关系。他将决定下一步的行动、进展的速度，以及最终的价格——如果交易能够达成的话。但首先，他会通过提出异议来回应天使的试探性收尾，试探对方是否会提供折扣、免费升级或其他示弱的迹象。

The buyer offers, “Well, you know, it’d be really hard for us to switch accounting software so late in the year; we haven’t fully budgeted for this kind of expense. It’s good to know what our options are.” The Angel has done little but push the buyer to voice a full range of objections. As the Angel is overwhelmed, these objections must be overcome, and the final transformation takes shape.

买家表示：“嗯，你知道，在年底这个时间更换会计软件对我们来说确实很困难；我们还没有为这笔开支做好预算。了解我们有哪些选择总是好的。”天使投资人几乎没做什么，只是引导买家提出了各种各样的反对意见。由于天使投资人感到压力巨大，这些反对意见必须被一一克服，最终的转变才得以实现。

5. The Wolf

5. 狼

Things are getting hairy, and the final sales archetype now emerges. With the first glimmer of an objection, like the first rays of moonlight falling on a man with the werewolf curse, the Angel rapidly transforms into the Wolf. The Wolf jumps on the buyer’s objections to wrangle him into submission and make the objections irrelevant in hopes each one will be dropped, clearing the way to a sale. In practice, the dramatic switch from the Angel to the Wolf is a shock to the buyer, who doesn’t know how to respond. He clearly does not enjoy dealing with the Wolf archetype because we have suddenly turned combative and aggressive, but what is even more off-putting is that by this point in the call or presentation, we have taken on the personality of five very different characters. The long-suffering buyer is tired, and doesn’t have much energy left for thoughtful debate and considering purchasing options. He either agrees to buy knowing he will drop out later, or pumps the brakes, explaining that no decision can be made until his partner reviews the proposal. (We have not heard of this partner or “committee” previously because they may not even exist.)

情况变得棘手起来，最终的销售原型浮现出来。就像第一缕月光洒在被狼人诅咒的人身上一样，只要出现一丝异议的苗头，“天使”便迅速蜕变为“狼”。“狼”会抓住买家的异议不放，试图迫使其屈服，并让这些异议变得无关紧要，希望最终能促成交易。实际上，这种从“天使”到“狼”的戏剧性转变会让买家感到震惊，他们不知所措。显然，他们不喜欢与“狼”这种原型打交道，因为我们突然变得咄咄逼人、充满攻击性。但更令人反感的是，在电话或演示进行到这个阶段时，我们已经扮演了五个截然不同的角色。饱受折磨的买家已经精疲力竭，没有多少精力进行深入的讨论和考虑购买方案。他要么明知之后会反悔而同意购买，要么踩下刹车，解释说在伴侣审阅方案之前无法做出任何决定。 （我们之前从未听说过这个合作伙伴或“委员会”，因为他们可能根本不存在。）

—

KNOWING WE DEFAULT to these five archetypes in the course of a sale, I have long wondered why. Why do we move through these dramatically different personas as we try to sell someone a product, service, or idea?

我知道在销售过程中我们默认会使用这五种原型，但我一直很想知道为什么。为什么我们在向别人推销产品、服务或理念时，会切换于这些截然不同的角色之间？

The cognitive psychologists on my payroll have explained it this way: The human brain is programmed to respond to the immediate demands of any social situation and modify our behavior accordingly. The demands of any presentation push us naturally into a pattern of behavior, virtually every time the same. So as our behavior adapts to what the buyer wants to hear, the classic archetypes of Ultimate Nice Guy, ShamWow guy, Sorcerer, Angel, and Wolf appear in response. While each archetype serves the immediate purpose, the summary effect is negative.

我聘请的认知心理学家是这样解释的：人脑天生就会对任何社交情境的即时需求做出反应，并相应地调整我们的行为。任何演讲的要求都会自然而然地将我们推入一种行为模式，几乎每次都是如此。因此，当我们的行为适应买家想听到的内容时，就会出现一些经典的形象原型，例如“完美好人”、“推销员”、“巫师”、“天使”和“狼”。虽然每种形象原型都能满足眼前的需求，但最终的效果却是负面的。

In the final analysis, the buyer concludes, “This guy has multiple personalities!” The problem is, the human brain is built to seek out relationships that offer consistency in character. We desperately want to build a matrix of reliable and predictable social relationships, because we have a deep desire to feel like we understand and control our world and can predict who will do what, and when.

最终，买家得出的结论是：“这家伙有多重人格！” 问题在于，人脑天生就渴望建立性格一致的人际关系。我们迫切地想要构建一个可靠且可预测的人际关系网络，因为我们内心深处渴望理解和掌控自己的世界，并能预测谁会在何时做什么。

With the typical sales script, however, it’s impossible for the buyer to form a consistent mental model of the real you because of the personality changes through five different archetypes. It’s easy to imagine how this kind of wearing of masks triggers alarm bells, leading the buyer to conclude that something is wrong here—“This salesperson keeps changing who he really is to chase the sale. And who will he become after I give him the money or agreement? I’m not sure I’ve seen that character yet, or that I want to.”

然而，在典型的销售话术中，由于销售人员会通过五种不同的原型来变换人格，买家根本无法对你的真实面目形成一致的认知。不难想象，这种“戴面具”的做法会如何引发买家的警觉，让他们觉得哪里不对劲——“这个销售员为了促成交易，一直在变换身份。等我付钱或签合同之后，他又会变成什么样呢？我不确定我是否见过他真正的面目，或者说，我是否想见到他。”

The solution, of course, is to stop modulating behavior as you move through a presentation. But what, exactly, should you replace it with? By studying Elias and dozens of other naturals in the art of compellingness, I’ve discovered the answer lies in flipping the script.

当然，解决办法是停止在演讲过程中调整自己的行为。但究竟应该用什么来代替呢？通过研究埃利亚斯和其他几十位天生具有感染力的演讲者，我发现答案在于彻底改变演讲方式。

MY TWO-DAY TRAINING IN COMPELLINGNESS

我的两天魅力训练

The training I delivered to our North Dakota sales team after I had realized what was really going on was a long, cold, yet productive two days. At one point, I even accepted a cup of microwave coffee (and regret having done so to this day). But the results were exactly what we wanted: a huge bump in sales revenue.

在我意识到问题的症结所在之后，我为北达科他州的销售团队进行了为期两天的培训，虽然天气寒冷，但成果丰硕。期间，我甚至还喝了一杯微波炉咖啡（直到今天我都后悔不已）。但最终的结果正是我们想要的：销售收入大幅增长。

So what did I possibly teach in two days that made such a huge difference? A principle called “I’m not always right, but never uncertain.”

那么，我在短短两天内究竟教了什么，才产生了如此巨大的影响呢？一个叫做“我并不总是对的，但我从不犹豫”的原则。

On day one, I taught the team about Stick to Your Guns Theory, an idea that goes far beyond the trope of self-confidence. In fact, self-assurance is a tired and worn-out concept you’ll find in chapter one of every old-fashioned sales manual, and basically what they teach salespeople at “win friends” seminars. Stick to Your Guns, by contrast, has the beating heart of a much bigger idea, the kind that wins wars, changes history, and gives rise to leaders who are talked about for a thousand years: how to have an unshakable set of values and moral boundaries that are always on display to the buyer and at the same time completely immovable. I explained it like this:

第一天，我给团队讲解了“坚持原则”理论，这个理念远不止于“自信”这个老生常谈。事实上，“自信”这个概念早已陈旧过时，几乎每本老式销售手册的第一章都会提到，基本上就是那些“人人都懂”的研讨会上教给销售人员的那些东西。相比之下，“坚持原则”的核心理念则更为宏大，它能够赢得战争、改变历史，并造就那些流传千年的领袖：那就是如何拥有一套坚不可摧的价值观和道德底线，这些价值观和底线始终展现在客户面前，同时又完全不可动摇。我是这样解释的：

Imagine a movie studio called this office, saying they wanted to spend one hundred fifty thousand dollars on a prop bike for Johnny Depp to ride off a cliff in an upcoming bank robbery–style film shoot. And the prop bike they want is a 1968 Moto Guzzi V7R. If Danny here answered the phone, or if any of you took that call, you would say, “Great. Where do you want us to deliver it?” and you’d fill out the paperwork, take the order, and book the sale.
想象一下，一家电影制片厂打电话到我们办公室，说他们想花十五万美元买一辆道具摩托车，让约翰尼·德普在即将拍摄的银行抢劫题材电影里骑着它冲下悬崖。他们想要的道具摩托车是一辆1968年的Moto Guzzi V7R。如果丹尼接了电话，或者你们当中有人接到这个电话，你们会说：“太好了。你们想让我们把车送到哪里？”然后填写文件，记下订单，完成交易。
Not Elias.
不是伊莱亚斯。
Elias would say, “Hold on there, chief—did you say ride a V7R off a cliff? I do not have to tell you the V7R is a holy grail motorcycle; there are just seventeen left in the world—ten of those are in museums . . . and yes, sure I can get one. But to drive one into the ocean, are you completely high on quaaludes? Lose my number.” Click.
埃利亚斯会说：“等等，老大——你说要骑着V7R冲下悬崖？V7R是摩托车界的圣杯，这不用我说你也知道；全世界只剩下17辆了——其中10辆还在博物馆里……没错，我当然可以搞到一辆。但要你骑着它冲进海里，你是不是嗑了药嗑嗨了？别再联系我了。” 咔哒一声。

In fact, this actually happened; the story is legendary among our customers. Paramount Studios had called looking for a period-accurate Moto Guzzi V7R, and Elias told them to go fly a kite, but not exactly in those words. Elias sells some of the most exotic, coveted, cherished vehicles of the modern era. He doesn’t burn museum pieces to the ground to make a few bucks. Customers love the fact that he has the integrity not to sell out to the studios, or anyone with a bad attitude, a bad business plan, or a bad reputation. Elias has a fixed set of principles. Now, for sure, they may not be in alignment with the Beverly Hills Police Department, the Catholic Church of West Hollywood, Interpol, Parents Against Rock and Roll, or your grandmother’s knitting club, but they are a complete set of principles, easy to understand, based on simple logic, and most important, they don’t change from moment to moment, day to day, or year to year. He sticks to his guns, no matter what .

事实上，这事儿确实发生过；在我们客户中，这个故事堪称传奇。派拉蒙影业曾打电话来，想找一辆符合时代特征的Moto Guzzi V7R摩托车，伊莱亚斯让他们滚蛋，当然，他没用这么直白的措辞。伊莱亚斯出售的是现代最稀有、最令人梦寐以求、最受珍视的车辆。他不会为了蝇头小利而毁掉博物馆的藏品。客户们喜欢他正直的品格，他不会为了迎合电影公司、任何态度恶劣、商业计划糟糕或名声不好的人而妥协。伊莱亚斯有一套固定的原则。当然，这些原则可能与比佛利山庄警察局、西好莱坞天主教堂、国际刑警组织、反对摇滚乐的家长协会，甚至是你奶奶的编织俱乐部都格格不入，但它们是一套完整的原则，简单易懂，基于简单的逻辑，最重要的是，它们不会因为任何时刻、任何一天、任何一年而改变。无论如何，他都坚持自己的原则。

I taught our sales team about the Five Personalities of the Sales Apocalypse. The key isn’t to try to act how Elias would or how Oren would. The key is to stop being reactive to the needs of the buyer, and write personal scripts that are authentic to who you are, then stick to your guns (politely) anytime a buyer offers resistance or tries to push you around. Discount? No, not on your life. Free upgrade? No, why would I do that? Send me a proposal? OK, so we have a verbal agreement on terms? This prevents the buyer from unmasking you, discrediting you, or changing the script in any way. The only thing he can do is work with you or go away—which sometimes is for the best.

我给销售团队讲授了“销售末日五种人格”。关键不在于模仿伊莱亚斯或奥伦的风格，而在于停止对买家需求的被动反应，而是撰写符合你真实个性的销售话术，并在买家提出异议或试图强迫你时，（礼貌地）坚持自己的立场。折扣？想都别想。免费升级？不，我为什么要这么做？给我发个报价单？好的，那我们就口头达成协议了。这样就能防止买家揭穿你的真面目、诋毁你或以任何方式更改你的销售话术。他唯一能做的就是与你合作或放弃——有时，放弃才是最好的选择。

On day two of the training, there were lots of questions. For example, asked Danny, “If I’m not the Ultimate Nice Guy, then what am I?” The answer to this is as easy as it is straightforward: You are the expert. You must become an undisputed expert in the mind of the buyer in the first few minutes, and then continue to add credibility, insight, and competence to this expert status throughout the conversation. The Status Tip-Off and the Flash Roll are the perfect points of entry to creating this expert status. Your own industry knowledge, principles, and experience will cement that status.

培训第二天，学员们提出了很多问题。例如，有人问丹尼：“如果我不是‘完美好人’，那我是什么？”答案其实很简单：你就是专家。你必须在最初几分钟内就让买家认可你的专家地位，然后在整个对话过程中不断提升你的可信度、洞察力和专业能力。“地位提示”和“快速展示”是建立专家地位的绝佳切入点。你自身的行业知识、原则和经验将巩固你的专家地位。

In Devils Lake, sales more than doubled the following quarter—and doubled again the quarter after that. The team was soon selling bikes and parts on pace with Elias, and we had learned how to be compelling.

在魔鬼湖，接下来的季度销售额翻了一番还多，再下一个季度又翻了一番。团队很快就能跟上伊莱亚斯的销售速度，而且我们也学会了如何吸引顾客。

#↩

CHAPTER 8

第八章

Flip the Script, Go Anywhere, Try Anything, and Put It All on the Line to Win an Impossible Deal

颠覆常规，不惜一切代价，孤注一掷，只为赢得一场看似不可能的交易。

How to Put All the Scripts to Work

如何让所有脚本发挥作用

A ll kinds of good news arrives to you via text message, without much emotion or ceremony, something like “we had a baby” or “we got the deal,” and you might even get a smiley face to go along with it. But bad news is something completely different because it’s usually delivered by a phone and in a serious tone. The other side really wants you to feel the pain they are feeling. This is why Simon’s taut tone telegraphed the bad news as soon as I picked up the phone. “Oren, old boy,” he said with a stiff British accent. “It seems we’ve gone pear shaped on a deal, and I never thought I’d be in this position, but I’m going to call in a favor you owe me.” He continued with the details: “We buggered up an important client, Volka Motors UK. Now the account is being awarded to Bradford-McCoy in New York next week.” I could hear bits of spit fly from his lips as he said the words Bradford-McCoy , the agency he’d left twelve years ago to start his own firm. “We’ve popped our clogs—it’s bad news to lose a UK account to a bunch of . . . Americans.”

各种好消息都会通过短信传来，语气平淡，比如“我们有宝宝了”或者“我们谈成了”，有时还会配个笑脸表情。但坏消息就完全不同了，它通常是通过电话，语气也十分严肃。对方恨不得让你感同身受。这就是为什么我一拿起电话，西蒙那紧张的语气就预示着坏消息。“奥伦，老兄，”他用一口生硬的英国腔说道，“看来我们这笔生意搞砸了，我真没想到会落到这步田地，不过我得让你帮我个忙。”他接着详细说道：“我们搞砸了一个重要的客户，英国沃尔沃汽车公司。现在，下周这个客户就要交给纽约的布拉德福德-麦考伊公司了。”当他提到布拉德福德-麦考伊——他十二年前离开创办自己公司的那家广告公司——时，我能听到他嘴里喷出的唾沫。“我们已经不行了——把英国客户拱手让给一群……美国人，这可不是什么好消息。”

“Yeah, how embarrassing,” I said, rolling my eyes as I sat in my office in California. But I couldn’t fault him for being so anxious. This was indeed very bad news for Simon, who was CEO of one of the hippest ad agencies in London. Simon is the kind of charming, tall, blue-eyed, square-jawed Brit you’d cast as the driver in a Range Rover commercial. In the world of ad agencies, his impeccable eye for design and color is legendary. According to the legend, he once fired the entire design team because of a dispute over gunmetal gray versus dark smoke gray. Simon’s agency, 12 Kings, is one of the most interesting, influential, and progressive ad firms in the world. Their slogan is “We push past the point of disruption.”

“是啊，真尴尬，”我坐在加州的办公室里，翻了个白眼说道。但我不能责怪他如此焦虑。这对于西蒙来说确实是个坏消息，他是伦敦一家最潮的广告公司的首席执行官。西蒙是那种魅力十足、身材高挑、蓝眼睛、方下巴的英国绅士，你会觉得他简直就是路虎揽胜广告里的男主角。在广告界，他对设计和色彩的敏锐眼光堪称传奇。据说，他曾经因为设计团队在枪灰色和深烟灰色之间争论不休，而把整个设计团队都解雇了。西蒙的广告公司“12 Kings”是世界上最有趣、最具影响力、最具前瞻性的广告公司之一。他们的口号是“我们超越颠覆的界限”。

Translation: “We’re too cool for school.”

翻译：“我们太酷了，不屑上学。”

“Could you hop over the pond straightaway and put us right?” Simon asked. I hesitated because I knew how much he hated bringing in outside help (especially from an American). There was an awkward silence as he trailed off. Finally, he spoke up again: “I’ll fly you first cabin, British Airways.” Now he was talking my language.

“你能立刻飞过大西洋来帮我们解决这个问题吗？”西蒙问道。我犹豫了一下，因为我知道他有多讨厌引入外援（尤其是一个美国人）。一阵尴尬的沉默后，他的声音渐渐低了下去。最后，他再次开口：“我给你安排英国航空的头等舱机票。” 这下他终于说到我心坎里了。

And so, thirty-three hours later, after an eleven-hour flight and a night at the Savoy, I poured over the Volka marketing materials Simon had sent me. Volka was an industrial giant who manufactured cars, trains, and construction equipment, so any mid-sized agency would want this account. To figure out the problem with Volka, I was chauffeured to 12 Kings’ headquarters, where I waited to meet Simon the Great to discuss where and how he’d messed up.

于是，三十三个小时后，经过十一小时的飞行和在萨沃伊酒店的一夜住宿，我仔细研读了西蒙发给我的沃尔卡公司的营销资料。沃尔卡是一家工业巨头，生产汽车、火车和建筑设备，任何一家中型广告公司都会想要拿下这个客户。为了弄清楚沃尔卡的问题所在，我被专车送到了十二王广告公司的总部，在那里我等待着与西蒙会面，讨论他究竟在哪方面犯了错。

The lobby of 12 Kings was like nothing else out there, with furniture in a retro-tech color palette of sky blue, sea-foam green, and Navajo white. At the center of the whole Bauhaus-inspired bête noire was an exposed plywood interior tunnel, offset and tilted 20 degrees, like some kind of interactive metaphor for the path less taken.

12 Kings酒店的大堂独树一帜，家具采用复古科技感十足的配色，以天蓝色、海沫绿和纳瓦霍白为主。整个包豪斯风格的设计中心，是一个裸露的胶合板室内隧道，偏移并倾斜20度，仿佛是对人迹罕至之路的一种互动式隐喻。

“The mood board that inspired this space was about gravity, vortex, action, and illusion,” a junior account executive told me as she led me into the tunnel, heading toward the conference room where Simon and his team were in session.

“这个空间的设计灵感源于重力、漩涡、行动和幻觉，”一位初级客户经理一边领着我走进隧道，一边告诉我，隧道通往西蒙和他的团队正在开会的会议室。

“Mission accomplished,” I said, and then had to fight my way through some high-concept plastic entry flaps (like they have at ice hockey rinks) to greet Simon, who grimly welcomed me on the other side. He wasted no time, and thrust me straight into the staff meeting.

“任务完成，”我说，然后不得不费力地穿过一些设计精巧的塑料入口门（就像冰球场上的那种），去迎接西蒙。西蒙面色阴沉地在另一边迎接了我。他没有浪费时间，直接把我推进了员工会议室。

“I’d like to introduce you all to Oren Klaff,” Simon said, putting a welcoming hand on my shoulder. “Oren is American .” He paused, as if my American-ness implied a whole host of positives and negatives and his listeners needed a few seconds to absorb them all. “I’ve asked Oren here today to give us his thoughts on how we lost Volka. Oren?” And just like that, the spotlight was on me.

“我想向大家介绍一下奥伦·克拉夫，”西蒙说着，友好地拍了拍我的肩膀。“奥伦是美国人。”他顿了顿，仿佛我的美国人身份意味着一系列优缺点，而他的听众需要几秒钟来消化这些信息。“我今天请奥伦来这里，谈谈他对我们失去沃尔卡的看法。奥伦？” 就这样，聚光灯打在了我身上。

“Thanks, Simon.” I glanced around the room. It was a midsize conference room. Like the lobby, it was the pinnacle of creative effort, complete with metal sculptures for chairs and a table made from the door of an actual castle. There were thirty-five executives in the room, some still damp from the morning rainstorm, all looking glum. “I’m glad we could get together this morning,” I said, smiling. “I love London. One of my favorite cities, except when it’s raining.” I waited for a laugh from the crowd of soggy people in front of me, but nobody cracked a smile. Tough room. They had just lost a huge account, which meant no bragging rights at the annual awards and no annual bonus. These people thought they were attending a funeral, but I was about to tell them the patient lived.

“谢谢你，西蒙。”我环顾四周。这是一间中等大小的会议室。和酒店大堂一样，这里处处体现着创意，椅子是金属雕塑，桌子是用一座城堡的大门改造的。房间里有三十五位高管，有些人身上还残留着早晨暴雨的湿漉漉的，个个都愁眉苦脸的。“很高兴今天早上我们能聚在一起，”我笑着说，“我喜欢伦敦。它是我最喜欢的城市之一，除了下雨的时候。”我等着眼前这群浑身湿透的人笑出来，但没人露出笑容。气氛很沉闷。他们刚刚丢掉了一个大客户，这意味着在年度颁奖典礼上没资格炫耀，也没奖金。这些人以为自己是在参加葬礼，但我即将告诉他们，病人活下来了。

“To get started,” I said calmly, “let’s flip the script, and not call this a lost account. You haven’t completely lost it. At least, not yet.”

“首先，”我平静地说，“我们换个角度想，不要把这个客户说成是丢了。你还没有完全失去它。至少，现在还没有。”

“Terrific, that’s terrific,” Simon stated, struggling to sit upright on a polished metal bench. He needed the staff to hear this, and understand that all hope was not lost.

“太好了，真是太好了，”西蒙说道，他努力在光滑的金属长凳上坐直。他希望员工们能听到这句话，明白一切希望尚未破灭。

“Seriously,” I said. “I think we can convince Volka Motors UK to take another look at the decision, and I think the outcome might be different this time, if you’re willing to listen to me and act on what I say. But, fair warning: You’re going to hear some things you might not like. And I’m going to ask you to do some things that might seem counterintuitive. It can be an uncomfortable process.” Now we were going to see just how disruptive this agency really was. Could they truly embrace change?

“说真的，”我说，“我觉得我们可以说服英国大众汽车公司重新考虑这个决定，而且这次结果可能会不一样，前提是你们愿意听我的，并按照我说的去做。不过，先提醒你们：你们可能会听到一些不喜欢听的话。而且我会要求你们做一些看似违反直觉的事情。这可能会是一个不舒服的过程。” 现在，我们要看看这家公司到底有多大的颠覆性。他们真的能接受改变吗？

A murmur of skepticism spread throughout the room, rising to an anticlimactic but distinctly English group grumble. It was still a glum party, but I also heard something else: attention. I had given them hope.

一阵怀疑的低语在房间里蔓延开来，最终汇成一阵略显平淡却又极具英式特色的抱怨声。聚会气氛依然沉闷，但我同时也听到了另一种声音：关注。我给了他们希望。

“Please, enlighten us,” said Simon. I recognized a bit of pessimism in his voice.

“请您指点迷津吧。”西蒙说道。我从他的语气中听出了一丝悲观。

“Let’s begin. First and foremost,” I said, “you guys are way too creative. Creatives are the guys always making mood boards and talking about how to ‘take it to the next level,’ about ‘blue-sky thinking,’ ‘tentpole ideas,’ and how ‘data is the new oil.’ We can’t get caught in those creative clichés. Yes, I know it’s hard to hear, but if we want to win this account back, we’re going to be all about the money.”

“我们开始吧。首先，”我说，“你们的创意太过了。创意人员总是做情绪板，谈论如何‘更上一层楼’，谈论‘天马行空的思考’，谈论‘核心创意’，谈论‘数据是新的石油’。我们不能陷入这些创意陈词滥调。我知道这很难接受，但如果我们想赢回这个客户，我们就必须专注于赚钱。”

“Forgive me, Oren,” said Brian, the director of emerging media, uncomprehendingly, “but we have to worry about creative. We’re up against Bradford. They have us beat on every other front. Creativity is the ground we stand on. We have to be defined by a restlessness where the creative process never stops.”

“奥伦，请原谅，”新兴媒体总监布莱恩茫然地说，“但我们必须重视创意。我们的对手是布拉德福德。他们在其他所有方面都胜过我们。创意是我们立足之地。我们必须保持永不停歇的创作热情。”

“We’re not here for that. If Volka wanted an ad agency to create mood boards and name custom colors and quote dead poets, they would have hired us already. Volka doesn’t want poetry; they want profit.”

“我们不是来做这些的。如果Volka想要的是一家广告公司来制作情绪板、命名定制颜色、引用已故诗人的诗句，他们早就雇佣我们了。Volka不想要诗意，他们想要的是利润。”

That got through.

成功了。

“You think Bradford tried to impress them with a radically innovative marketing campaign idea?” I continued. “No, they probably came up with a pitch that sounded like this: ‘We’re the car advertising experts and we’re going to deliver five hundred million euros in new global sales to your brand.’ . . . Five hundred million. Notice anything about that number? First of all, it’s a number, not a color. Second, it’s a big number, but also conveniently a five percent increase in revenue for Volka. It’s huge, but still feels doable. That would be a massive win for a Volka UK campaign. So, of course, Volka skipped over you and went with the other guys.”

“你觉得布拉德福德是想用一个极具创新性的营销方案来打动他们吗？”我继续说道，“不，他们大概是想出了这么个方案：‘我们是汽车广告专家，我们将为你们的品牌带来五亿欧元的全球新销量。’……五亿欧元。注意到这个数字了吗？首先，它是一个数字，而不是一种颜色。其次，这是一个很大的数字，但恰好是沃尔卡营收增长的5%。这笔钱数额巨大，但感觉还是可以实现的。这对沃尔卡英国的营销活动来说将是一次巨大的胜利。所以，沃尔卡当然会跳过你，选择其他公司。”

I could see from the looks on their faces that I was speaking a different and mysterious language in this space devoted to design and illusion. I was speaking the language of money, and as they were finding, money doesn’t need colorful metaphors. At least one person seemed to be hearing me, though: Simon was taking mad notes in his Moleskine.

从他们的表情中，我看出在这个崇尚设计和幻象的空间里，我说的是一种截然不同、神秘莫测的语言。我说的是金钱的语言，而正如他们后来发现的，金钱并不需要华丽的辞藻。不过，至少有一个人似乎听懂了：西蒙正奋笔疾书地记着笔记。

“But we already have a big idea,” said Ian, the director of lightbulb moments (his actual title). Obviously, the original pitch concepts had been his.

“但我们已经有了一个很棒的想法，”伊恩说道，他是灵感迸发的总监（这是他的正式头衔）。显然，最初的提案概念都出自他之手。

“Oh yeah,” I said, waving the packet of information I was holding. “You mean this big idea that said, ‘We’re the coolest agency in the world and we’ve won a thousand prestigious French awards and we invented Pantomime Blue’? This is the worst thing ever. Let me explain something to you about ad agencies. To regular people, nobody really can tell the difference between any of you guys. ‘We are a full-service integrated marketing agency,’” I read, hurling their own meaningless selling points back at them. “‘We collaborate with our clients.’ ‘We’ve been in business for ten years and have more than a hundred and fifty years of combined management experience.’”

“哦，是吗？”我挥舞着手里的资料包说，“你是说那个‘我们是世界上最酷的广告公司，我们赢得了上千项法国著名奖项，我们还发明了哑剧蓝’之类的大创意？简直糟透了。让我来给你解释一下广告公司是怎么回事。对普通人来说，根本分不清你们这些公司之间的区别。‘我们是一家提供全方位服务的整合营销公司，’”我念着，把他们那些毫无意义的卖点扔了回去。“‘我们与客户紧密合作。’‘我们已成立十年，拥有超过一百五十年的管理经验。’”

I tossed the materials down on the table.

我把材料扔到桌子上。

“These are forgettable statements that anyone could make. These kinds of claims make it more difficult to figure out whether one agency is better than another. And so it just boils down to the money. So please, guys, put away your charcoal pencils. Put away the mood board too. If you love creativity that much, go write a graphic novel. Our job here is not that hard. All we need to do is find clear, persuasive concepts for the client, win back the account and get a ten-million-dollar budget approved.”

“这些都是些人人都能说出口的空话。这种说法只会让人更难判断哪家公司更胜一筹。最终，一切都取决于钱。所以，各位，请收起你们的炭笔吧。也别再搞什么情绪板了。如果你们真的那么热爱创意，那就去写漫画小说吧。我们的工作没那么难。我们只需要为客户找到清晰、有说服力的创意，赢回客户，然后拿到一千万美元的预算。”

“So what can we say to get them to reconsider our bid?” Simon asked, breaking the nervous silence. It takes a strong leader to ask a question that vulnerable in front of his team. I was impressed.

“那我们该怎么说才能让他们重新考虑我们的报价呢？”西蒙打破了令人窒息的沉默问道。敢在团队面前问出如此敏感的问题，需要一位强大的领导者。我对此印象深刻。

“You need to show Volka a formula for how to hire the right ad agency,” I explained. “Help them understand Bradford-McCoy was the easy choice and most obvious decision, but it was still the wrong one. And then show them what to do about it. So how about starting a conversation like this: ‘Volka, everyone agrees you need a new agency, and if you want to play it safe and feel like you did the ‘right thing for the shareholders,’ then don’t overthink this decision. Just hire Bradford-McCoy, Ogilvy, Interpublic or BBDO, because any of those is a pretty good choice. Ogilvy has been around since 1948, and Interpublic about the same—and has fifty-one thousand employees. Those are huge companies with billions in revenue—Interpublic did eighteen billion last year. You hire one of those firms for the same reason you hire IBM or Boston Consulting or Goldman Sachs or Skadden Arps. They are good firms. They’re convenient. No one is going to blame you if something goes wrong with that choice. You’re safe.

“你需要向沃尔卡展示如何聘请合适的广告公司的公式，”我解释道。 “帮助他们理解，选择布拉德福德-麦考伊（Bradford-McCoy）虽然是最简单、最显而易见的选择，但仍然是错误的。然后告诉他们该如何应对。不妨这样开始对话：‘沃尔卡，大家都同意你需要一个新的广告公司。如果你想稳妥起见，觉得你“为股东做了正确的事”，那就别想太多了。直接聘用布拉德福德-麦考伊、奥美（Ogilvy）、埃培智集团（Interpublic）或BBDO，因为这些公司都是不错的选择。奥美自1948年就成立了，埃培智集团也差不多——而且拥有5.1万名员工。这些都是年收入数十亿美元的大公司——埃培智集团去年的收入高达180亿美元。你聘用这些公司的原因和你聘用IBM、波士顿咨询公司、高盛或世达律师事务所（Skadden Arps）的原因一样。它们都是优秀的公司。它们很方便。如果这个选择出了问题，没人会责怪你。你很安全。’”

“‘But for a moment consider this: At Bradford your account will be small. They want Nestlé or Exxon or Coca-Cola. Those are the big-boy accounts. Who at a Big Five ad agency actually wants the Volka UK account? No one really. So if you hire Bradford, the team assigned to you will be getting your account as a punishment. The boss would say, “Hey Smith, Hey Johnson, get over here. You idiots screwed up big on the Ford-China account, so now I’m sticking you with Volka UK.”

“但请你仔细想想：在布拉德福德，你的客户规模很小。他们想要的是雀巢、埃克森美孚或者可口可乐。这些都是大客户。五大广告公司里谁会想要沃尔卡英国的客户呢？几乎没人会。所以，如果你雇佣了布拉德福德，分配给你的团队会把你的客户交给他们，作为对他们的惩罚。老板会说：‘嘿，史密斯，嘿，约翰逊，过来。你们这些笨蛋把福特中国的客户搞砸了，所以现在我把沃尔卡英国的客户交给你们了。’”

“‘So that’s it. You are now working with Smith and Johnson, the guys who screwed up on Ford-China or are fresh out of school and have never done a big campaign before. That’s who you get from Bradford or BBDO or Interpublic. People working on your account as a punishment or a rookie assignment.

“所以就是这样。你现在要和史密斯、约翰逊一起工作，这些人要么在福特对华项目上搞砸了，要么刚毕业，以前从未做过大型广告活动。这就是你从布拉德福德、BBDO或埃培智集团那里得到的。这些人要么是受罚，要么是新手任务，才会被派来负责你的项目。”

“‘But for us, you’re not some small-market account to be mistreated. Not at all. We’d give Volka to our most senior people, and these are people who all turned down jobs at the Big 5. Our people don’t want to work on Coke or Nestlé or Exxon, because those are big, boring accounts where careers go to die. Our people want to do real ad work—they want to make advertising to sell your cars in the UK to tens of thousands of new buyers. In other words, our most senior people live and breathe and will practically die to get onto a Volka account, and they will stake their careers on doing it right.’”

“但对我们来说，你们可不是什么可以随意对待的小客户。绝对不是。我们会把Volka交给我们最资深的团队负责，而这些人都是拒绝了五大广告公司的工作邀请。我们的人不想去服务可口可乐、雀巢或者埃克森美孚，因为那些都是规模庞大、枯燥乏味的客户，在那里，职业生涯就等于走向终结。我们的人想做真正的广告工作——他们想制作广告，把你们的汽车卖给英国成千上万的新买家。换句话说，我们最资深的团队对Volka这个客户无比热爱，甚至愿意为此付出一切，他们会把自己的职业生涯押在做好这件事上。”

I shrugged and smiled.

我耸了耸肩，笑了笑。

“Anyway,” I said, “that’s what I’d tell Volka.”

“总之，”我说，“我会这么告诉沃尔卡。”

Simon and his team were scrambling to write down every word, because I was talking fast. In reality, this was a simple Flash Roll I’d delivered a thousand times. The same script works in virtually every industry. But to Simon it was all new and fresh and exciting, and his team was eating up every word.

西蒙和他的团队手忙脚乱地记下每一个字，因为我语速很快。实际上，这只是一个我做过无数次的简单演讲稿。同样的稿子几乎适用于所有行业。但对西蒙来说，一切都是新鲜的、令人兴奋的，他的团队对我说的每一个字都如饥似渴。

“Bollocks, then, let’s do it,” Simon said finally. “Whatever it costs. We want to hire you to win the deal back.”

“那好吧，就这么办，”西蒙最后说道。“不管付出什么代价，我们都要雇你把这笔生意赢回来。”

“OK, good,” I said, just beginning to realize what I was getting myself into. “Here is what we’re going to do. Simon and I are going to give the people at Volka a call and talk them into giving us another shot at the pitch. Then we are all getting on a plane, and going to spend two weeks on the ground in beautiful downtown Brinz-Prisk, near Volka headquarters, so we have a much better understanding of just what the hell it is we’re trying to sell.”

“好的，没问题，”我说，这才开始意识到自己即将面临什么。“我们打算这么做。我和西蒙会给Volka的人打个电话，说服他们再给我们一次机会。然后我们全家会坐飞机去美丽的布林茨-普里斯克市中心，那里离Volka总部很近，待上两周，这样我们就能更清楚地了解我们到底在推销什么。”

A SECOND BITE AT THE APPLE

再咬一口苹果

In my business, usually no means no. So the first thing I was worried about was that maybe I’d been a bit too confident about how easy it would be to get a second pitch lined up. And while I was giving that “go get ’em tiger” speech, I didn’t realize I was the poor SOB who was going to have to make all this actually happen. Before, I’d been talking more in the abstract. Now I would have to get to work.

在我的行业里，通常“不”就是“不”。所以我首先担心的是，我可能太自信了，以为安排第二次提案会很容易。当我还在发表那番“加油，老虎！”的豪言壮语时，我却没意识到，真正要靠我自己把这一切变成现实的，竟然是我自己。之前我只是在纸上谈兵，现在我得开始动手了。

I dialed the number Simon had given me, and slipped on the oversize noise-canceling Bluetooth headset with boom-mic I always wear for important calls. “Hi, Josef,” I said when I got their director of marketing on the line. “This is Oren Klaff calling from 12 Kings. Listen, Simon asked me to come on board specifically to take a look at your account, because we feel we could have done better.
