Truth is, the first pitch meeting was rushed, and we’d like another bite at the apple.”

我拨通了西蒙给我的号码，戴上我平时接重要电话时都会戴的超大号降噪蓝牙耳机，耳机带麦克风杆。“你好，约瑟夫，”电话接通后，我是他们的市场总监。“我是12 Kings公司的奥伦·克拉夫。听着，西蒙特意让我来负责你们的业务，因为我们觉得我们本可以做得更好。说实话，第一次提案会议太仓促了，我们想再争取一次机会。”

“Didn’t Simon tell you?” Josef asked in a thick Eastern European accent. “We already went in another direction. We’re announcing next week.”

“西蒙没告诉你吗？”约瑟夫用浓重的东欧口音问道，“我们已经另寻他路了。下周公布。”

“Yes, I understand you’ve decided on Bradford. But I think you ought to give us another look. We feel strongly about it. I think it’s worth your while to do a quick second round meeting with us.” I paused and lowered my voice slightly. “And it would be a shame if word got out in the agency world that you only give your biggest accounts to your buddies at Bradford-McCoy. Why would anybody want to waste time bidding on Volka proposals after that? I mean, why should the best new agencies bid on an account that is just going to end up at Bradford anyway? Look, I understand—if they are the only firm you ever want to use, then go ahead. . . . But think about it this way for a moment . . .”

“是的，我知道您已经决定选择布拉德福德。但我认为您应该再考虑一下我们。我们对此充满信心。我认为您值得花点时间与我们进行第二轮会面。”我停顿了一下，略微压低了声音。“如果广告界知道您只把最大的客户交给布拉德福德-麦考伊的哥们儿，那就太可惜了。那样的话，谁还会浪费时间去竞标沃尔卡的方案呢？我的意思是，那些优秀的新兴广告公司为什么要竞标一个最终肯定会落入布拉德福德手中的客户呢？听着，我明白——如果您只想和他们合作，那就随您便吧……但请您换个角度想一想……”

Then I started speaking at a faster pace and used the same Flash Roll I’d given Simon. “At Bradford, your account would be small . . .”

然后我加快语速，用了之前教给西蒙的那套“快速开场白”。“在布拉德福德，你的账户会很小……”

From there I went into the full pitch, giving all the necessary details and industry jargon and then my suggested solution.

然后我就开始全面阐述我的观点，提供了所有必要的细节和行业术语，以及我提出的解决方案。

There were a tense few moments of silence. Surprisingly, Josef made only light-duty protests before he agreed with me. “OK, we can accept a second review; that’s a reasonable request. On our end, all the key decision makers will be together in six days for a quarterly meeting at the factory headquarters,” he told me. “If you have prepared a better pitch, this will be the time to present it.”

一阵令人窒息的沉默之后，约瑟夫出乎意料地只是略作抗议，便同意了我的提议。“好吧，我们可以接受第二次审查；这是个合理的要求。我们这边，所有关键决策者将在六天后齐聚工厂总部，召开季度会议，”他告诉我，“如果你准备了更好的方案，那就到时候再做陈述。”

“Thank you, Josef,” I said. “That would be perfect.” I hung up the phone and immediately called Simon over. “We’re on. But we only have six days to prepare, not a few weeks. Let’s take our team to Prague, ASAP—and book the economy seats, please.”

“谢谢你，约瑟夫，”我说，“那太好了。”我挂断电话，立刻叫西蒙过来。“就这么定了。但我们只有六天时间准备，不是几周。咱们尽快带队去布拉格——记得订经济舱的票。”

“The cheap seats are pure torture,” Simon said irritably.

“便宜的座位简直是折磨，”西蒙烦躁地说。

“Yes, I know,” I said. “But we’re trying to win Volka, not Rolls-Royce, so we go economy all the way.”

“是的，我知道，”我说。“但我们的目标是赢得沃尔卡，而不是劳斯莱斯，所以我们会全力以赴节省成本。”

WELCOME TO BOHEMIA

欢迎来到波西米亚

The picturesque city of Brinz-Prisk, nestled along the lush banks of the Jizera River, is located in the heart of Bohemia, about eighty miles from Prague. It’s hard to find any aspect of the city that hasn’t been heavily influenced by Volka, and it’s hard to miss the Volka factory when you arrive in the city. The auto manufacturer had a major hand in the development of the Czech Republic’s economy and culture over the past hundred years.

风景如画的布林茨-普里斯克小城坐落在郁郁葱葱的伊泽拉河畔，位于波西米亚中心地带，距离布拉格约80英里。这座城市几乎处处都深受沃尔卡汽车的影响，当你抵达这座城市时，很难忽略沃尔卡工厂。在过去的一百年里，这家汽车制造商对捷克共和国的经济和文化发展做出了巨大贡献。

In the nineteenth century, the town was known as Jerusalem on the Jizera, and there is a sixteenth-century Jewish cemetery that still exists inside the city limits. The town itself was named for the ancient castle Brinz-Prisk, which still towers over the city from atop the ghostly Rhube Rocks. You’ll also find Catholic monuments, Roman architecture, plenty of bars and beer by the barrelful, and a peculiar local penchant for modern-day jousting, which I don’t understand at all.

十九世纪时，这座小镇被称为伊泽拉河畔的耶路撒冷，城内至今仍保留着一座十六世纪的犹太公墓。小镇的名字来源于古老的布林茨-普里斯克城堡，这座城堡至今仍巍然耸立在幽暗的鲁贝岩之上，俯瞰着整座城市。你还能在这里看到天主教纪念碑、罗马式建筑、数不胜数的酒吧和桶装啤酒，以及当地人对现代马上比武的独特爱好——对此我完全无法理解。

Of the top ten things to do in the city, five involve the Volka factory, three involve church, and the remaining two are bars. And then, of course, there is jousting. They also have a leaning tower, which isn’t as famous as the one in Pisa, even though it’s about to topple over. Basically, Brinz-Prisk is a manufacturing town in a romantic, old European setting.

在布林茨-普里斯克这座城市十大必游景点中，五项与沃尔卡工厂有关，三项与教堂有关，剩下的两项则与酒吧有关。当然，还有马上比武。这里还有一座斜塔，虽然摇摇欲坠，但远不如比萨斜塔那么出名。总而言之，布林茨-普里斯克是一座充满浪漫气息的古老欧洲风情的制造业小镇。

Simon, three of the 12 Kings “disruptive geniuses,” and I landed at Václav Havel Airport Prague. We were two and a half hours behind schedule, and they were out of cars at the airport, so we hailed a couple of Liftago’s and hit the road. We toured the Volka museum, the factory, and even the gift shops. Everywhere we went, we learned more about the company’s backstory.

西蒙、三位“颠覆性天才”——“十二国王”之一——和我抵达了布拉格瓦茨拉夫·哈维尔机场。我们比原计划晚了两个半小时，机场也没有车了，所以我们叫了几辆Liftago巴士就出发了。我们参观了Volka博物馆、工厂，甚至还逛了逛礼品店。每到一处，我们都能了解到更多关于这家公司发展历程的信息。

We learned Volka is a proud brand, with deep roots that represent the history and aspirations of the Czech Republic. In the past, Volka had made all the “world’s worst cars” lists, yet it’s one of motoring’s most unkillable companies. The Czech-based marque has been making cars for a hundred years, a feat equaled by only a handful of automotive firms. Anyone familiar with the design and quality of Eastern Bloc cars might wonder how Volka, of all brands, managed to stay in business while hundreds of “better” automotive companies bought the farm. And Volka hasn’t just survived, but has thrived over the years, selling more than twenty-five million cars.

我们了解到，沃尔卡是一个引以为傲的品牌，其深厚的根基代表着捷克共和国的历史和抱负。过去，沃尔卡曾多次登上“世界最差汽车”榜单，但它却是汽车行业最顽强的品牌之一。这家捷克汽车制造商已经生产汽车一百年了，这一成就鲜有其他汽车公司能够企及。任何熟悉东欧集团汽车设计和质量的人都可能会好奇，在数百家“更优秀”的汽车公司纷纷倒闭的情况下，沃尔卡是如何做到生存下来的。而沃尔卡不仅生存了下来，而且多年来蓬勃发展，累计销量超过2500万辆。

Volka’s founders were a welder and a gunmaker. They started off manufacturing bicycles and guns in 1895, and switched to their first automobiles a decade later. The Volka 200 looked like a cross between a lawn mower and wheelbarrow and topped out at a dizzying 40 mph—so these were not cars that you bought for speed or looks. But it was beautifully constructed and, man, was it tough . From the beginning Volka vehicles were defined by economy, efficiency, and sturdiness. They were not the fanciest car in town, but they were the most sensible and the most reliable, much like Czechs themselves.

Volka的创始人是一位焊工和一位枪械制造商。他们于1895年开始生产自行车和枪支，十年后转而生产第一辆汽车。Volka 200的外形像是割草机和独轮车的混合体，最高时速只有令人眼花缭乱的40英里/小时——所以，这可不是那种追求速度或外观的车。但它的做工精良，而且非常坚固耐用。从一开始，Volka汽车就以经济、高效和耐用为特点。它们或许不是城里最豪华的汽车，但却是最明智、最可靠的，就像捷克人本身一样。

From 1948 to 1991, when the Soviet Union’s Iron Curtain was draped around Czechoslovakia, Volka came under government control. During that period, the brand quality and creativity fell far behind Western automotive standards.

从1948年到1991年，苏联的铁幕笼罩着捷克斯洛伐克，沃尔卡汽车公司也处于政府的控制之下。在此期间，该品牌的质量和创新能力远远落后于西方汽车标准。

Then, in 2012, Wolfgang Schmidt took over as Volka’s CEO. Schmidt, a former mechanic, was the sales and marketing director at Porsche. This was the guy we would have to convince if we wanted to pull this account away from Bradford-McCoy. He was dedicated to making Volka a dynamic global company, a shining representative of the Czech Republic—and establishing Bohemia as one of the cradles of European automobile manufacturing innovation. He could achieve his vision only by making a breakthrough in the consumer’s mind about Volka, which led him to search for a brilliant ad agency to pull it off. Convince Schmidt, and all other decision makers would fall in line. He was our target.

2012年，沃尔夫冈·施密特接任沃尔卡首席执行官。施密特曾是一名机械师，后来担任保时捷的销售和市场总监。如果我们想从布拉德福德-麦考伊广告公司手中拿下这个客户，就必须说服他。他致力于将沃尔卡打造成为一家充满活力的全球性公司，成为捷克共和国的杰出代表，并将波西米亚打造成为欧洲汽车制造创新摇篮之一。他要想实现这一愿景，就必须在消费者心中树立沃尔卡的全新形象，因此他开始寻找一家优秀的广告公司来完成这项任务。只要说服了施密特，其他所有决策者都会乖乖听话。他就是我们的目标。

That night, in what was considered the third-nicest hotel in the city but was really more reminiscent of a college dorm, our team was lying around the living room drinking beer, exhausted from a long day of traveling but in good spirits.

当晚，在这家被认为是城里第三好的酒店（但实际上更像是大学宿舍）里，我们的团队躺在客厅里喝啤酒，虽然经过一整天的旅行很累，但精神状态很好。

I had my laptop open and was starting to write down some ideas for the new pitch. “I’m tougher than I look,” I said, typing as I spoke. “Volka is a way of telling people that I’m practical, not cheap. I’m tough, and in this world, I either find a way, or make one.” Then I paused and looked up. A very bad thought had entered my mind. “All these guys speak English, right?” I asked. “What level of vocabulary can I use during this pitch—third grade, college, MBA?”

我打开笔记本电脑，开始记录一些新方案的想法。“我比看起来更强硬，”我一边打字一边说。“Volka这个名字是想告诉大家，我务实，而不是吝啬。我很坚强，在这个世界上，要么找到出路，要么自己创造出路。”然后我停顿了一下，抬起头。一个非常糟糕的念头涌上心头。“这些人都会说英语，对吧？”我问。“我这次推介可以用什么水平的词汇——小学三年级、大学还是MBA？”

Silence. Nobody answered me.

一片寂静。没有人回答我。

“Hello?” I prodded.

“喂？”我问道。

Finally, Jonathan, 12 Kings’ top copywriter, spoke up. “Oren, this is a Czech client. Has to be done in Czech.”

最后，12 Kings 的首席文案撰稿人乔纳森开口说道：“奥伦，这是个捷克客户，必须用捷克语写。”

My heart sank. This was certainly bad news. “So who gave the pitch last time?” I asked.

我心头一沉。这肯定是个坏消息。“上次是谁做的提案？”我问道。

Trevor raised his hand. As the head of finance and accounting, he hadn’t spoken much until now. “I speak German, Czech, all that stuff,” he stated proudly. “I can do it, no problem.”

特雷弗举起了手。作为财务主管，他之前很少说话。“我会说德语、捷克语，所有这些语言我都会，”他自豪地说。“我能做到，没问题。”

The accountant? “No offense,” I said. “You seem like a nice guy, but I’m not sure you’re our best option here.”

会计？“别介意，”我说，“你看起来是个不错的人，但我不太确定你是不是我们最好的选择。”

Trevor had a nervous demeanor, wrung his hands while talking, and said “umm” a lot. Could I train him to deliver our master presentation? Sure I could. But it would take three weeks—not three days.

特雷弗神情紧张，说话时双手不停地搓着，还经常“嗯”一声。我能训练他做我们的主题演讲吗？当然可以。但这需要三周时间，而不是三天。

“I need someone with acting talent, someone with poise and calm, with a presence.” Had I said that aloud?

“我需要一个有表演天赋、沉着冷静、有气场的人。” 我刚才把这些话说出口了吗？

Before Trevor could register what I’d said and feel insulted, Jonathan pointed at the TV screen and said, “Someone like that guy.”

特雷弗还没来得及反应过来我说了什么，还没来得及感到被冒犯，乔纳森就指着电视屏幕说：“像他那样的人。”

We couldn’t figure out how to change the channel from the Czech soap opera playing on the TV, and had left it on in the background. Jonathan was pointing at the star of the show, a heartthrob businessman type who at that moment was wowing a room of other business types with some kind of impassioned speech—no idea what it was about. I had to admit, Jonathan was right. That was the kind of guy we needed. A warm face with cool blue eyes, a voice that could read the phone book and make it sound interesting, someone who could learn the script, deliver the lines, stick to the plan, and do it all in the local language.

我们搞不懂怎么换台，电视上正播放着捷克肥皂剧，只好让它在后台播放着。乔纳森指着剧中的男主角，一个英俊潇洒的商人，此刻正对着一群商人发表着激情澎湃的演讲——我们完全不知道他在讲什么。我不得不承认，乔纳森说得对。这正是我们需要的那种人。一张温暖的脸庞，一双清澈的蓝眼睛，声音洪亮，就算念电话簿都能念得生动有趣；他能记住台词，能把台词念出来，能严格按照计划执行，而且还能用当地语言完成这一切。

A thought struck me. “I mean, it’s Czech Republic TV,” I said. “There’s no SAG or AFTRA [American Federation of Television and Radio Artists]. How much could it possibly cost to hire this guy for a few days?”

我突然想到：“我的意思是，这是捷克电视台，”我说。“那里没有美国演员工会（SAG）或美国电视和广播艺术家联合会（AFTRA）。请这个人来几天能花多少钱呢？”

Catching on quickly, Jonathan agreed we had to throw some serious money at this problem. He said, “Yeah, let’s find him, buy him out for the week, pay him ten thousand, twenty thousand—whatever, who cares? The meeting is on Friday; we need this!”

乔纳森很快就明白了，同意我们必须花大价钱解决这个问题。他说：“是啊，我们得找到他，把他买下来，让他休息一周，给他一万、两万——随便多少都行，管他呢？会议周五开，我们需要这笔钱！”

With a bit of quick googling, I found his agent, and a short while and two thousand euros later we had hired Lukas, the best actor in the Czech Republic (at least as far as we were concerned).

经过一番简单的谷歌搜索，我找到了他的经纪人，不久之后，我们花了2000欧元就聘请了卢卡斯，他是捷克共和国最好的演员（至少在我们看来是这样）。

Now that we had officially hired an actor who knew nothing about pitching or advertising or Volka manufacturing, I had three days to prepare him to be in front of a huge client, where he would need to tell our story, deliver a complicated pitch, and negotiate a 10 million euro advertising account for Volka UK, an account we had already lost a week ago.

既然我们已经正式聘请了一位对推销、广告或 Volka 生产一无所知的演员，我只有三天时间来让他做好准备，去面对一位大客户，在那里他需要讲述我们的故事，进行复杂的推销，并为 Volka 英国公司谈判一个价值 1000 万欧元的广告账户，而我们一周前已经失去了这个账户。

“I need a coffee,” Simon said.

“我需要一杯咖啡，”西蒙说。

I was thinking, “Move over, coffee, this is a job for alcohol.”

我当时想，“咖啡靠边站，这才是酒的用武之地。”

A SURPRISE IN THE WAITING ROOM

候诊室里的惊喜

The Volka factory is a giant facility sprawled across the otherwise motionless meadowlands of the Czech Republic. The plant itself is organized and clean in a way that only Eastern Europeans can conceive, with spotless white pine floors and gleaming assembly lines. As we walked in, I glanced through an open doorway to the factory floor, where conveyer belts carried half-built vehicles past assembly and inspection stations. Men and women in white jumpsuits examined every detail, testing every aspect of the machinery. The place was literally humming.

沃尔卡工厂是一座庞大的厂房，坐落在捷克共和国原本静谧的草地上。工厂内部井然有序，干净整洁，这种景象恐怕只有东欧人才会想象：一尘不染的白松木地板，闪闪发光的装配线。我们走进工厂时，我透过敞开的门瞥见了车间，传送带将半成品车辆运送到各个装配和检验站。身穿白色工作服的男男女女仔细检查每一个细节，测试机器的每一个部件。整个工厂运转得嗡嗡作响。

The executive offices were in the south end of the factory, in a building that looked a lot like the entrance to any building you might find somewhere more familiar, like New Jersey, only this had better landscaping and reliable trash removal.

行政办公室位于工厂南端，那栋建筑看起来很像你在新泽西州等更熟悉的地方看到的任何建筑物的入口，只是这里的景观更好，垃圾清运也更可靠。

Leading our team was Lukas, our Czech soap star.

带领我们团队的是卢卡斯，他是我们捷克肥皂剧明星。

The past three days had been a whirlwind. I’d spent every waking minute with Lukas and I was completely burnt out. In person, the guy was nothing like his businessman personality on TV. He talked incomprehensibly fast and said, “Please, you know what I mean?” every two seconds. He would argue with a point I was making, then would scowl and pout for an hour. Then he was happy and easygoing, until the next meltdown. It was the opposite of what I needed.

过去三天简直像一场旋风。我醒着的每一分钟都和卢卡斯待在一起，已经筋疲力尽了。真人跟电视上那个商人形象完全不一样。他说话语速快得让人听不懂，而且每隔两秒钟就说一句“拜托，你知道我的意思吗？”。他会反驳我的观点，然后皱着眉头撅嘴，一闹就是一个小时。之后他又会变得开心随和，直到下一次情绪崩溃。这完全不是我需要的。

Every time I attempted to lead him on a training exercise, it turned into a lengthy ordeal as he monologued about the importance of “method acting” and needing to know the motivation of his character so he was perfectly in sync with the actions and reactions of the story’s antagonist—so the plot’s rising action would correctly climax in a moment of gravitas leading to an emotional denouement for the audience.

每次我试图引导他进行训练时，都会变成一场漫长的折磨，因为他会滔滔不绝地讲述“方法演技”的重要性，以及需要了解角色的动机，以便与故事反派的行动和反应完全同步——这样情节的上升动作才能正确地在庄严的时刻达到高潮，从而为观众带来情感上的结局。

“Hey, buddy,” I said repeatedly, “we aren’t doing Shakespeare here. Let’s just focus on the scripts as they are written and not get caught up with all of that.” But it was no use. He claimed he could not act until he had completed his “inner work.”

“嘿，伙计，”我反复说道，“我们又不是在演莎士比亚。咱们就专注于剧本本身，别纠结那些乱七八糟的事。” 但都没用。他声称，在完成“内心功课”之前，他无法演戏。

At one point I came dangerously close to firing him when he wouldn’t stop asking me about my “true purpose” in the role-play we were doing. “My purpose is to get the money,” I kept repeating. “To win the deal.” Apparently that wasn’t the right answer.

有一次，他不停地追问我在角色扮演中的“真正目的”是什么，我差点就把他炒了。“我的目的是拿到钱，”我反复说道，“拿下这笔交易。” 显然，这并不是正确答案。

Anyway, as difficult as the guy was—and seriously, he was a bit nuts—in the end he was really a brilliant actor, which I will get to in a moment. And it turned out he used to drive a Volka, it was his first car, first speeding ticket, first romp in the backseat, and so on.

总之，虽然这人很难相处——说真的，他有点疯——但最终他确实是个才华横溢的演员，这一点我稍后会详细说明。后来才知道，他以前开的是一辆沃尔卡，那是他的第一辆车，也是他第一次超速罚单、第一次在后座上寻欢作乐等等的缘由。

—

FIGHTING LIKE A married couple, we had practiced the key elements of the scripts over and over again during those three days, and the pitch really started coming to life.

就像一对夫妻一样，我们在那三天里反复练习剧本的关键要素，提案也真正开始鲜活起来。

But now it was time to put all that training to the test. As we stepped into the lobby of the Volka corporate headquarters building, our fate was in the hands of Lukas the 33-year-old temperamental Czech method actor and soap opera star.

但现在是时候检验我们所有的训练成果了。当我们踏入沃尔卡公司总部大楼的大厅时，我们的命运就掌握在卢卡斯手中了，这位33岁、脾气暴躁的捷克方法派演员兼肥皂剧明星。

The receptionist nodded when we introduced ourselves, and led us down a long hallway to a small but comfortable executive waiting area. The six of us—Simon, Lukas, Trevor, and I, along with two creative types—sat down on a couch right outside the CEO’s office complex. Just across from us sat a pair of men in charcoal suits with tightly cropped hair and narrow ties, who exchanged knowing glances as we sat down.

我们自我介绍后，接待员点点头，领着我们穿过一条长长的走廊，来到一个虽小但舒适的高管等候区。我们六个人——西蒙、卢卡斯、特雷弗和我，还有两位创意人员——在首席执行官办公室外的一张沙发上坐了下来。对面坐着两位身穿炭灰色西装、头发剪得很短、系着窄领带的男士，我们坐下时，他们交换了一个心照不宣的眼神。

“Hello, gents,” Simon said, engaging the men in friendly conversation, as he does with every person he meets. “American? What brings you this way?”

“你们好，先生们，”西蒙说着，像对待遇到的每个人一样，友好地和他们攀谈起来。“美国人？你们怎么会来这里呢？”

“From Bradford-McCoy, New York,” said one of the men. “Here to meet with Wolfgang. So you’re Simon from 12 Kings, right? Well, it’s my second trip to Czech Republic in two weeks, thanks to all your whining and complaining about a second pitch meeting.”

“我来自纽约的布拉德福德-麦考伊公司，”其中一人说道，“来见沃尔夫冈。你就是《十二王》里的西蒙，对吧？嗯，这已经是我两周内第二次来捷克了，都怪你一直抱怨要开第二次提案会议。”

Wait. Bradford guys at our pitch meeting? Before we could ask any questions, an admin poked her head through the door and waved us all in. There was nothing else to do. We stood up, along with the two guys from Bradford, and followed her into the CEO’s massive offices.

等等。布拉德福德那帮人居然来参加我们的提案会议？还没等我们开口，一个行政人员就探头进来，挥手示意我们进去。没办法，我们只好站起来，和那两个布拉德福德来的家伙一起，跟着她走进CEO那间巨大的办公室。

The interior of the Volka executive office suite was Spartan and felt strangely empty compared to the quirky furnishings of 12 Kings’ offices. It was large, and jutted out from the rest of the building so that it had windows on three sides. But we only had a few seconds to take all this in before we were shuffled over to some empty chairs and told to have a seat. The guys from Bradford sat down next to us.

Volka高管办公室的内部装潢十分简朴，与12 Kings办公室里别具一格的家具相比，显得格外空旷。办公室面积很大，从建筑主体向外突出，三面都有窗户。但我们只有几秒钟的时间来消化这一切，就被安排到几把空椅子旁坐下。来自布拉德福德的几个人坐在了我们旁边。

“Next, we have representatives from the ad agencies here for a final decision meeting on the new campaign,” a little man holding a clipboard and wearing a Volka polo shirt said, announcing us to the room. I glanced over at the men seated in the back of the office. Wolfgang was easy to spot. He sat right out front with an attitude of absolute authority. Obviously, he was the boss. Just from the body language, and having been in thousands of these kinds of meetings before, I could also make out the CFO, COO, director of marketing, and even the head of the legal department. I noticed a few board members were present as well. This was a big decision. The men nodded and looked toward us as our introduction continued: “First, we have Bradford. And second, we have . . . um . . .”—the man glanced down at his clipboard for an awkward moment—“the Kingsford agency.”

“接下来，我们邀请了广告公司的代表来开会，最终决定新广告方案。”一个身材矮小、拿着写字板、穿着Volka polo衫的男人说道，同时向我们介绍着房间。我瞥了一眼坐在办公室后排的男人们。沃尔夫冈很容易辨认。他坐在最前面，一副绝对权威的姿态。显然，他是老板。仅凭肢体语言，再加上我之前参加过成千上万次类似的会议，我还能认出首席财务官、首席运营官、市场总监，甚至还有法务主管。我还注意到几位董事会成员也在场。这可是个重大决定。在我们继续介绍时，男人们点点头，看向我们：“首先是布拉德福德广告公司。其次是……嗯……”——男人尴尬地低头看了看手中的写字板——“金斯福德广告公司。”

“Bollocks,” Simon whispered, nudging me in the ribs. “They got our name wrong.”

“糟了，”西蒙低声说道，用胳膊肘捅了捅我的肋骨。“他们把我们的名字搞错了。”

“Who cares?” I whispered back excitedly. “At least they said it in English . I’ll be able to do the pitch myself. We won’t need to use Lukas!”

“谁在乎呢？”我兴奋地低声回应道，“至少他们用英语说的。我可以自己做提案了。我们不需要卢卡斯了！”

Just at that moment, the executives offered some polite welcomes and the man with the clipboard waved at us to send our representative forward. One of the Bradford-McCoy men stood up and strode toward the first podium. Oh, God. This was high school debate club all over again. I got up, heart thumping in chest, and stepped over to my assigned podium.

就在这时，几位高管礼貌地致意，拿着写字板的男士示意我们派代表上前。布拉德福德-麦考伊公司的一位男士站起身，大步走向第一个讲台。天哪！这简直就像高中辩论社的场景重现。我心跳加速，站起身，走到我被分配到的讲台前。

DEBATE CLUB FOR 10 MILLION EUROS

辩论俱乐部获1000万欧元

“Why should we pick your firm to create our new UK ad campaign?” Wolfgang asked, gesturing toward the man from Bradford.

“我们为什么要选择贵公司来制作我们在英国的新广告宣传活动？”沃尔夫冈问道，同时指向那位来自布拉德福德的男士。

“Thank you, I’m Kevin, representing Bradford-McCoy,” he said with a confident smile. “As one of the largest, most well-established marketing firms with major offices in London and New York, we are excited to partner with Volka on this fantastic project. We think you have been an Eastern European brand for far too long and we want to make you more well-known in the West, including the UK. We want to show Western Europe how a Volka automobile meets their needs. So stop hogging all of that greatness for yourselves. Let us reserve you a seat at the global commerce table with the big guys. We have a plan that will serve up another half billion in revenue for you, within twelve months.”

“谢谢，我是凯文，代表布拉德福德-麦考伊公司，”他自信地笑着说。“作为一家规模最大、历史最悠久的营销公司之一，我们在伦敦和纽约都设有主要办事处，我们非常高兴能与沃尔卡合作开展这个意义非凡的项目。我们认为，沃尔卡长期以来一直被视为东欧品牌，我们希望提升沃尔卡在西方，包括英国的知名度。我们希望向西欧展示沃尔卡汽车如何满足他们的需求。所以，别再独占这些优势了。让我们助您在全球商业舞台上与巨头们并肩而立。我们有一个计划，将在十二个月内为您带来五亿美元的额外收入。”

I glanced at Simon and he was sitting stiffly, tight-lipped with arms crossed, because I had been 100 percent right about Bradford’s pitch and now he knew it. These guys didn’t talk about how creative they were or how many awards they had won or what colors they had invented. They spoke the language of money. No time to gloat at being right again, though, because Kevin continued to give a very credible presentation about market size, cost-per-customer acquisition, advertising metrics, KPIs, and return on investment.

我瞥了一眼西蒙，他僵硬地坐着，嘴唇紧抿，双臂交叉抱在胸前，因为我对布拉德福德的预测百分之百正确，现在他也明白了。这些人从不谈论他们的创意有多棒，得了多少奖，或者发明了什么颜色。他们只谈钱。不过，我没时间沾沾自喜，因为凯文继续就市场规模、获客成本、广告指标、关键绩效指标和投资回报率等问题做了非常有说服力的演讲。

Eventually, his presentation petered out and I was up to make the rebuttal.

最终，他的发言逐渐结束，轮到我进行反驳。

“Hi, I’m Oren,” I began, “with 12 Kings. I hope you take my comments in the spirit they are intended, because I think the Bradford plan we all just heard will take Volka in completely the wrong direction.”

“大家好，我是奥伦，”我开口说道，“来自 12 Kings。我希望你们能理解我话里的意思，因为我认为我们刚才听到的布拉德福德计划会把沃尔卡带向完全错误的方向。”

I saw them looking at me skeptically. As the losers of the previous pitch, we were starting off in a handicapped position, so I knew it would be especially important to open with status alignment. “Think about it for moment,” I said, and pointed at the Bradford team. “They want to adapt your cars and your brand to fit European values. But what is so good about Western European values? Seriously, not much. We think Western European values are in decay. Oh, I get it—England, Germany, France are the nations who made the modern world truly modern and ushered humankind into the great cultural Renaissance. Sure, these countries gave us the Mona Lisa , Romeo and Juliet , Beethoven’s Fifth, and a bunch of other cultural achievements. But all that happened centuries ago. Today, the sun is rising in the East, and Western aesthetic values and moral values are fading fast. In the UK, most every consumer product is fifty percent or one hundred percent made in China, which is to say it’s designed by a computer, made cheaply as possible, and meant to be thrown away in a year. Clocks and watches are digital, books are read online, business meeting attire is sneakers and a T-shirt. Dinner is ordered on an app and arrives in a cardboard box. Millennials in the UK don’t even want cars. Most of them are not going to get a driver’s license.”

我看到他们用怀疑的眼神看着我。作为上一次推介的失败者，我们一开始就处于劣势，所以我知道，在开局阶段就确立地位至关重要。“你们考虑一下，”我说着，指了指布拉德福德队。 “他们想让你的汽车和品牌适应欧洲价值观。但西欧价值观到底好在哪里呢？说真的，没什么好说的。我们认为西欧价值观正在衰落。哦，我明白——英国、德国、法国是真正使现代世界现代化的国家，引领人类进入了伟大的文化复兴。当然，这些国家创造了《蒙娜丽莎》、《罗密欧与朱丽叶》、贝多芬第五交响曲以及其他许多文化成就。但所有这些都发生在几个世纪以前。如今，太阳从东方升起，西方的审美和道德价值观正在迅速消逝。在英国，几乎所有消费品都有百分之五十或百分之百产自中国，也就是说，它们是由电脑设计的，尽可能廉价地生产，并且注定一年后就被丢弃。钟表是电子的，书籍在网上阅读，商务会议的着装是运动鞋和T恤。晚餐通过应用程序订购，然后装在纸盒里送来。英国的千禧一代甚至不想要汽车。他们中的大多数人也不会……”去考个驾照。

I was starting to get nods of approval from the men in the room. Bingo , a little Status Alignment achieved. These men felt like I understood them, that the West was not superior to the East. Now I would move to the next step using another flipped script. I’d have to pitch their own brand to them to demonstrate my deep understanding of their company, culture, and product.

我开始收到房间里男士们的点头认可。Bingo！初步达成了地位认同。他们觉得我理解他们，让他们明白西方并不比东方优越。现在我要换个角度，用另一种方式切入下一步。我要向他们推介他们的品牌，以此展现我对他们公司、文化和产品的深刻理解。

“Why attach ourselves to Western European values?” I asked. “Instead we should be exporting Czech values. Let me explain. No one should try to make you look cooler or hipper than you are, or to reinvent your brand at all. In my experience, that’s very risky. Sometimes it works out. Most of the time, it doesn’t. The best campaign for Volka is one that’s simple and Plain Vanilla. We have prepared a pitch that new customers will recognize immediately because it captures what has made your brand great for a hundred years, and I might tell a prospective Volka owner something like this:

“为什么要固守西欧价值观呢？”我问道。“我们应该输出捷克价值观。让我解释一下。任何人都不应该试图让你看起来比实际更酷或更时髦，或者试图彻底重塑你的品牌。以我的经验来看，这样做风险很大。有时成功，但大多数时候失败。对Volka来说，最好的营销活动就是简单朴实的。我们准备了一套宣传方案，新客户一眼就能认出，因为它抓住了Volka品牌百年来的精髓。我可能会这样跟潜在的Volka用户说：

“Driving a Volka is a way of telling people, I’m practical, not cheap. I’m tough, and I’m the kind of person who can either find a way, or make one. I’m reliable. I may not be from the Czech Republic, but my values sure match, because I have an inner strength I don’t need to show off. I’m strong and I’m uncomplicated. My life has just two purposes: work and family. When I’m working, I do my business without a fuss, I deal with the things that come across my path, and people can rely on me. At home, we are not too fancy, we tell each other the truth, we make time for each other and appreciate what God has provided.

开沃尔卡（Volka）就等于告诉别人，我务实，不吝啬。我坚韧不拔，总能找到解决办法，或者自己创造办法。我值得信赖。我或许不是捷克人，但我的价值观绝对契合，因为我内心强大，无需炫耀。我坚强而简单。我的人生只有两个目标：工作和家庭。工作时，我做事干脆利落，处理遇到的各种事情，人们可以信赖我。在家，我们生活简朴，彼此坦诚相待，抽出时间陪伴家人，并感恩上帝的恩赐。

“Driving a Volka is not a flashy thing to do. Volka cars are not designed by futuristic robots and 3-D lasers from China. They are designed using pencils, paper, and clay models that are carefully sculpted by Bohemian craftsmen. People might think our designers are too old, drink beer that is too dark, and take too many smoke breaks. But we like them exactly for these reasons, and because they don’t design the swoopiest, shiniest, coolest-looking car in the world. I think Kia does that just fine, which is why their marketing depends on singing hamsters. Instead, the people in this room are designing a car like the one my dad would have bought—except with better brakes, a more reliable engine, and better overall features to keep the passengers safe.

开一辆沃尔卡汽车并不是什么引人注目的事。沃尔卡汽车并非出自中国的未来机器人和3D激光之手，而是由波西米亚工匠用铅笔、纸张和黏土模型精心雕琢而成。人们或许会觉得我们的设计师年纪太大，喝的啤酒颜色太深，而且烟瘾太大。但我们恰恰喜欢他们，正是因为他们如此，也因为他们没有设计出世界上最炫酷、最闪亮、最时髦的汽车。我觉得起亚在这方面做得已经很好了，所以他们的营销才依赖于会唱歌的仓鼠。而我们，在座的各位，正在设计一款我父亲会买的车——只不过它配备了更好的刹车、更可靠的发动机，以及更完善的乘客安全配置。

“This is the car my family would want me to have; it’s the car my dad would have bought me. It’s made the old way, but with new stuff that makes it even better. That’s a Volka. It might look utilitarian, but it has brakes that could stop a dump truck, a heater that works at the North Pole, and a motor that never quits. Go anywhere, do anything without a complaint—experience your adventures without having to worry about the machine that’s taking you there.”

“这就是我的家人希望我拥有的车；这就是我父亲会给我买的车。它采用传统工艺制造，但融合了现代科技，性能更胜一筹。这就是沃尔卡。它看起来或许朴实无华，但它的刹车性能足以刹住一辆翻斗卡车，暖气在北极也能正常工作，发动机永不停歇。无论去哪里，无论做什么，都无需抱怨——尽情体验你的冒险之旅，无需担心载你而行的车辆。”

I glanced at the man with the clipboard and he gestured to his wrist. Time to wrap it up. I had to find a way to wrestle this account out of Bradford’s hands into ours and decided on giving a quick Buyer’s Formula.

我瞥了一眼拿着写字板的男人，他指了指自己的手腕。该收尾了。我得想办法把这个客户从布拉德福德手里抢过来，于是决定快速讲解一下买方策略。

“I know you asked what we can do for you in the UK,” I said, getting to the point. “Sure, we can promise you five hundred million euros in new sales . . . we can promise a billion euros too. But the number has no meaning until you find the agency who understands your brand and can communicate with your customers. I’d ask you a question: How would the average worker on your production line sell a car? I’m talking about the guy on the floor who is actually putting the cars together. What does Volka mean to him? That’s what the campaign needs to say and that’s what the agency who creates your UK campaign needs to understand.

“我知道您问的是我们在英国能为您做些什么，”我开门见山地说。“当然，我们可以承诺为您带来五亿欧元的新销售额……我们甚至可以承诺十亿欧元。但是，除非您找到一家了解您的品牌并能与您的客户沟通的代理商，否则这些数字毫无意义。我想问您一个问题：您生产线上的普通工人会如何推销汽车？我指的是那些在车间里实际组装汽车的人。大众汽车对他们来说意味着什么？这才是广告活动需要传达的信息，也是负责您英国广告活动的代理商需要理解的内容。”

“The workers will know how to talk about the cars. The agency’s job is to boil down that talk-track for consumers in the UK. Nothing fancy. So pick the agency your workers would actually pick. At least, that’s what I would do, and I’ve been doing this kind of thing a long time. But of course, I can’t tell you what to do; you guys will obviously do whatever is best for the Company.”

“员工们自然知道如何谈论汽车。广告公司的工作就是把这些术语提炼成英国消费者能理解的内容。没什么花哨的。所以，选择一家你们员工真正会选择的广告公司。至少，我会这么做，而且我从事这行很久了。当然，我不能告诉你们该怎么做；你们肯定会做对公司最有利的事情。”

And I stopped talking.

我停止了说话。

It was Bradford’s turn to explain how bad my idea was. That’s how debates work. But they never got the chance.

轮到布拉德福德解释我的想法有多糟糕了。辩论就是这样。但他们根本没机会。

“Yes!” Wolfgang exclaimed after barely a second had passed. “I love it! So let’s do it.”

“好啊！”沃尔夫冈几乎立刻喊道，“我喜欢！那就这么办吧。”

“Do what?” I wondered.

“做什么？”我疑惑地想。

With that, he jumped up out of his chair. “Come, everyone. To the factory. I want you both to explain all this to our workers directly.”

说完，他猛地从椅子上跳了起来。“都过来，到工厂来。我要你们俩直接跟工人们解释清楚这一切。”

I glanced over at Lukas and he was already looking back at me, eyes wide. We both knew factory workers at Volka Brinz-Prisk don’t speak English and that he was going to be onstage next, which quite possibly meant we were dead.

我瞥了一眼卢卡斯，他正瞪大眼睛看着我。我们都知道沃尔卡·布林茨-普里斯克工厂的工人不会说英语，而且他接下来就要上台了，这意味着我们很可能死定了。

ON THE FACTORY FLOOR AT VOLKA HQ

在沃尔卡总部工厂车间

It was a strange scene, this huge group of executives in suits, trailing their assistants and admin staff, followed by these buttoned-up New York ad guys and, finally, Simon, me, and Lukas bringing up the rear. I was using the extra time to prepare Lukas as much as I could, whispering under my breath.

那场面真够奇特的：一大群西装革履的高管，后面跟着他们的助理和行政人员，再后面是那些衣冠楚楚的纽约广告人，最后，西蒙、我和卢卡斯落在队伍的最后面。我利用这段额外的时间，尽可能多地帮卢卡斯做准备，一边低声说着什么。

“What’s your first step going to be in there?” I asked.

“你进去后的第一步是什么？”我问。

“Status Alignment,” Lukas said. “They need to feel like I’m one of them.”

“地位认同，”卢卡斯说，“他们需要觉得我是他们中的一员。”

“Right,” I said. “And remember you’re going to be talking to factory workers, not corporate executives. The Status Tip-Off will be important to show that even though you look like a corporate executive, you’re really part of the local scene.”

“没错，”我说。“记住，你要和工厂工人交谈，而不是企业高管。身份提示很重要，它能表明，即使你看起来像个企业高管，你实际上也是当地社区的一份子。”

“Yes,” he said, nodding. “I can do that. I know what to say.” Then he reached into his pocket and pulled out a small model car. It was a Volka Speedomatic, an older model from about five years back. He smiled. “My Flash Roll. I sell them this car. And they need to buy, because Oren, I explain Winter Is Coming.”

“是的，”他点点头说，“我可以做到。我知道该怎么说。”说着，他伸手进口袋，掏出一辆小型汽车模型。那是一辆沃尔卡速跑车，大约五年前的老款。他笑了笑。“我的闪电卷轴。我把这辆车卖给他们。他们必须买，因为奥伦，我得跟他们解释，凛冬将至。”

The awkward group of executives and admins and marketing people was now making its way into the main factory. We squeezed through the large sliding door and stepped right up onto the factory floor.

这群略显尴尬的高管、行政人员和市场营销人员正陆续进入主厂房。我们挤过那扇巨大的滑动门，径直踏上了生产车间。

“One more thing,” I whispered to Lukas as we followed the herd toward the front of the room. “These guys are tough-as-nails mechanics and line workers. They are going to be highly skeptical of an outsider wearing a suit, and you’re wearing a really nice suit. How will you stay compelling in the face of that?”

“还有一件事，”我一边跟着人群走向房间前面，一边低声对卢卡斯说，“这些人都是身经百战的机械师和流水线工人。他们肯定会对一个穿着西装的外来者抱有极大的怀疑，而你穿的却是一套非常体面的西装。面对这种情况，你打算如何保持自己的威信呢？”

“I don’t pretend to be big shot. I’m just me, some local guy. Yes, I’m lucky guy to work for ad agency, but no, not a big shot. I stick to guns, not change story to make them happy.” Lukas beamed.

“我并不自诩为大人物。我只是个普通的本地人。没错，能在广告公司工作我很幸运，但绝不是什么大人物。我坚持原则，不会为了讨好别人而改变说法。”卢卡斯笑容满面地说。

Volka’s CEO, Wolfgang, was getting everyone’s attention now. He pressed the emergency shutdown button and brought the humming, whirring, and hissing of the factory to a stop. Each press of the button held the line up for eleven minutes, and cost twenty thousand euros. There was a small area perfect for addressing the crowd of workers, and he stepped onto a little platform, grabbing a microphone that had appeared from a helpful administrative assistant.

沃尔卡公司的首席执行官沃尔夫冈现在吸引了所有人的注意力。他按下紧急停机按钮，工厂里嗡嗡作响、呼呼作响、嘶嘶作响的机器声戛然而止。每次按下按钮，生产线都会停工十一分钟，损失两万欧元。工厂里有一小块地方，正好适合向工人们讲话。他走上一个小平台，从一位热心的行政助理手中接过麦克风。

“Good morning,” he said in Czech, his low voice booming over the small crowd. “These men here have come from advertising agencies. I’d like you to listen to them and help me decide which one understands us the best. Which one of these firms should we hire to tell the UK and maybe even all Western Europe about Volka? Today, I want you to help make the decision.”

“早上好，”他用捷克语说道，低沉的声音在人群中回荡。“这些人来自广告公司。我想请你们听听他们的意见，帮我决定哪家公司最了解我们。我们应该聘请哪家公司来向英国乃至整个西欧推广Volka品牌？今天，我希望你们能帮我做出这个决定。”

Wolfgang gestured toward us to send our representatives forward. I nudged Lukas and he jogged over and climbed up to the platform. He grabbed the microphone with a smile and, unbelievably, followed his training. He started his Status Tip-Off, Czech-style as Trevor translated for me.

沃尔夫冈示意我们派代表上前。我碰了碰卢卡斯，他小跑过来，爬上讲台。他笑着拿起麦克风，令人难以置信的是，他竟然按照训练内容完成了发言。他用捷克式的口吻开始了发言，特雷弗则为我翻译。

“Hi. My name is Lukas. I got my first car when I was eighteen. The parking brake didn’t work, the alarm went off when it rained, and you had to kick the trunk twice to get it to open. Oh yeah, and it only came in two colors. I had the best one: red. But that car was special because it started every time, no matter what . And one time a police officer borrowed my car because his car was stuck in the mud and I was driving around with no problem. Do I really have to tell you what model of car it was?”

“嗨，我叫卢卡斯。我十八岁的时候有了第一辆车。手刹坏了，下雨的时候警报器会响，而且后备箱要踹两脚才能打开。哦对了，它只有两种颜色。我的是最好看的红色。但这辆车很特别，因为它每次都能启动，不管什么情况。有一次，一个警察的车陷在泥里了，就借了我的车，而我开着它到处跑，一点问题都没有。我真的需要告诉你那是什么型号的车吗？”

“The Kovat 480!” someone shouted.

“科瓦特480！”有人喊道。

“Yeah, the 480,” came a few dozen echoes, because every Kovat 480 had the same story and only someone who grew up driving in the Czech Republic would know about the brake, that damn alarm, and the double-kick rear trunk—and how red was the best color.

“是啊，480，”几十个回声传来，因为每辆 Kovat 480 都有着相同的故事，只有在捷克共和国长大、开着车的人才会知道它的刹车、该死的警报器和双踢式后备箱——以及红色是最好的颜色。

“That’s right,” Lukas said. “The 480 was the toughest damn thing on four wheels short of a tank.”

“没错，”卢卡斯说。“除了坦克之外，480型车简直是四轮车里最坚固的玩意儿。”

A low murmur rose up from the workers gathered around the platform. Heads started to nod vigorously. I smiled. Nodding heads and leaning in are always clear signs that Status Alignment has been achieved. I was loving this. Lukas was right on schedule, like he’d been doing this kind of presentation for years.

工人们聚集在站台周围，低声议论起来。他们开始用力点头。我笑了。点头和身体前倾总是表明双方已经达成共识的明显信号。我喜欢这种感觉。卢卡斯的演讲非常顺利，就像他已经做过很多年这类演讲一样。

Now that we had their attention, it was time for Lukas’s Flash Roll. He drew a deep breath and launched, rapid-fire: “Today, your best quality car is the Volka Láska 100, but it has more than thirty competitors! Even though it’s not the cheapest small car out there—that’s the Nissan Versa—it costs less to buy than the Ford Fiesta or VW Polo, and what’s amazing is you still deliver the Láska with alloy wheels, air-con, digital radio, rear parking sensors, automatic emergency braking, and a leather steering wheel. It’s impressive. Sure, I know some of your competition offer fancier technology, but as a safe, dependable supermini, the Láska is very hard to fault. Your real advantage over the other superminis is horsepower. I know you’re still selling the 74 horsepower non-turbo three-cylinder Láska to the older people and the boosted 1 liter Tuned Port Injection in 94 horsepower trim to commuters—the 94 horse version is the one I like to drive. But you really caught the attention of the younger generation with the supercharged 108 bhp horse turbo in the seven-speed twin-clutch DSG automatic. If we could convince you to add a rear spoiler, front air intakes, and a lumpier camshaft—say we get 115 horsepower—we’d have a solid shot at another 250 million euros of annual sales in the supermini segment.”

既然我们已经吸引了他们的注意力，那就该轮到卢卡斯的闪电翻滚了。他深吸一口气，连珠炮似地说道：“如今，你们最好的车是Volka Láska 100，但它的竞争对手超过三十家！虽然它不是市面上最便宜的小型车——最便宜的是日产Versa——但它的售价比福特嘉年华或大众Polo都低，更令人惊叹的是，你们仍然为Láska配备了合金轮毂、空调、数字收音机、后驻车雷达、自动紧急制动和真皮方向盘。这令人印象深刻。当然，我知道你们的一些竞争对手提供了更先进的技术，但作为一款安全可靠的小型车，Láska几乎无可挑剔。你们相对于其他小型车的真正优势在于马力。我知道你们仍然在向老年人销售74马力自然吸气三缸Láska，而向通勤族销售94马力1.0升涡轮增压TUP发动机版本——我个人最喜欢开94马力的版本。但是……”你们那款搭载108马力机械增压涡轮增压发动机和七速双离合DSG自动变速箱的车型，确实吸引了年轻一代的目光。如果我们能说服你们加装后扰流板、前部进气口，以及更大凸轮轴——比如说，把马力提升到115匹——那么我们在小型车市场就很有可能再添2.5亿欧元的年销售额。”

Man, what a Flash Roll! The guy was a champion. After this speech, the crowd was silent, no jeers or heckles. That’s usually a sign that the buyers have accepted your authority and expertise in the subject. You have instilled certainty in the listener. From here on out, they won’t interrupt or waste your time. With this kind of rapt attention from the buyer, it’s time to deliver the Pre-Wired Ideas: Winter Is Coming, 2X, and Skin in the Game. I was on the edge of my seat, waiting to see how Lukas was going to pull it off. It was hard to follow perfectly because, again, Trevor the accountant had to translate everything for me, but this is pretty accurate for what Lukas said next about how Winter Is Coming.

哇，这开场白真是精彩绝伦！这家伙简直就是个冠军。演讲结束后，全场鸦雀无声，没有丝毫嘘声或嘲讽。这通常表明买家已经认可了你在该领域的权威性和专业知识。你成功地让听众信服。从现在开始，他们不会再打断你，也不会浪费你的时间。有了买家如此专注的聆听，是时候抛出预设理念了：凛冬将至、双倍收益和切身利益。我紧张得坐立不安，迫不及待地想看看卢卡斯会如何演绎。由于会计师特雷弗又一次帮我翻译，我很难完全听懂，但以下对卢卡斯接下来关于“凛冬将至”的论述基本准确。

“For 120 years your competitors have tried to discredit you, to outsell you, to take your customers, and they have succeeded from time to time, but they never succeeded in building a tougher car than you. So 750 of those competitors are now in the junkyard of history and you’re still here, making the Láska, Vik, Zipp, and Basecamp. Today, after making twenty-five million cars . . . Volka is one of the most important manufacturers in the world! But you cannot relax, because now, some real competitors are coming for you fast and they’re out for blood.

“120年来，你的竞争对手一直试图诋毁你、超越你、抢走你的客户，他们也时常得逞，但他们从未造出比你更坚固耐用的汽车。如今，其中750家竞争对手已销声匿迹，而你依然屹立不倒，继续生产着Láska、Vik、Zipp和Basecamp等车型。今天，在生产了2500万辆汽车之后……大众汽车已成为世界上最重要的汽车制造商之一！但你不能掉以轻心，因为现在，一些真正的竞争对手正迅速逼近，他们势在必得。”

“On one end, the Koreans are coming. They sold 1.3 million cars last year and they want all your customers. Not some— all of them . Volka has never faced a smart, rich, and aggressive global competitor like this. But it gets worse, because coming from the other direction is BMW. They’re trying to build a submini that will eat the entire segment. If we get caught between Kia and BMW, it will not be good. We will be in retreat and they will take over the market. But there’s still enough time to maneuver against them by creating a clear message for UK buyers about our vehicles. We have to get that message out fast, and do it correctly, or we’ll start to lose market share.”

“一方面，韩国车企正在逼近。他们去年卖出了130万辆汽车，他们想要抢走你们所有的客户。不是一部分，而是全部。大众汽车从未遇到过如此精明、财力雄厚且咄咄逼人的全球竞争对手。但更糟糕的是，宝马也正从另一个方向逼近。他们正试图打造一款能够吞并整个小型车市场的车型。如果我们被夹在起亚和宝马之间，情况就不妙了。我们将节节败退，而他们将会占领市场。但我们仍然有足够的时间来应对他们，方法是向英国消费者清晰地传达我们车辆的信息。我们必须迅速有效地传递这一信息，否则我们将开始失去市场份额。”

Now it was time for Lucas to get into the 2X formula.

现在轮到卢卡斯运用 2X 公式了。

“If we act now, I know we can double sales in the next five years, and we’ll kick Kia all the way back to Korea. And BMW will walk away wishing they’d never heard the words submini or Volka .

“如果我们现在采取行动，我知道我们可以在未来五年内实现销量翻番，并将起亚彻底赶回韩国。而宝马将会后悔当初听到‘小型车’或‘沃尔卡’这两个词。”

“What kind of advertising message will do this? What can we tell consumers to avoid the frontal attack by Kia and the rear assault by BMW? What marketing will double sales in just a few years? Today, we have a very good ad campaign ready to launch, but it will take a little time to test, refine, and make it perfect. Give us that time.

“什么样的广告信息才能达到这个效果？我们该如何引导消费者避开起亚的正面进攻和宝马的尾随？什么样的营销策略才能在短短几年内实现销量翻番？今天，我们已经准备好了一套非常优秀的广告方案，但还需要一些时间进行测试、完善和优化。请给我们一些时间。”

“Why us? In the next six months, we will dedicate all of our key staff to making this campaign work. In other words, we will be all in . No other agency can offer that level of commitment. We will fight Kia. We will send BMW back to Bavaria. Together we will double your sales. This is how we fight—together—because I would rather die on my feet fighting with you against Kia than live on my knees, watching them take the UK market. And I know you feel the same way. ”

“为什么选择我们？在接下来的六个月里，我们将投入所有核心人员全力以赴，确保这次营销活动取得成功。换句话说，我们将全力以赴。没有其他任何一家代理公司能够提供如此高的投入。我们将与起亚展开激烈的竞争。我们将把宝马赶回巴伐利亚。我们将携手合作，使您的销量翻番。这就是我们的战斗方式——并肩作战——因为我宁愿与您并肩作战，与起亚殊死搏斗，也不愿苟且偷生，眼睁睁地看着他们占领英国市场。我知道您也和我一样。”

Shouts went up from the workers as Lukas finished. A few fists were thrust into the air. This resonated with them, of course, because Lukas was describing their brand in a way that they would have described it to their friends or even a person who knows nothing about cars. He was touching on the values that already resonated with them. It was all very Plain Vanilla. But if we wanted to cement our status as the clear choice, we couldn’t be entirely Plain Vanilla. We’d have to show these workers that we were also offering to take them into the new normal, that we were different from everyone else in one key way.

卢卡斯说完后，工人们爆发出欢呼声，有人甚至高举拳头。这当然引起了他们的共鸣，因为卢卡斯描述他们品牌的方式，就像他们会向朋友，甚至是对汽车一窍不通的人描述品牌一样。他触及了他们早已认同的价值观。一切都显得平淡无奇。但如果我们想巩固自己作为首选的地位，就不能完全平淡无奇。我们必须让这些工人看到，我们也在努力帮助他们适应新的常态，我们在关键的一点上与众不同。

“In the past, consumers chose a car by its reputation. Volvos were safe. A Toyota lasts forever. BMWs are fun to drive. Mercedeses are classy. Jeeps go anywhere. Hondas sip gas. But today, things are different. Consumers have discovered that all cars are good, efficient, fun to drive, and super safe. There isn’t a bad car out there. Believe it or not, a Pontiac is as safe as a Volvo. And the cost from one model to the next is similar. The supposed differences between brands have mostly become myths. Quality is the new normal. It’s the same with Volka: Your cars are high quality, have advanced technology, and are extremely safe and low-cost to operate. But so are others. So in the consumer’s mind, you are just another car, very similar to Toyota, Nissan, VW, and Hyundai. Except . . . for one big difference. A Volka is tough. This is a real difference that Western Europeans can understand and appreciate. More than any other car, we are practical, honest, and tough. So if you want a high-quality car with all the features and performance of any other car, but you want something functional and tough , then you want a Volka.”

过去，消费者选择汽车主要看品牌口碑。沃尔沃安全可靠，丰田经久耐用，宝马驾驶乐趣十足，奔驰尽显优雅，吉普车无所不能，本田省油。但如今，情况已大不相同。消费者发现，所有汽车都各有千秋，高效节能，驾驶乐趣十足，而且超级安全。市面上根本没有劣质车。信不信由你，庞蒂亚克和沃尔沃一样安全。而且不同车型之间的价格也相差无几。所谓品牌间的差异大多已成为迷思。品质才是新的标准。沃尔沃也是如此：你们的汽车品质卓越，技术先进，极其安全且运行成本低廉。但其他品牌的汽车也同样如此。因此，在消费者眼中，你们只是众多汽车品牌之一，与丰田、日产、大众和现代等品牌非常相似。然而……有一个很大的不同。沃尔沃坚固耐用。这是西欧人能够理解和欣赏的真正区别。与其他任何汽车品牌相比，我们更加务实、诚实，而且坚固耐用。所以，如果你想要一辆拥有其他任何汽车都具备的所有功能和性能的高品质汽车，但你又想要一辆实用且坚固耐用的汽车，那么你就应该选择沃尔卡。”

I continued to be impressed. Lukas had obviously been practicing for this moment during the off hours, and a star was born. He had expertly framed our offer as Plain Vanilla with just one unique element. He showed them that we could become the new normal for a big part of the UK market. But he wasn’t done yet. It was almost time to invite pessimism and ask the buyers to question him and the deal. But first, Lukas was going to reveal his Buyer’s Formula. He was going to teach these factory workers a quick lesson on choosing an ad agency.

我仍然印象深刻。卢卡斯显然在业余时间一直在为这一刻做准备，一颗新星冉冉升起。他巧妙地将我们的方案包装成平平无奇，却又独具特色。他向他们展示了我们能够成为英国市场很大一部分的新标杆。但他还没完。他几乎就要开始挑起买家的疑虑，让他们质疑他和这笔交易了。但首先，卢卡斯要揭晓他的“买家秘诀”。他要给这些工厂工人上一堂关于如何选择广告公司的速成课。

“I know . . . up here we’re a bunch of guys in suits; we have ten minutes to talk to you, give you a few lines, make a few promises, then we all fly back to New York, London, Frankfurt, Tel Aviv . . . wherever. And you never see us again, but you still have to rely on us to help you sell cars. How are you supposed to make such a big decision in such a short amount of time? I cannot tell you who to choose, but since I do this kind of thing a lot, maybe I can show you how to choose.

我知道……我们这儿都是些穿着西装的家伙；我们只有十分钟时间和你聊聊，说几句，做几个承诺，然后我们就都飞回纽约、伦敦、法兰克福、特拉维夫……随便什么地方。你再也见不到我们了，但你还得指望我们帮你卖车。你怎么能在这么短的时间内做出这么重要的决定？我不能告诉你该选谁，但我经常做这种事，或许我可以教你该怎么选。

“First, pick someone who has studied your 125-year history and has driven your cars. And not just the mighty flagship Basecamp but the lowly ten-thousand-euro Minimoto too. And ‘driving’ doesn’t mean a one-hour test-drive; it means driving thousands of miles over many years. For example, I once drove my Kovat 480 to Spain and back . . . in three days!

“首先，要找一个研究过你们125年历史，并且开过你们车的人。而且不仅仅是强大的旗舰车型Basecamp，就连售价一万欧元的入门级Minimoto也得开。“开”可不是指一小时的试驾；而是指多年来行驶数千英里。举个例子，我曾经开着我的Kovat 480往返西班牙……只用了三天！”

“Second, forget how big an ad agency is, because in our world, a big agency looks like it would be the best, but big is slow—and slow is dead—meaning size hurts you instead of helping you. Third, don’t pick someone you feel good about, and think you might ‘like as a person’ and get along with (and this might not make sense now), but pick someone you can argue with, fight with, disagree with . . . and still, even though mad and frustrated—they will show up the next day, to work. They don’t show up for ‘sensitivity counseling’ or to talk through their feelings or to complain about you to the bosses. They just show up to do the work.

第二，别太在意广告公司的规模，因为在我们的世界里，大公司看起来似乎是最好的，但规模大意味着效率低下——而效率低下就意味着失败——也就是说，规模越大反而会阻碍你，而不是帮助你。第三，不要选择你感觉良好、觉得“人品好”、能相处融洽的人（这一点现在可能听起来有点奇怪），而是要选择那些你可以和他们争论、争吵、意见不合的人……即便如此，即使他们生气、沮丧，第二天他们仍然会来上班。他们不会来接受“情感辅导”，不会来倾诉自己的感受，也不会来向老板抱怨你。他们只是来工作而已。

“The table stakes are high, because we’re talking about the very future of Volka, so you don’t want to hire prima donnas and sensitive types. If it were me, I’d pick the kind of people you can have a few drinks with, and make sure they drink Branik dark, not Corona Light.”

“这次招聘意义重大，因为这关系到Volka的未来，所以我们不能聘用那些自命不凡或过于敏感的人。如果是我，我会选择那种可以一起喝几杯的人，而且我会确保他们喝的是Branik黑啤，而不是Corona淡啤。”

Many heads nodded knowingly about Branik dark, possibly the best beer in the Czech Republic.

许多人心领神会地点头称赞 Branik 黑啤，它可能是捷克共和国最好的啤酒。

“Finally, I think you pick someone who knows cars, not car advertising. Because look at these ads—they are all the same.” He held up a stack of small posters and flipped through them. “Is this an ad for Toyota or Nissan? Ford or Kia? Who knows? The right agency won’t make these cliché ads, because they love cars, not advertising. Now look at this Porsche ad. You can tell they love cars. And this ad for Ford trucks. These were done by agencies like us—small agencies, people who love cars and make easy-to-understand car ads. And may God strike me down, but we will never put singing hamsters in a Volka TV commercial.”

“最后，我觉得你应该找个懂车的人，而不是懂汽车广告的人。因为你看这些广告——全都一个样。”他举起一叠小海报，翻阅起来。“这是丰田还是日产的广告？福特还是起亚？谁知道呢？真正优秀的广告公司不会做这种老套的广告，因为他们爱的是车，而不是广告。你看这个保时捷的广告。一看就知道他们爱车。还有这个福特卡车的广告。这些都是像我们这样的小公司做的——我们热爱汽车，而且会做简单易懂的汽车广告。老天保佑，我们绝对不会在沃尔卡的电视广告里放唱歌的仓鼠。”

With that final dig at Kia, it was done. He stopped talking, put the microphone down, and hopped off the platform. The small crowd erupted into applause that seemed to go on and on. It took a few precious and expensive minutes to get everyone settled down enough to listen to the Kevin guy from Bradford-McCoy. And they hated him right from the start. Although he spoke some decent Czech, it sounded like he had learned it from a Rosetta Stone app on an iPad on the flight over. He came across as elitist and privileged. These factory workers weren’t buying what he was selling. He had failed to achieve Status Alignment. After just a few minutes he was talking to some very bored workers. Giving the wrong speech to the wrong audience, he finally accepted defeat, slumped down off the platform, and trailed off without any real call to action. When he finished, the manufacturing line restarted and the workers were gone.

随着对起亚汽车的最后一次挖苦，一切都结束了。他停止了讲话，放下麦克风，跳下讲台。现场一小群人爆发出经久不息的掌声。费了好大劲才让大家安静下来，听布拉德福德-麦考伊公司的凯文讲话，这可是耗费了不少时间和金钱。而且，他们从一开始就讨厌他。虽然他的捷克语说得还不错，但听起来像是在飞机上用iPad上的罗塞塔石碑应用学的。他给人的感觉是精英主义和特权阶级。这些工厂工人根本不买账。他没能成功拉拢他们。仅仅几分钟后，他就发现自己面对的是一群百无聊赖的工人。对着错误的听众发表了错误的演讲，他最终承认失败，颓然地走下讲台，没有提出任何实质性的行动号召，就此结束了讲话。他讲完后，生产线重新启动，工人们也早已离开。

The rest is history. A few hours later Simon and team were all on a flight back to London with a signed Volka Motors UK contract for 10 million euros in hand. And Lukas had earned a place in advertising history.

剩下的故事大家都知道了。几个小时后，西蒙和他的团队带着与沃尔沃汽车英国公司签订的价值1000万欧元的合同，乘飞机返回伦敦。卢卡斯也因此在广告史上留下了浓墨重彩的一笔。

Personally, I just couldn’t wait to get back home to California to cook a large meal in my new kitchen and take my son to hockey practice. Just be a dad for a little while and slow things down. Yeah, that was going to be nice.

我个人而言，迫不及待地想回加州老家，在新厨房里做顿丰盛的晚餐，然后送儿子去冰球训练。就想好好当一会儿爸爸，放慢生活节奏。是啊，那该多好啊。

Simon had pulled the Volka card on me, same as I had on him, claiming the rules “forced” him to book me an economy ticket on the return flight to the States, so I leaned back and snuggled into the world’s most uncomfortable seat, then glanced down at my phone as a new text message came in. It was from an unknown number but the sender clearly knew who I was.

西蒙也对我使出了“沃尔卡牌”，就像我之前对他做的那样，声称规定“迫使”他给我订了回程美国的经济舱机票。于是我向后靠去，蜷缩在世界上最不舒服的座位上，这时手机收到了一条新短信。号码是陌生的，但发件人显然知道我是谁。

“Oren. Confidential deal. $40 million. I’m in Boston tomorrow. See attached file. You in or out?” That was all it said.

“奥伦。秘密交易。4000万美元。我明天在波士顿。请看附件。你加入还是退出？”邮件里就只有这些内容。

I had to admit, I was intrigued. Was it Anton? John King? Logan? Billy?

我不得不承认，我很好奇。是安东吗？约翰·金？洛根？比利？

“Who’s this?” I texted back.

“你是谁？”我回复短信问道。

“Mike Bixby,” came the immediate reply.

“迈克·比克斯比，”对方立即回答道。

OK, that got my attention. He was the CEO of Hyperloop, the revolutionary transportation company that was worth almost a billion dollars.

好吧，这引起了我的注意。他是Hyperloop的首席执行官，这家革命性的交通运输公司市值近10亿美元。

“I’m IN. See you there,” I typed. Then I paused, my finger over the Send key.

“我同意了。到时见。”我打字道。然后我停顿了一下，手指放在发送键上。

I took a breath. I thought about my little boy back home, and my beautiful wife who missed the heck out of me (if her recent texts were to be believed). Too many deals lately. It was starting to take a toll. I tried to remember the last time I’d been home for two weeks straight. It had just been deals, deals, deals. Maybe one too many.

我深吸了一口气。我想起了家里的小儿子，还有我美丽的妻子，她肯定非常想念我（如果她最近的短信属实的话）。最近生意太多了，开始让我疲惫不堪。我努力回想上次连续两周待在家里是什么时候。那段时间也是生意接踵而至，也许是太多了。

I deleted my first message and wrote, “Sorry Mike. Love to, but I’ll have to catch you on the next one. I’m Out.” Then I put the phone into airplane mode. This time, I was going to keep it there.

我删掉了第一条信息，然后写道：“抱歉啊迈克。我很想跟你聊，但下次再聊吧。我先走了。”说完，我把手机调成了飞行模式。这次，我打算一直保持飞行状态。

#↩

CONCLUSION

结论

IT’S YOUR TURN

轮到你了

You’ve seen how I used these principles in high-stakes situations to land important deals without pressuring or coercing the buyers. With a little practice, you’ll soon be doing the same.

你已经看到我是如何在关键时刻运用这些原则，在不给买家施加压力或胁迫的情况下达成重要交易的。只要稍加练习，你很快也能做到。

Since developing this set of techniques, I’ve taught it to thousands of people—and regardless of their skill level or experience, I’ve watched them apply this approach, flip the script, and achieve inception in their deals. They’ve been astounded by the results, and so have I.

自从我开发出这套技巧以来，我已经教给了成千上万的人——无论他们的技能水平或经验如何，我都亲眼见证了他们运用这种方法，扭转乾坤，并在交易中取得成功。他们对结果感到震惊，我也一样。

So here’s a quick recap of the process; think of it as a quick-start guide:

以下是对整个流程的简要回顾；您可以将其视为快速入门指南：

You’ll start by getting your audience—whether they’re a buyer, an investor, or a business partner—to pay full attention to you and take you seriously, as they would a partner or colleague. And you’ll do this by achieving Status Alignment, the first step to making a deal.

首先，你要让你的受众——无论他们是买家、投资者还是商业伙伴——全神贯注地关注你，并像对待合作伙伴或同事一样认真对待你。而要做到这一点，你需要达成地位一致，这是达成交易的第一步。

No buyer of any kind is going to listen to you until they feel they’re in the right place at the right time with the right person. That’s why the Status Tip-Off is so powerful. When your buyer sees that you understand who they are, can speak their language, and are part of their in-group, they’ll immediately become receptive to what you have to say. Whether you’re talking to an assembly line worker or the CEO of the company, you need to establish that you fit right into their world.

任何类型的买家，只有在感觉时机、地点和对象都合适的时候，才会认真听取你的意见。这就是“身份暗示”如此强大的原因。当买家意识到你了解他们，能用他们的语言与他们沟通，并且是他们圈子里的一员时，他们就会立刻愿意倾听你的想法。无论你是在和流水线工人还是公司CEO交谈，你都需要让他们感受到你与他们的世界息息相关。

Either way, a Status Tip-Off works the same—it’s a brief story or phrase that would be known only by an in-group member and will instantly cement your status as “one of us.”

无论哪种方式，“身份提示”的作用都一样——它是一个只有内部成员才知道的简短故事或短语，可以立即巩固你作为“我们中的一员”的地位。

But achieving Status Alignment is not enough to make a deal happen. You probably have friends whom you trust and respect. However, how many of them would you hire to manage and invest your money?

但仅仅达成地位一致并不足以促成交易。你可能有一些值得信赖和尊重的朋友。然而，你会聘请其中多少人来管理和投资你的资金呢？

When the stakes are high, you need to instill absolute Certainty in the buyer’s mind that you’re a true expert in your field and that things will happen exactly as you say they will. To do this, you’re going to use a Flash Roll.

当风险很高时，你需要让买家绝对确信你是该领域的真正专家，并且事情会完全按照你承诺的那样进行。为此，你需要使用“闪电卷轴”。

While the Status Tip-Off aligns you with your audience by showing them you have a lot in common, the Flash Roll should distance you from your audience, demonstrating your technical expertise in one very specific field—which happens to be the area in which they are having a difficult problem.

虽然“状态提示”通过向观众展示你们有很多共同点来拉近彼此的距离，但“闪电演讲”应该让你与观众保持距离，展示你在某个非常具体的领域的技术专长——而这恰好是他们遇到难题的领域。

Once you’ve established your Status and expertise, it’s time to explain your big idea to the buyer. Specifically, to answer the three questions in the buyer’s mind: Why do I care? What’s in it for me? and Why you? The faster you answer these, and the less cognitive strain you place on the buyer, the better your chances are of closing the deal. The easiest way to do this is using a sequence of Pre-Wired Ideas:

一旦你确立了自己的地位和专业能力，就该向买家阐述你的核心理念了。具体来说，就是要回答买家心中的三个问题：我为什么要关心这个？这对我有什么好处？为什么是你？你回答这些问题的速度越快，买家的认知负担越轻，成交的几率就越大。最简单的方法是使用一系列预先构思好的理念：

  • Winter Is Coming
    凛冬将至
  • 2X
    2倍
  • Skin in the Game
    切身利益

These ideas are designed to fit into the deepest pre-wired idea receptors in the human brain while supplying your audience with the answers they need to move forward with you. With Pre-Wired Ideas, your audience will understand everything they need to know about you and what you’re offering.

这些理念旨在契合人脑深处预设的认知区域，同时为您的受众提供他们所需的答案，以便与您携手前行。借助预设理念，您的受众将全面了解您以及您所提供的产品或服务。

But you don’t just want your buyer to understand your idea, you want them to buy in and pitch it back to you—to invite you into your own deal. You want to flip the script. And this isn’t going to happen until the buyer feels safe to explore your idea more deeply and entertain both the positives and the potential negatives.

但你不仅希望买家理解你的想法，还希望他们接受并向你推销——邀请你参与到你的交易中来。你想扭转局面。而这一切只有在买家感到安全，愿意更深入地了解你的想法，并认真考虑其积极和潜在的消极因素时才会发生。

To make the buyer feel interested enough to explore a new idea but safe enough to move forward, you need to find their novelty sweet spot. Show them how your offer is the New Normal—a Plain Vanilla concept with just one key and valuable difference. To keep things moving along, you should lump together all of the ways your product or idea is new and unique so the buyer isn’t overwhelmed or scared to buy it. Then show how your offer is new and different from the status quo in just one key way. If you’re in a room full of Czech business executives as I was, you can tell them you’re exactly the same as the top ten creative agencies in the world, but much smaller (and therefore more effective).

为了让买家对新想法产生足够的兴趣去探索，同时又让他们感到足够安心而继续推进，你需要找到他们眼中的“新奇点”。向他们展示你的产品或服务如何成为“新常态”——一个看似平淡无奇的概念，却拥有一个关键且极具价值的差异。为了保持沟通顺畅，你应该将产品或理念的所有新颖之处集中起来，避免买家感到不知所措或害怕购买。然后，着重展示你的产品或服务在某个关键方面与现状有何不同。如果你像我一样，身处一群捷克企业高管之中，你可以告诉他们，你和全球排名前十的创意机构完全一样，只是规模小得多（因此效率更高）。

By this point, the buyer is becoming attracted to your idea and the idea of working with you, and you won’t feel the need to control, pressure, or corner them. Instead, you’ll be in free exchange of ideas and plans to move forward.

到了这个阶段，买家开始被你的想法以及与你合作的意愿所吸引，你不会再觉得需要控制、施压或逼迫他们。相反，你们会自由地交流想法和计划，共同推进项目。

However, before you actually turn the power to make the decision over to your buyer, there’s one final step: You need to contain their pessimism within a set of pre-defined boundaries. I call this an invisible fence. To do this, use a Buyer’s Formula to teach them how to buy whatever you’re selling.

然而，在真正将决策权交给买家之前，还有最后一步：你需要将他们的悲观情绪控制在预设的范围内。我称之为“无形围栏”。为此，你可以运用“买家公式”来引导他们如何购买你销售的产品。

When you list the obvious ways to fail before you relinquish control to the buyer, you block off certain options in their mind, like when you tell a late-career athlete about the common mistakes made by other big name late-career athletes or when you tell a car company about the obvious mistakes in hiring a car advertising firm that can cost millions. That’s why it’s so important to build Alignment and Certainty, so you are credible, believable, and in position as the world’s best expert in the buyer’s specific problem.

在将控制权移交给买家之前，如果你列举出所有显而易见的失败方式，就会在他们心中排除某些选项，就像你告诉一位职业生涯末期的运动员其他知名运动员常犯的错误，或者告诉一家汽车公司聘请汽车广告公司可能耗资数百万美元一样。这就是为什么建立共识和确定性如此重要，这样你才能获得信任，让人信服，并成为买家特定问题领域的全球最佳专家。

One note of caution: Through the above five steps, you can’t change who you are or change your values to make the buyer happy. One reason why so many people are mistrustful of salespeople is because they see the seller move through different characters during a sales pitch, and this leaves buyers feeling confused and uncertain. Flipping the script isn’t about changing yourself to give the buyer what they want; it’s about sticking to your guns. Stay consistent to your personality, your character, and most importantly, your values. This is what the most compelling people in the world have that others don’t: character and values.

需要特别注意的是：通过以上五个步骤，你无法改变自己或改变自己的价值观来取悦买家。很多人不信任销售人员的原因之一，就是他们看到销售人员在推销过程中不断变换角色，这让买家感到困惑和不安。所谓“扭转局面”，并非是要你改变自己去迎合买家的需求，而是要你坚持自己的原则。保持你的个性、品格，以及最重要的——你的价值观的一致性。这正是世界上最具魅力的人所拥有的特质：品格和价值观。

In the final delivery of your ideas, if you’re considered an insider and an expert, if the buyer knows why they should care about your idea, what’s in it for them, and why you; if you acknowledge their concerns or objections, and guide them through the process of buying your product; and in all this they find you to be a compelling person, they will search for, find, and suggest a way to do business with you.

在最终交付你的想法时，如果你被认为是业内人士和专家，如果买家知道他们为什么应该关心你的想法，这对他们有什么好处，以及为什么选择你；如果你承认他们的担忧或反对意见，并引导他们完成购买你产品的过程；并且在所有这些过程中，他们发现你是一个有说服力的人，他们就会寻找、发现并提出与你合作的方式。

It can be nerve-racking to attempt Inception, especially when you give autonomy to the buyer to make his own decision. This pressure intensifies when you’re dealing with someone with a lot more power than you, or if you’re stuck on a team that’s used to doing things the old way. In these scenarios, it can feel tempting to fall back on the old sales methods you’re used to. You have to resist this temptation. While it feels safe to resort to your old argumentative sales methods (because everyone feels like they have “a shot at closing” when trying to overcome the buyer’s objections), doing so will undermine any progress you’ve made towards encouraging your buyer to work with you.

尝试“诱导式销售”可能会让人紧张不已，尤其是在你给予买家充分自主权，让他们自行做决定的时候。如果你面对的是一个比你权力大得多的人，或者你身处一个习惯于老一套做事方式的团队，这种压力会更加强烈。在这些情况下，你很容易会不由自主地回到过去那种销售模式。你必须抵制这种诱惑。虽然使用传统的辩论式销售方法似乎很安全（因为每个人都觉得在试图克服买家的异议时“有机会成交”），但这样做会破坏你之前为说服买家与你合作所做的一切努力。

If you stick to the steps and practice your delivery, you’ll be flipping the script, incepting ideas into the buyer’s mind, and stacking up many financial wins and social rewards.

如果你坚持这些步骤并练习你的表达方式，你就能扭转局面，将想法灌输到买家的脑海中，并积累许多经济上的成功和社会上的回报。

Soon, the people you want to work with will find their way to you, start pitching you on the idea of getting together, and doing a deal.

很快，你想与之合作的人就会找到你，开始向你推销合作的想法，并提出达成交易。

If you want to join me in one more adventure, I invite you to read the lost chapter , an important story and set of methods that didn’t make the publishing deadline of this book but definitely should be read.

如果你想和我一起踏上另一段冒险之旅，我邀请你阅读这本遗失的章节，它讲述了一个重要的故事，并介绍了一系列方法，虽然未能赶上本书的出版期限，但绝对值得一读。

You can read it at orenklaff.com/flip [inactive].

您可以在 orenklaff.com/flip [已失效] 阅读。

ABOUT THE AUTHOR

关于作者

Oren Klaff is one of the world's leading experts on sales, raising capital and negotiation. His first book, Pitch Anything , is required reading throughout Silicon Valley, Wall Street and the Fortune 500, with more than 1,000,000 copies in print worldwide. He has written for Harvard Business Review , Inc. , Advertising Age , Entrepreneur and has been featured in hundreds of periodicals, podcasts and blogs. He is an investment partner in a $200 million private equity investment fund and in his spare time is a motorcycle enthusiast.

奥伦·克拉夫是世界顶尖的销售、融资和谈判专家之一。他的第一本书《推销任何产品》（Pitch Anything）是硅谷、华尔街和财富500强企业的必读书目，全球销量超过100万册。他曾为《哈佛商业评论》、《Inc.》、《广告时代》、《创业者》等杂志撰稿，并在数百家期刊、播客和博客上发表过文章。他是一家规模达2亿美元的私募股权投资基金的投资合伙人，业余时间是一位摩托车爱好者。
